Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
The Qawida of Problematic Time (Waqt Mushkil) and Its Application to Hajj
Defines and applies the qawida of waqt mushkil to Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a waqt mushkil, apply the qawida to determine the ruling based on intention, and evaluate the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the timing of obligatory Hajj.

Core Idea
A problematic time is both measure and vessel: absolute intention fulfills the fard; specific intention determines the type.

In this passage, the author of al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair introduces the concept of 'problematic time' (waqt mushkil) – a time that has characteristics of both a measure (mi'yar) and a vessel (zarf). The prime example is the time of Hajj, which occupies only a few days but spans several months. How does intention interact with such a time? The answer reveals a nuanced Hanafi qawida and a subtle difference of opinion between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Define the three categories of time
Identify the three types: pure measure (mi'yar) – only one specific act fits (e.g., a Ramadan fast day); pure vessel (zarf) – multiple acts can be done (e.g., prayer times); and problematic (mushkil) – both aspects exist.
The passage focuses on mushkil.
2
Identify the dual aspects of Hajj time
Hajj time (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah) is a measure because only one Hajj can be performed in a year. It is a vessel because the rituals do not fill the entire period.
The text gives two examples: one from the time itself, another from the obligation once in a lifetime.
3
Apply the qawida: intention determines the ruling
With absolute intention (mutlaq niyyah), the measure aspect dominates and the Hajj counts as the obligatory (fard) Hajj. With specific intention (e.g., nafl), the vessel aspect dominates and it becomes that type.
If nafl is intended while fard is still owed, the nafl is valid but sinful due to delay.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf (emphasizing mi'yar) held that Hajj must be performed in the year it becomes obligatory. Muhammad (emphasizing zarf) held it can be delayed. Both are valid in the school.
The passage does not give a definitive tarjih.
5
Note the istithna: prayer times are not mushkil
Even though prayer times have surplus capacity, ta'ayyun (specification) is required. Prayer time is pure zarf, not mushkil, so the qawida does not apply.
The text states ta'ayyun is not dropped due to narrowness of time because capacity remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ وَقْتُهَا مُشْكِلاً كَوَقْتِ الْحَجِّ يَشْبَهُ الْمِعْيَارَ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ لَا يَصْحُ فِي السَّنَةِ إِلَّا حَجَّةً وَاحِدَةً، وَالطَّرْفَ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ أَفْعَالَهُ لَا تَسْتَغْرِقْ وَقَتَهُ فَيُصَابُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ نَظراً إلَى الْمِعْبَارِيَّةِ وإن نوى نَفْلًا وَقَعَ عَمَا نَوَى نَظُراً إلى الطَّرْفِيَّةِ. وَلَا يَسْقُطُ التَّخَيْنُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ لِصِيْنِ الْوَقْتِ لأنَّ السَعَةَ بَاقِيَة أَنَّهُ لَوْ شَرَعَ مُتَنََفِلا صَحٌ، وَ إِنْ كَانَ حَرَاماً .

ترجمہ: اور اگر اس کا وقت مشکل ہو جیسے حج کا وقت تو وہ معیار کے مشابہ ہے، اس اعتبار سے کہ سال میں صرف ایک مرتبہ حج ہوتا ہے اور ظرف کے مشابہ ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ اس کے افعال اس کے وقت کو نہیں گھیر تے تو وہ معیار کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے مطلق نیت سے صحیح ہو جائے گا اور اگر نفل کی نیت کی تو ظرفیت کی طرف نظر کرنے کو ہوئے اس کی نیت کے مطابق واقع ہوگا۔ اور وقت کی تنگی کی وجہ سے نماز میں تعیین ساقط نہیں ہوگی اس لئے کہ گنجائش باقی ہے بایں معنی کہ اگر نفل شروع کیا تو صحیح ہے اگر چہ حرام ہے۔ تشریح تیسری قسم کہ جس میں وقت عبادت کے لئے من وجہ معیار ہو اور من وجہ ظرف جس کو مشکل کہتے ہیں ) اور مشکل اس معنی کر ہے کہ حج کا وقت شوال، ذیقعدہ اور ذی الحجہ کے دس دن ہیں لیکن چند ایام میں ادا ہو جاتا ہےاور باقی وقت فاضل رہتا ہے اس اعتبار سے حج کا وقت حج کے لئے ظرف ہے اور چونکہ ان اشہر حج میں صرف ایک ہی جج ادا ہوتا ہے اس اعتبار سے حج کا وقت حج کے لئے معیار ہے۔ دوسری وجہ اس کے مشکل ہونے کی یہ ہے کہ حج زندگی میں صرف ایک مرتبہ فرض ہوتا ہے اگر حج کی فرضیت کے بعد دوسرا، تیسر اسال بھی مل گیا تو اس اعتبار سے وہ وقت حج کے لئے ظرف کے مشابہ ہے اور اگر حج فرضیت کے سال کے علاوہ دوسرا سال نہ مل پایا اور انتقال ہو گیا تو وہ وقت حج کے لئے معیار ہے تو چونکہ اس میں دونوں جہتیں ہیں اس لئے حج کے وقت کو حج کے لئے مشکل کہا جاتا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے حالت تفسیق کا اختیار کر کے کہا کہ حج فرض کے سال ہی حج کرنا ضروری ہے اور امام محمد نے جانب توسیع کا اعتبار کیا ہے جس سال حج فرض ہوا ہے اسی سال حج کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے اب مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر رنج کرتے وقت مطلق نبیت کی ہے تو معیار کو دیکھتے ہوئے حج فرض ادا ہو جائے گا اور اگر کسی نے اشہر حج میں نقل کی نیت کا تو ظرف کو دیکھتے ہوئے حج نفل ہو جائے گا اور اس کی نسبت درست ہوگی اگر چہ حرام ہوگا۔ علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں حج کے وقت میں حج نفل کو حرام کہنا شروع کرنے کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ حج فرض میں تاخیر کی وجہ سے حج نفل کو حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے لیکن چونکہ حج نفل کو شروع کرنے کی وجہ سے حج فرض میں تاخیر ہوئی ہے اس لئے حرمت کی نسبت شروع فی انفل کی طرف کر دی گئی۔

قوله بوقت مشکل اى مشتبه الحال يشبه المعيار من وجه والظرف من وجه ونظيره وقت الحج فانه مشكل بهذا المعنى وذلك من وجهين الاول ان وقت الحج شوال و ذو القعدة وعشرة ذى الحجة والحج لا يؤدى الا فى بعض عشرة ذى الحجة فيكون الوقت فاضلا فمن هذا الوجه يكون ظرفاً ومن حيث أنه لا يؤدى في هذا الوقت الا حج واحد يكون معياراً في هامش الحسامي ص (٢٧) ولا يقع التعيين : نماز کا وقت نماز کے لئے ظرف ہے اس لئے اس میں وقتیہ نماز کے علاوہ دوسری نمازیں بھی
And if its time is problematic (mushkil), like the time of Hajj, it resembles a measure (mi'yar) in that only one Hajj is valid in the year, and a vessel (zarf) in that its actions do not occupy its entire time; so with absolute intention (mutlaq niyyah), it is valid by looking at the measure aspect, and if he intended nafl, it occurs according to his intention by looking at the vessel aspect. And in prayer, specification (ta'ayyun) is not dropped due to the narrowness of time, because capacity remains, in that if he begins a nafl, it is valid even if it is haram.

Translation: And if its time is problematic, like the time of Hajj, then it is similar to a measure, in that only one Hajj occurs in the year, and similar to a vessel, in that its actions do not encompass its time; so with absolute intention, it will be valid by looking at the measure aspect, and if he intended nafl, it will occur according to his intention by looking at the vessel aspect. And in prayer, specification is not dropped due to narrowness of time, because capacity remains, meaning if he begins a nafl, it is valid even if it is haram. Explanation: The third category where the time is a measure in one respect and a vessel in another is called 'problematic'. The meaning of problematic is that the time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, but it is performed in a few days, so the remaining time is surplus; from this aspect, the time of Hajj is a vessel for Hajj, and since only one Hajj is performed in these months, from this aspect the time is a measure. Another reason for its being problematic is that Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime. If after the obligation of Hajj, a second and third year also come, then from that aspect the time is like a vessel; and if no other year comes after the year of obligation and he dies, then the time is a measure. So because both aspects exist, the time of Hajj is called problematic for Hajj. Imam Abu Yusuf, adopting the aspect of narrowing, said that Hajj must be performed in the year it becomes obligatory; and Imam Muhammad, adopting the aspect of expansion, said it is not necessary to perform it in that year. Now the issue: if at the time of performing, he made an absolute intention, then by looking at the measure, the obligatory Hajj will be fulfilled; and if someone in the months of Hajj intended nafl, then by looking at the vessel, it will become a nafl Hajj, and his attribution will be correct even if it is haram. Allamah Hamawi says: calling nafl Hajj haram is not due to starting it, but because of delay in the obligatory Hajj; but since the delay occurred due to starting nafl, the prohibition is ascribed to starting nafl.

His statement: 'at a problematic time' meaning ambiguous in condition, resembling a measure in one aspect and a vessel in another. Its example is the time of Hajj, for it is problematic in this sense, and that in two aspects: first, the time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, and Hajj is only performed in part of those ten days, so the time is surplus; from this aspect it is a vessel. And in that only one Hajj is performed in this time, it is a measure. In the margin of al-Hisami, page 27: And specification does not occur: the time of prayer is a vessel for prayer, therefore besides the time-specific prayer, other prayers can also [be performed]...
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a definition and application of the qawida (maxim) regarding 'problematic time' (waqt mushkil). The author classifies times for acts of worship into three: times that are purely a 'measure' (mi'yar), times that are purely a 'vessel' (zarf), and times that are problematic (mushkil) – having characteristics of both. The example given is the time of Hajj. The time of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah) is a measure because only one Hajj is performed in a year; it is a vessel because the actual rituals of Hajj do not occupy the whole period – there is surplus time. Because of this dual nature, if one makes an absolute intention (e.g., simply intends 'Hajj') without specifying fard or nafl, the act is valid as the fard (obligatory) Hajj due to the measure aspect. If one explicitly intends nafl, it will be a nafl Hajj due to the vessel aspect – even though it might be sinful to delay the fard. The passage then discusses the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding whether Hajj must be performed in the year it becomes obligatory. Abu Yusuf considers the narrowing aspect and says it must be done that year; Muhammad considers the expansion and says it may be delayed. The consequence: if someone intending nafl, the act is valid as nafl but the person is sinful for delaying the fard. The maxim is that in problematic times, the type of act is determined by the specific intention, whereas in purely measure times (like Ramadan), absolute intention goes to the fard. The passage also contrasts with prayer, where time is purely a vessel and specification (ta'ayyun) is not dropped due to capacity.

Key Terms
وقت مشکل (waqt mushkil): Time that is ambiguous, having both characteristics of a measure (mi'yar) and a vessel (zarf)
معیار (mi'yar): Measure; a time that can only accommodate one specific obligatory act (e.g., one Ramadan fast per day)
ظرف (zarf): Vessel; a time that can accommodate multiple acts, both obligatory and voluntary
حج (hajj): Pilgrimage to Mecca; fard once in a lifetime; time is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person who still has to perform obligatory Hajj goes to Makkah in the month of Shawwal and intends 'absolute Hajj' without specifying fard or nafl, what is the result according to the Hanafi ruling on problematic time?
A) The Hajj is invalid because intention was not specific
B) It counts as nafl Hajj because of the vessel aspect
C) It counts as obligatory Hajj because of the measure aspect
D) It does not count at all because fard Hajj cannot be performed before its year

Key Takeaway
The time of Hajj is problematic (mushkil) because it is both a measure and a vessel; absolute intention fulfills the fard, while specific intention determines the type, but delaying the fard makes the nafl sinful.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
The Problematic Time (Waqt Mushkil) for Hajj and Its Effect on Intention
Defining and applying the qawida of problematic time for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida of 'waqt mushkil' to determine whether an absolute intention or a specific nafl intention fulfills the obligatory Hajj, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of performance.

Core Idea
A problematic time is both a measure and a vessel; absolute intention defaults to fard, but specifying nafl is valid though sinful.

This passage introduces a key qawida in Hanafi usul: the concept of 'waqt mushkil' (problematic time) as applied to the Hajj season. The time of Hajj is ambiguous because it simultaneously resembles a measure (only one Hajj fits in a season) and a vessel (the actual rituals occupy only part of the season). This duality has direct consequences for the validity of intention—absolute intention suffices for the fard, while explicit nafl intention creates a sin of delay. Understanding this qawida enables a mufti to correctly resolve cases where the worshipper's intention is unclear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dual nature of the time
Read the passage and note that the time of Hajj is called 'mushkil' because it resembles both a measure (mi'yār) and a vessel (zarf). Identify the two reasons given: the surplus time beyond performance, and the possibility of multiple years.
This ambiguity is key to the qawida.
2
Derive the qawida from the text
Formulate the maxim: 'When a time has dual characteristics (measure and vessel), the ruling on intention is affected: absolute intention fulfills the obligation, while specifying nafl is valid but sinful.'
The qawida is implicit in the passage.
3
Apply the qawida to the intention scenario
Consider two cases: (1) absolute intention (niyyah muṭlaqah) during the Hajj months → measure aspect dominates → fard Hajj fulfilled. (2) explicit nafl intention → vessel aspect considered → nafl valid but haram due to delay.
The prohibition is attributed to the delay, not the act itself.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that Hajj must be performed in the year of obligation (measure), while Imam Muhammad allows delay (vessel). Note that both opinions are valid and the passage does not give tarjih.
This dispute illustrates how the dual nature can be interpreted differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله بوقت مشکل اى مشتبه الحال يشبه المعيار من وجه والظرف من وجه ونظيره وقت الحج فانه مشكل بهذا المعنى وذلك من وجهين الاول ان وقت الحج شوال و ذو القعدة وعشرة ذى الحجة والحج لا يؤدى الا فى بعض عشرة ذى الحجة فيكون الوقت فاضلا فمن هذا الوجه يكون ظرفاً ومن حيث أنه لا يؤدى في هذا الوقت الا حج واحد يكون معياراً تشريح تيسري قسم كہ جس مين وقت عبادت كے لئے من وجه معيار ہو اور من وجہ ظرف جس كو مشكل كہتے ہيں) اور مشكل اس معني كر ہے كہ حج كا وقت شوال، ذي قعدہ اور ذي الحجہ كے دس دن ہيں ليكن چند ايام ميں ادا ہو جاتا ہےاور باقي وقت فاضل رہتا ہے اس اعتبار سے حج كا وقت حج كے لئے ظرف ہے اور چونكہ ان اشہر حج ميں صرف ايك ہی حج ادا ہوتا ہے اس اعتبار سے حج كا وقت حج كے لئے معيار ہے۔ دوسري وجہ اس كے مشكل ہونے كي يہ ہے كہ حج زندگي ميں صرف ايك مرتبہ فرض ہوتا ہے اگر حج كي فرضيت كے بعد دوسرا، تيسر سال بھي مل گيا تو اس اعتبار سے وہ وقت حج كے لئے ظرف كے مشابہ ہے اور اگر حج فرضيت كے سال كے علاوہ دوسرا سال نہ مل پايا اور انتقال ہو گيا تو وہ وقت حج كے لئے معيار ہے تو چونكہ اس ميں دونوں جہتيں ہيں اس لئے حج كے وقت كو حج كے لئے مشكل كہا جاتا ہے۔ امام ابو يوسف نے حالت تفسيق كا اختيار كر كے كہا كہ حج فرض كے سال ہی حج كرنا ضروري ہے اور امام محمد نے جانب توسيع كا اعتبار كيا ہے جس سال حج فرض ہوا ہے اسي سال حج كرنا ضروري نہيں ہے اب مسئلہ يہ ہے كہ اگر رنج كرتے وقت مطلق نيت كي ہے تو معيار كو ديكھتے ہوئے حج فرض ادا ہو جائے گا اور اگر كسي نے اشہر حج ميں نقل كي نيت كي ہے تو ظرف كو ديكھتے ہوئے حج نفل ہو جائے گا اور اس كي نسبت درست ہوگی اگر چہ حرام ہوگا۔ علامہ حموي فرماتے ہيں حج كے وقت ميں حج نفل كو حرام كہنا شروع كرنے كي وجہ سے نہيں ہے بلكہ حج فرض ميں تاخير كي وجہ سے حج نفل كو حرام قرار ديا گيا ہے ليكن چونكہ حج نفل كو شروع كرنے كي وجہ سے حج فرض ميں تاخير ہوئي ہے اس لئے حرمت كي نسبت شروع في النفل كي طرف كر دي گئي۔
His saying: 'In a problematic time' meaning ambiguous in condition, resembling the measure from one aspect and the vessel from another. Its analogue is the time of Hajj, for it is problematic in this sense, and that from two aspects: First, the time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, and Hajj is not performed except during some of the ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, so the time is surplus, so from this aspect it is a vessel; and from the aspect that only one Hajj is performed in this time, it is a measure. Commentary: Third subdivision, in which the time for worship is in one respect a measure and in another a vessel, called 'mushkil'. And 'mushkil' means that the time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, but it is performed in a few days, and the remaining time is surplus. From this aspect, the time of Hajj is a vessel for Hajj, and since only one Hajj is performed in these months of Hajj, from this aspect the time of Hajj is a measure. The second reason for its being problematic is that Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime. If after the obligation of Hajj a second or third year also becomes available, then from that aspect the time resembles a vessel, and if no other year than the year of obligation is available and death occurs, then the time is a measure. So since it has both aspects, the time of Hajj is called problematic. Imam Abu Yusuf, choosing the aspect of time restriction, said that it is necessary to perform Hajj in the same year it becomes obligatory. Imam Muhammad considered the aspect of extension: it is not necessary to perform Hajj in the same year. Now the issue: if at the time of ihram one makes an absolute intention, then considering the measure aspect, the obligatory Hajj will be fulfilled; but if someone in the months of Hajj intends a nafl, then considering the vessel aspect, it will become a nafl Hajj, and his intention will be correct, although it will be haram. Allama Hamawi says: The prohibition of nafl Hajj at the time of Hajj is not because of starting it, but because it causes delay of the obligatory Hajj, so the prohibition is attributed to starting the nafl.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'waqt mushkil' (problematic time) and applies it to the time of Hajj. The time is problematic because it has dual characteristics: from one perspective it acts as a 'measure' (mi'yār) because only one Hajj can be performed in that season, and from another it acts as a 'vessel' (zarf) because the actual rituals occupy only a portion of the time. Two reasons are given for the problematic nature. First, the Hajj season spans months, but the performance takes only a few days, so the remaining time is surplus (zarf aspect); however, only one Hajj occurs per season (mi'yār aspect). Second, Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime, so if subsequent years are available, the time is like a vessel; but if only one year is available, it is like a measure. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad differ on whether Hajj must be performed in the year of obligation. The passage derives the following ruling: if one makes an absolute intention (without specifying whether it is fard or nafl) during the Hajj season, the measure aspect dominates and the fard Hajj is fulfilled. If one explicitly intends nafl, the intention is valid but it is sinful (haram) because it delays the obligatory Hajj. Allama Hamawi clarifies that the prohibition is due to delay, not the act of starting nafl itself.

Key Terms
وقت مشکل (waqt mushkil): A time that ambiguously resembles both a measure (only one worship fits) and a vessel (surplus time remains).
معيار (mi'yār): A time that measures the worship, i.e., only one instance fits within it.
ظرف (zarf): A time that serves as a vessel for the worship, i.e., it can contain multiple acts or the worship occupies only part of it.
نية مطلقة (niyyah muṭlaqah): An absolute intention without specifying whether the worship is fard or nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs Hajj during the months of Hajj with an absolute intention (niyyah muṭlaqah), what is the result according to the Hanafi position derived from the measure aspect?
A) The Hajj is considered nafl.
B) The Hajj is considered fard.
C) The Hajj is invalid due to lack of specification.
D) The Hajj depends on the intention of the heart alone.

Key Takeaway
The problematic time (waqt mushkil) of Hajj combines measure and vessel, so absolute intention fulfills the fard, but explicit nafl intention is valid though sinful due to delay.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Ta'yin in Performance and Make-Up: When Words or Actions Specify Worship
Explaining the maxim that ta'yin by action suffices in ada but verbal ta'yin is required in qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in ada action suffices for ta'yin but in qada verbal ta'yin is required, and identify exceptions for multiple missed fasts of the same kind.

Core Idea
In on-time worship, action specifies; in make-up, words are necessary—because time itself is no longer the marker.

This lesson unpacks a key qāʿida from Al-Ashbāh wa al-Naẓāʾir: verbal specification alone does not determine a part of time; action does. But there is a sharp turn when we move from on-time prayer (adāʾ) to make-up (qaḍāʾ). Understanding this distinction is essential for anyone who gives fatwa regarding missed prayers and fasts, because common errors arise when this rule is generalized too broadly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim and Its Scope
Locate the Arabic maxim: 'وَلَا يَتَعَيَّنُ جُزْءٌ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ الْوَقْتِ بِتَعْيِينِ الْعَبْدِ قَوْلًا وَإِنَّمَا يَتَعَيَّنُ بِفِعْلِهِ'. Understand that it applies to acts of worship that must be performed in a specific time (e.g., prayers). The maxim denies that mere words can fix which part of the time is occupied; only action does.
The maxim is a dabt (restricting sub-maxim) under the broader qāʿida 'al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā'.
2
Understand the Analogical Basis (Oath Expiation)
Study the analogy to breaking an oath: if someone breaks an oath, the specific expiatory act (feeding, clothing, freeing) is not determined by mere words but by the actual performance. Similarly, in worship, verbal ta'yin is insufficient without corresponding action.
This analogy (qiyās) shows that the Hanafi rule is consistent across different chapters of fiqh.
3
Distinguish Between Adāʾ and Qaḍāʾ
The maxim operates only in adāʾ (on-time performance). In qaḍāʾ, the daīl changes: because the specific time for the missed worship has passed, there is no natural marker. Hence, verbal ta'yin becomes indispensable to identify which missed obligation is being fulfilled.
The text explicitly states: 'وَأَمَّا فِي الْقَضَاءِ: فَلَابُدَّ مِنَ التَّعْيِينِ'.
4
Apply to Fasting: Single vs. Multiple Ramadans
For qaḍāʾ of fasts: if the missed fasts are from one Ramadan, no additional specification beyond the intention of qaḍāʾ is needed because the cause (sabab) is the same month. But if from two different Ramadans, specification of the year is required because the causes differ.
This is the 'aṣaḥḥ (most authentic) view in the Hanafi school.
5
Practical Implication for the Mufti
The mufti can ease the burden on the layperson by allowing general intention when many prayers of the same type are missed. For example, one can intend 'the first Zuhr upon me' or 'the last Zuhr' without specifying the exact day. This is a legitimate application of the maxim.
See al-Tātārkhāniyya: 'إذا أراد تسهيل الأمر ينوي أول ظهر عليه'.

ترجمہ: اور بہر حال جب چھوٹی ہوئی عبادات زیادہ ہو جائیں تو جنس واحد کے متحدہ فروض میں تمیز کے لئے تعیین کی شرط لگانے میں فقہاء کا اختلاف ہے۔ اور اصبح یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی پر ایک رمضان کے روزے کی قضا ہو اور اس نے ایک دن کا روزہ رکھا اس دن کی نیت سے لیکن اس نے متعین نہیں کیا کہ وہ فلاں دن کا روزہ رکھ رہا ہے تو یہ جائز ہے اور دورمضانوں میں جائز نہیں ہے جب تک کہ متعین نہ کرے کہ وہ فلاں سنہ کے رمضان کا روزہ رکھ رہا ہے۔ تشریح : جب کسی شخص پر فوائت زیادہ ہو جا ئیں اور وہ فوائت ایک ہی جنس کے متحدہ فرائض کے قبیل سے میاں ان میں تعیین کے شرط ہونے یا نہ ہونے میں فقہاء کا اختلاف ہے۔ اصح قول یہ ہے کہ جب چھوٹے ہوئے فرمائش ایک ہی جنس کے ہوں تو الگ الگ تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور جب ان کی جنس الگ الگ ہو تو عین ضروری ہے۔ ولو كانت الفوات كثيرة فاشتغل بالقضاء يحتاج الى تعيين الظهر او العصر او نحوها وينوى ايضاً ظهر يوم كذا وعصر يوم كذا فاذا اراد تسهيل الامر ينوى اول ظهر علیه او آخر ظهر علیا واذا نوى الاول وصلى فيما يليه يصير اولا (تاتار خانیه: ج/ ص/ ۴۳۹)
اگر کسی شخص پر ایک ہی رمضان کا روز د تھا اب اس نے قضا کی نیت سے وہ روز وہ کھلیا لیکن اس نے تین بار کہ وہ فلاں دن کا روز در رکھ رہا ہے تو اس کا روزہ صحیح ہو جائے گا کیونکہ ایک رمضان کے سب روز سے ایک ہی جنس کے ہیں اور ایک جنس کے فروض متحدہ میں تمیز کے لئے تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے البتہ اگر اس پر دور مضان کے روزے تنا ہیں تو جب تک وہ یہ تعین نہ کرے کہ کون سے سن کے رمضان کے روزے رکھ رہا ہے اس وقت تک اس کی تند درست نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اب جنس مختلف ہو چکی ہے اس لئے تعیین لازم ہے۔ فرق بين الـصــلاة وبين الصوم: في الصوم لو كان عليه قضاء يومين فقضى يوما ولم ين جاز لان فى الصوم السبب واحد وهو الشهر وكان الواجب عليه اكمال العدد...
It can be performed, therefore specification of prayer is necessary. But if the time becomes narrow, e.g., the time for Zuhr prayer becomes so narrow that only Zuhr prayer can be offered therein, then the need for specification of prayer should not remain. Yet you still deem specification of prayer necessary in such a situation. Why?
Answer: Because when the time is narrow, although performing another prayer besides the prayer of that time is permissible, doing so is not permissible. Thus, when even during narrow time one can perform another prayer besides the time's prayer, the need for specification does not remain. And specification is necessary. Al-Shami said under it: In al-Ashbah, specification is not dropped due to narrowness of time, because if one begins a supererogatory prayer therein, it is valid although forbidden. (Shami, Karachi, vol.7, p.418)
And no part of the parts of time is determined by the servant's verbal specification; it is only determined by his action, like the one who breaks an oath: none of the types of expiation is determined except within his action. This pertains to performance (ada).
Translation: And no part of the parts of time is determined by the servant's verbal specification; it is only determined by his action, like the one who breaks an oath: none of the types of expiation is determined except within his action. This is in performance. Explanation: If someone specifies by word but does not specify by action, his specification is not considered; rather, practical specification is necessary. For example, a person breaks an oath and has three options of expiation: (1) feeding ten poor people, (2) clothing them, (3) freeing a slave. If he verbally specifies one, his verbal specification is not valid until he does it in action, i.e., performs one of the three. Or like a person who verbally says 'I will pray Zuhr at 3 o'clock' — mere lip movement does not constitute specification until he starts the prayer. But this detail is in ada; if the acts of worship are qada (make-up), then verbal specification is necessary.
And as for qada: specification is absolutely necessary, whether prayer, fasting, or Hajj.
Translation: And as for qada: specification is necessary, whether prayer, fasting, or Hajj. Explanation: Qada, whether prayer, fasting, or Hajj, requires specification in each. Allama Jamoomi objects: just as specification is necessary in qada, it should also be necessary in ada, as detailed above.
The answer is that in ada, the basic specification is sufficient, e.g., he says 'I am performing Zuhr prayer', while in qada, additional specification is intended, i.e., along with the prayer, specification of the day is also necessary, e.g., he says 'I am performing the Zuhr prayer of such-and-such day.'
And when missed prayers are many, they differed about the condition of specification for distinguishing the identical obligations of the same kind. The most authentic view is that if one owes the qada of one Ramadan day and fasts a day intending it but does not specify that he is fasting for a particular day, it is permissible. But it is not permissible for two Ramadans unless he specifies that he is fasting for the Ramadan of a certain year.
Translation: And when missed prayers are many, they differed about the condition of specification for distinguishing the identical obligations of the same kind. The most authentic view is that if one owes the qada of one Ramadan day and fasts a day intending it but does not specify that he is fasting for a particular day, it is permissible. But it is not permissible for two Ramadans unless he specifies that he is fasting for the Ramadan of a certain year. Explanation: When a person has many missed acts and they are identical obligations of the same kind, there is disagreement among jurists about the condition of specification. The most authentic view is that when the missed acts are of the same kind, separate specification is not necessary; and when their kinds are different, specification is necessary. 'And if missed prayers are many and he engages in qada, he needs to specify whether it is Zuhr or 'Asr etc., and also intend Zuhr of such day and 'Asr of such day. If he wants to ease the matter, he intends the first Zuhr upon him or the last Zuhr upon him. If he intends the first and prays immediately after, it becomes the first.' (Tatar Khaniyya, vol., p.439)
If a person had the qada of only one Ramadan, he fasted a day with the intention of qada but did not specify that he is fasting for a particular day, his fast is valid because all days of one Ramadan are of the same kind; for identical obligations of the same kind, specification is not necessary. However, if he had the qada of two Ramadans, his fast will not be valid until he specifies which year's Ramadan he is fasting for, because now the kind differs, thus specification is necessary. Difference between prayer and fasting: In fasting, if one owes qada of two days and fasts one day without specifying, it is permissible because in fasting the cause is one, i.e., the month, and what was obligatory upon him was completing the number...
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a maxim from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir regarding the rule of ta'yin (specification) in acts of worship. The text distinguishes between ada (on-time performance) and qada (make-up) regarding the necessity of verbal specification. In ada, the maxim states that verbal specification alone does not determine the time; rather, action is what specifies it. For example, when the time for Zuhr is ample, one must verbally specify that he is praying Zuhr because other prayers could be performed. But if the time is so narrow that only Zuhr can be prayed, the need for verbal specification drops—though the relied-upon position (as per al-Shami) maintains that specification is still required even then, because one could theoretically start a supererogatory prayer (even if sinful), so the possibility of other prayers remains. This is based on the analogy of one who breaks an oath: the specific expiatory act is not determined by mere words but by the action itself. In qada, however, verbal specification is absolutely necessary because there is no specific time for make-up prayers; one must specify which missed prayer is being performed. Moreover, for multiple qada of the same kind (e.g., several missed Zuhr prayers), the 'asahh (most authentic) position is that additional specification of the day is not required if they are of the same type; but if they belong to different types (e.g., qada of two different Ramadans), one must specify the year. This difference arises because the cause (sabab) in fasting is the month, which unifies the obligations, whereas in prayer each missed prayer is a separate obligation with a unique time. The text also cites al-Tatar Khaniyya for a practical easing: one may intend the first or last missed prayer and it will be valid.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of which particular act of worship is intended, either verbally or through action.
اداء (ada'): Performance of an act of worship within its prescribed time.
قضاء (qada'): Performance of a missed act of worship after its time has passed.
فوات (ج. فوائت) (fawat (pl. fawa'it)): Missed obligations that need to be made up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'asahh view in the Hanafi school, if a person owes qada of five days from two different Ramadans (three from 1440, two from 1441), and he fasts one day intending qada but without specifying which year, is his fast valid?
A) Yes, because all missed fasts are the same type.
B) No, because the years differ, so specification of the year is required.
C) Yes, because he intended qada generally.
D) No, because he must specify the exact day of the month.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ta'yin by action suffices in ada, but in qada verbal ta'yin is necessary; for multiple missed acts of the same kind, additional specification of the day is not required.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
The Maxim of Specification: Ta'yin for Distinguishing Types in Qada Prayers
Critical refinement of a ruling on intention for qada prayers using a legal maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-ta'yin li tamyiz al-ajnas' to evaluate differing views on intention for missed prayers and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Specification in intention is to distinguish types of worship, not merely to maintain order.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym clarifies a critical dispute regarding the intention for missed (qada) prayers. A view from al-Muhit suggests ta'yin is only needed to preserve tartib, and if tartib drops, one general intention suffices. Ibn Nujaym rejects this, affirming that the Hanafi maxim 'Specification is for distinguishing types' governs here. Understanding this maxim is essential for framing a correct fatwa on qada prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the contested ruling: Is the intention of specification (ta'yin) required for missed prayers when the obligation of order (tartib) has dropped due to a large number of missed prayers?
The passage directly presents this dispute between the view of al-Muhit and the relied-upon view.
2
State the governing Hanafi maxim
State the maxim: 'al-ta'yin li tamyiz al-ajnas' (Specification is for distinguishing types). This is a fundamental legal principle in Hanafi ibadat.
The maxim applies to all acts of worship that have different causes (asbab).
3
Analyze the view from al-Muhit
Examine why al-Muhit argues that ta'yin is not inherently required but only needed to maintain tartib. According to this view, when tartib drops, a single intention (e.g., Zuhr) suffices for all missed prayers.
This view treats ta'yin as a means to an end rather than a requirement by itself.
4
Apply the maxim to critique the opposing view
Use the maxim to show why al-Muhit's reasoning is flawed: if ta'yin is for distinguishing types, then even if tartib drops, prayers of different types (Zuhr, Asr, etc.) still require separate specification. The maxim is not contingent on tartib.
Ibn Nujaym calls the opposing view 'problematic' because it would nullify the agreed-upon rule.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which position is relied upon in fatwa. The passage states that the view of Qadi Khan and other Hanafi scholars (requiring ta'yin) is al-mu'tamad (the relied-upon).
This resolution is based on the authority of later Hanafi masters and its consistency with core usul.

اسی طرح نیت کرتا رہے تو اسی نیت سے اس کی قضاء نمازیں ادا ہوتی رہیں گی یہ طریقہ ان لوگوں کے لئے مفید ہے جن کو فوت شدہ نمازوں کی تعداد معلوم نہ ہوں یہ چھوٹی ہوئی نمازوں میں اشتباہ پیدا ہو جائے یا آسمانی کے مقصد سے اس طرح سے نیت کرے تو اس طرح کی تعیین کافی ہے۔
وَذَكَرَ فِي الْمُحِيْطِ : أَنَّ نِيَّةَ التَّعْمِيْنِ فِى الصَّلَاةِ لَمْ تُشْتَرَطُ بِااعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ مُخْتَلِفٌ مُتَعَدِدٌ، بَلْ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ مُرَاعَاةَ التَّرْتِيْبِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُهُ مُرَاعَاةُ التَّرْتِيبِ إِلَّا بَنية النَّعْيَيْنِ حَتَّى لَوْسَقَطَ التَّرْتِيْبُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْفَوَائِتِ تَكْفِيْهِ نِيَّةُ الظُّهْرِ لَا غَيْرَ، وَهَذَا مُشْكِل وَمَا ذَكَرَهُ أَصْحَابُنَا كَقَاضِيْ خَانٍ وَغَيْرِهِ خِلَافُهُ، وَهُوَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ كَذَا فِي النَّبِيِّنِ. ترجمہ: اور جیب میں ذکرکیا گیا ہے کہ نمازمیں تعین کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ واجب مختلف شعور ہے بلکہ اس اعتبار سے کہ ترتیب کی رعایت اس پر واجب ہے اور ترتیب کی رعایت بدون نیت تعین ممکن نہیں ہے تھی کہ کثرت فوائت کی وجہ سے اگر ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے تو ظہر کی نیت کافی ہے نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ اور یہ مشکل ہے اور جو ہمارے اصحاب نے ذکر کیا ہے جیسے قاضی خاں وغیرہ وہ اس کے خلاف ہے اور یہی قابل اعتماد ہے تبیین میں اسی طرح ہے۔ تشریح : علامه ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ محیط میں یہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ نیت کی تعین نماز میں اس کے شرط نہیں ہے کہ واجب مختلف اور متعدد ہے بلکہ اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ مصلی پر ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا واجب ہے اور تعیین کی نیت کے بغیر ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا ممکن نہیں لہذا اگر کثرت فوائت کی وجہ سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے تو صرف ظہر کی نیت اس کے لئے کافی ہوگی یوم وغیرہ کی نیت کی ضرورت نہ ہوگی ۔ علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحب محیط کی یہ تشریح مشکل ہے اور وجہ اشکال یہ ہے کہ اس بات کو تلیم کرنے کی صورت میں فقہاء کا وہ قاعدہ ختم ہو جاتا ہے جس پر انہوں نے اتفاق کیا ہے وہ یہ کہ تین اجناس کی تمیز ے لئے ہوتی ہے اور تمام نمازیں مختلف اجناس کے قبیل سے ہیں کیونکہ اسباب مختلف ہیں۔ علامہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارے اصحاب مثلاً قاضی خاں وغیرہ نے اس سلسلہ میں جو بات ذکر کی ہے وہ اگر چان کے خلاف ہے لیکن وہی معتمد ہے۔
Similarly, if he continues with this intention, his missed prayers will be fulfilled with this intention. This method is useful for those who do not know the number of missed prayers or are confused about them. If he intends with this method, such specification is sufficient. And it is mentioned in Al-Muhit: 'The intention of specification in prayer is not required considering that the obligatory prayers are different and numerous, but rather considering that observing the order is obligatory upon him, and he cannot observe order except with the intention of specification. So if order is dropped due to the abundance of missed prayers, the intention of Zuhr suffices him, not otherwise. And this is problematic; what our companions like Qadi Khan and others mentioned is contrary to it, and it is the relied-upon, as in Al-Tibyan.' Translation: And it is mentioned in Al-Muhit that the intention of specification in prayer is not a condition because the obligatory prayers are different and numerous, but rather because observing order is obligatory upon him, and observing order is not possible without the intention of specification. If order drops due to abundance of misses, then the intention of Zuhr alone suffices, not the intention of day or other. And this is problematic; what our companions like Qadi Khan and others mentioned is contrary to it, and it is reliable, as in Al-Tibyan. Explanation: Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that it is mentioned in Al-Muhit that intention of specification in prayer is not a condition because the obligatory is different and numerous, but rather because observing order is obligatory upon the worshipper, and without intention of specification, observing order is not possible. So if order drops due to abundance of misses, then the intention of Zuhr alone suffices; there is no need for intention of day or other. Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that this explanation of the author of Al-Muhit is problematic, and the reason for the problem is that if this statement is accepted, then the rule upon which the jurists have agreed is nullified, which is that specification is for distinguishing types, and all prayers are of different types because their causes are different. Allama says that what our companions like Qadi Khan etc. mentioned is contrary to this, but it is the relied-upon.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage deals with the requirement of ta'yin (specification) in the intention for performing missed (qada) prayers. The author begins by presenting a practical method: if a person has a large number of missed prayers and does not know exactly how many or which ones, they can make a general intention to make up prayers, and that will suffice. This is a necessary concession for those with many qada prayers. The core legal discussion is the quote from al-Muhit, where it is argued that the intention of specification is not inherently required because the different missed prayers are distinct obligations, but rather it is required solely to maintain the obligatory order (tartib) among the prayers. According to this view, if the number of missed prayers becomes so great that the order is dropped (by fatwa), then even the intention of just Zuhr will suffice for all, without specifying each. However, the author (Ibn Nujaym) strongly criticizes this position, calling it 'problematic' (mushkil). The reason is that this would undermine the established Hanafi rule that specification is meant to distinguish between different types (ajnas) of worship. All prayers are of different types because each has a unique cause (sabab), so ta'yin is necessary to differentiate them as a matter of principle. Therefore, the relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is the opposite: that specification is required even when tartib drops, because the very natures of the acts differ. The author affirms that the view of Qadi Khan and others is correct and authoritative.

Key Terms
نِية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): The intention of specification, i.e., specifying which particular prayer (e.g., Zuhr of a certain day) one is performing.
تَرْتِيب (tartib): The obligatory order between obligatory prayers within the same day, or between missed prayers.
قَضَاء (qada): Making up an obligatory prayer that was missed after its prescribed time.
التعيين لتمييز الأجناس (al-ta'yin li tamyiz al-ajnas): The maxim: Specification is for distinguishing types. It means that when performing acts of worship of different types (based on cause), one must specify which type in intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, why is intention of specification (ta'yin) required for missed prayers?
A) Because it is a condition for the validity of prayer.
B) To maintain the obligatory order between prayers.
C) To distinguish between different types of prayers.
D) Because it is a sunnah of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'Specification is for distinguishing types' requires ta'yin in intention for missed prayers even when the obligation of order drops.

Intention for Tayammum: Specifying Hadath vs Janabah
Ruling on whether specification of impurity is required in tayammum intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the required intention for tayammum and apply the principle that conditions require only existence to resolve the dispute with al-Khassaf.

Core Idea
Tayammum needs only intention of purification, not impurity type, because it is a condition, not worship.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling: whether one must specify the type of impurity (hadath or janabah) when performing tayammum. The dispute with al-Khassaf reveals a foundational distinction between conditions (shurut) and acts of worship (‘ibadat). Understanding this distinction is essential for correct fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is tayammum and the ruling under discussion is the requirement of intention to specify the impurity type.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that no specification between hadath and janabah is required; general intention of purification suffices.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Contrast with al-Khassaf’s view
Al-Khassaf argues that specification is necessary because both tayammum acts are physically identical, so intention must distinguish them—similar to the five daily prayers.
Al-Khassaf is a Hanafi scholar, so this is intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi jurists respond that tayammum is a condition (shart), not an intended act of worship. Conditions require only their existence, not specification. The analogy to prayer is a qiyas ma‘a al-fariq.
Key principle: al-shurut yu‘tabaru wujudiha la ta‘yiniha.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a person in janabah who intends only wudu can still pray with that tayammum; al-Khassaf would require specifying janabah.
The fatwa is on the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوا : فِي التَّيَمُّمِ لَا يَجِبُ التَّمْيِيزِ بَيْنَ الْحَدَثِ وَالْجَنَابَةِ حَتَّى لَوْ تَيَمَّمَ الْجُنُبُ يُرِيدُ بِهِ الْوُضُوْءُ جَازَ خِلَافَاً لِلْخَصَّافِ لِكَوْنِهِ يَقَعُ لَهُمَا عَلَى صِفَةِ وَاحِدَةٍ، فَيُمَيَّزُ بِالنِّيَّةِ كَالصَّلَاةِ الْمَفْرُوضَةِ، قَالُوا: وَلَيْسَ بِصَحِيح؛ لأنَّ الحَاجَةَ إِلَيْهَا لِبَقَعَ طَهَارَةً، وَإِذَا وَقَعَ طَهَارَة جَازَ أَنْ يُؤدِّيَ بِهِ مَا شَاءَ لأَنَّ الشَّرُوْطَ يُرَاعِي وُجُوْدُهَا لَا غَيْرَ، أَلَا تَرَىٰ أَنَّهُ لَوْ تَيَمَّمَ الر جَازَ لَهُ أَنْ يُصَلَّى بِهِ غَيْرَهُ.
ترجمہ: اور فقہاء نے تیمم کے سلسلہ میں فرمایا کہ حدث اور جنابت کے مابین تمیز ضروری نہیں ہے حتی کہ اگر کسی نے وضو کے ارادے سے تیمم کیا تو جائز ہے خصاف کا اختلاف ہے یتیم کے دونوں کے لئے ایک ہی طریقہ پر ہونے کی وجہ سے تو نیت کے ذریعہ تمیز کی جائے کی جیسے فرض نماز اور فقہاء نے کہا یہ بیج نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے کہ طہارت ہو جائے اور جب طہارت ہو گئی تو اس سے ادا کرنا جائز ہے جو چاہے اس لئے کہ شرائط میں صرف ان کا حصول مقصود ہوتا ہے نہ کہ ان کا غیر ۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے اگر عصر کے لئے تقسیم کیا تو اس کے علاوہ اس سے پڑھنا جائز ہے۔
تشریح تیم حدث اور جنابت دونوں کے لئے ہوتا ہے لیکن دونوں میں تمیز پیدا کرنے کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے ولا يجب التمييز بين الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريدبه الوضوء جائز وعليه الفتوى (بند بیج اس (۲۶) جبکہ امام خصاف فرماتے ہیں کہ حدث اور جنابت دونوں کے لئے تیم ایک ہی طریقہ پر ہوتا ہے اس لئے دونوں میں تمیز کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے جیسے فرائض خمسہ ایک ہی انداز پر پڑھی جاتی ہیں لیکن تمیز کے لئے نیت ضروری ہوتی ہے۔ قتصاد فرماتے ہیں کہ تمیم کا مقصد طہارت ہے خواہ جنابت کا تختم ہو یا حدث کا لہذا اس سے نماز وغیرہ پڑھنا جائز ہے لہذا تیم کو نماز پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے اس لیئے کہ نماز عبادت مقصودہ میں سے ہے اور تیم شرائط میں سے لہذا شرط کا صرف وجود کافی ہوتا ہے نیت ضروری نہیں ہوتی اس لئے مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عصر کی نماز کے لئے تیم کیا تو اس سے دوسری نماز بھی پڑھی جاسکتی ہے ویصلى الرجل بتيممه ماشاء من الصلواة من الفرائض والنوافل الفوائت مالم يحدث او تزول العلة او يجد الماء (تاتار خانیه ج ۱ ص۲۵۸) علامہ جموعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کو یہاں ذکر کرنا بر محل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہاں ان عبادات کا بیان ہے جو منوی ہیں ۔
And they said: In tayammum, distinction between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah) is not required, so much so that if a person in a state of janabah performs tayammum intending wudu, it is permissible, contrary to al-Khassaf, because tayammum occurs for both in the same manner, so it is distinguished by intention like the obligatory prayer. They said: This is not correct, because the need for it is for purification to occur, and when purification occurs, it is permissible to perform with it whatever he wishes, because conditions only consider their existence, nothing else. Do you not see that if he performed tayammum for Asr, it is permissible for him to pray another with it. Translation: And the jurists said regarding tayammum that distinction between minor and major impurity is not necessary; even if a person in janabah does tayammum with the intention of wudu, it is permissible—al-Khassaf disagreed because tayammum for both is done in the same manner, so distinction should be made by intention as in the case of obligatory prayers. And the jurists said: This is not correct because the need is for purification to occur, and when purification occurs, it is permissible to perform with it whatever he wishes, because conditions only require their existence, not other considerations. Do you not see that if he performed tayammum for Asr, it is permissible to pray another with it. Explanation: Tayammum is performed for both minor and major impurity, but intention to distinguish between them is not required. 'Distinction between hadath and janabah is not obligatory, even if a person in janabah does tayammum intending wudu, it is permissible, and the fatwa is upon it' (Bada'i'. while Imam al-Khassaf says: Tayammum for both is done in the same manner, so intention to distinguish is necessary, just as the five obligatory prayers are performed in the same manner but intention is required to distinguish them. The chosen view says: The purpose of tayammum is purification, whether it is for janabah or hadath, so it is permissible to pray with it. Therefore, comparing tayammum to prayer is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq) because prayer is an intended act of worship, while tayammum is among the conditions. So for conditions, mere existence suffices; intention is not necessary. The ruling: If someone performs tayammum for Asr prayer, he can pray another prayer with it. 'A man may pray with his tayammum whatever prayers he wishes, obligatory and supererogatory and missed, as long as he does not hadath, or the excuse ceases, or he finds water' (Tatarkhaniyya vol.1 p.258). Allama Jami' says: Mentioning this issue here is not appropriate because this is a discussion of acts of worship that are intended (maqsuuda).
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement of specifying the type of impurity when performing tayammum. The Hanafi position, as stated by the (unnamed) jurists, is that no distinction between hadath (minor impurity) and janabah (major impurity) is obligatory in tayammum. Even if a person in janabah intends only wudu, the tayammum is valid because the act itself is the same for both conditions. The reason is that tayammum is a substitute for both, and the essential need is simply to achieve purification. Once purification is achieved, it can be used for any act requiring purity. The opposing view of al-Khassaf states that since both tayammum are performed in the same physical manner, intention is needed to distinguish them, just as the five daily prayers are identical in form but require specific intention. The Hanafi jurists refute this by pointing out that tayammum is a condition (shart) for prayer, not an intended act of worship ('ibada maqsuda) itself. Conditions only require existence, not specific designation. Therefore, comparing tayammum to prayer is a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The fatwa is on this Hanafi view. The author also cites al-Tatarkhaniyya that a person can perform any number of prayers with one tayammum as long as the state of purity is not broken. Allama al-Jami' comments that mentioning this ruling here is somewhat out of place because this section deals with acts of worship that require intention (muniyyat).

Key Terms
تَيَمُّم (tayammum): Dry purification using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
حَدَث (hadath): State of minor impurity requiring wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine).
جَنَابَة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (e.g., sexual intercourse, menstruation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum intention required for tayammum to be valid?
A) Intending to remove hadath or janabah specifically.
B) Intending purification (taharah) in general.
C) Intending a specific prayer, like Zuhr.
D) Intending to perform tayammum for the most recent impurity.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tayammum requires only the intention of purification, not specification of the impurity, because it is a condition for worship, not worship itself.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Determination in a Single Genus is Void
Explains the maxim ta'yin in single genus is void with derivations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'ta'yin in a single genus is void' to identify when specification of intention is required or void in acts of worship, using the criterion of cause (sabab).

Core Idea
Specifying intention within the same genus is futile — the genus is defined by the cause, not the day.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi legal maxim that governs the validity of intention (niyyah) in worship. The maxim states that if an act belongs to a single genus (jins), then specifying a particular instance is void because there is nothing to distinguish. The genus is determined by the cause (sabab) of the obligation; all prayers have different causes, while all fasts of one Ramadan share one cause. Understanding this maxim is essential for muftis when issuing fatwas about qada and expiations.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its meaning
Restate the Arabic qawida 'فَنِيَّةُ التَّعْيِينِ فِي الْجِنسِ الْوَاحِدِ لَغَوُ' and its English translation. Recognize that 'ta'yin' means specifying a particular instance in intention.
The maxim is void because there is no benefit in distinguishing when only one genus exists.
2
Identify the purpose of ta'yin
The purpose of ta'yin (specification) is to create distinction between different genera. When only one genus is present, the specification is unnecessary and therefore void.
3
Define the criterion for genus: sabab
The passage states that difference of genus is known by difference of cause (sabab). Understand that sabab is what triggers the obligation (wujub) or the act of performance (ada).
The rule is: 'وَيُعْرَفُ اخْتِلَافُ الْجِنْسِ بِاخْتِلَافِ السَّبَبِ'.
4
Apply the criterion to prayers and fasts
All prayers have different causes (each time of day is a distinct sabab), so they are different genera and require ta'yin. All fasts of one Ramadan share the cause of shuhud al-shahr, making them a single genus; thus ta'yin is void.
Example: qada of two Zuhr prayers from different days requires specifying each day. Qada of multiple Ramadan fasts from one month does not require specifying each day.
5
Note the internal Hanafi dispute and its thamarah
Some Hanafi scholars (Qadi Abu Zaid) hold that the cause for Ramadan fasts is the first part of each day; others ('Allama Sarkhasi) hold it is the witnessing of the month. Sahib al-Hidayah reconciles: the month causes overall obligation, each day causes performance. The practical effect is that qada from one Ramadan needs no specification, but from multiple Ramadans requires specification.
This reconciliation is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

فَنِيَّةُ التَّعْيِينِ فِي الْجِنسِ الْوَاحِدِ لَغَوُ لِعَلمٍ الْفَائِدَةِ والتصرف إِذَا لَمْ يُصَادِق مَحَلَّهُ كَانَ لِغَوا ترجمه : پس جنس واحد میں تعیین کی نیست لغو ہے فائدہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور تصرف جب اپنے کل میں نہ ہو تشریح جنس واحد میں نیت تعیین افو ہے تین نیت کا مقصد اجناس کے مابین تمیز پیدا کرتا ہوتا ہے بہت واحد ہونے کی صورت میں مفقود ہے جنس واحد میں نیت تعیین کا تصرف غیر حل تصرف ہے جو لغو اور بے فائدہ ہے اگر کوئی آج کا روزہ رکھ رہا ہے تو یہ کافی ہے کہ میں آج کا روزہ رکھ رہا ہوں، یہ ضروری نہیں کہ یہ بھی کہے کہ کل کا نہیں رکھ رہا ہوں ۔
وَيُعْرَفُ اخْتِلَافُ الْجِنْسِ بِاخْتِلَافِ السَّبَبِ.
:ترجمه اور اختلاف جنس کا پتہ اختلاف سبب سے ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: اتحاد جنس اور اختلاف جنس کا پتہ اختلاف سب سے چلتا ہے اگر سب مختلف ہے تو اختلاف پر ہے اور اگر سبب متحد ہے تو اتحاد جنس ہے۔ وباختلاف السبب يختلف الواجب ( تاتارخانيج راص (۴۲۹) والصَّلوةَ كُلُّهَا مِنْ قَبْلِ المُخْتَلِفِ حَتَّى الظَّهْرَيْنِ مِنْ يَوْمَيْنِ أَوِ الْعَصْرَيْنِ مِنْ يَوْمَينِ بِخِلَافِ أَيَّامٍ رَمَضَانَ فَإِنَّهُ يَجْمَعُهَا شُهُوْدُ الشَّهْرِ .
ترجمہ: اور تمام نمازیں مختلف جنس کے قبیل سے ہیں حتی کہ دو دن کی دو ظہر کی نماز میں یا دوران کی عصر کے نمازیں بخلاف ایام رمضان کے اس لئے کہ شہود شہر ان کو جمع کر دیتا ہے۔
تشریح: جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ اختلاف جنس کا مدار اختلاف سبب پر ہے تو تمام نمازیں مختلف الاجناس ہو۔ گی کیونکہ ان کے وجوب کا سبب مختلف ہے۔ لہذا ان میں سے جس وقت کی بھی فرض نماز ادا کریں گے اس وقت کہ اس دن کی تعیین ضروری ہوگی ، مثلاً آج کی ظہر اور کل گذشتہ کی ظہر یا آج کی عصر یا کل گذشتہ کی عصر کا سب وجوب مختلف ہے تو ہر ایک کی ادائیگی کے لئے نیت تعیین ضروری ہے۔
فائدہ: رمضان کے سبب وجوب میں فقہاء کرام کا اختلاف ہے۔ (۱) رمضان کے روزے کا سبب دن ہے رات نہیں یہ قاضی ابوزید کا اختیار کردہ مسلک ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ دن کا جزء اول اس کے روزے کے وجوب کا سبب ہے۔ (۲) رمضان کے روزوں کا سبب مطابق شہور شہر ہے اس میں رات اور دن شامل ہیں یہ علامہ سرخی کا پسندیدہ قول ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے دونوں قولوں کے درمیان عدم منافاة کا قول نقل کرنے کے بعد اس طور پر جمع کیا ہے کہ رمضان کے مہینہ کا جزء اول پورے رمضان کے روزوں کے لئے سبب وجوب ہے پھر ہر دن وجوب ادا کا سبب ہے۔ فَتَفَرَّعَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ قَضَا يَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ، فَصَامَهُ بِنِيَّةٍ يَوْمٍ آخَرَ، أَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ قَضَاءُ صَوْمِ يَوْمَيْنِ، أَوْ أَكْثَرَ ، فَصَامَ يَوْماً عَنْ قَضَاءَ صَوْمِ يَوْمَيْنِ، أَوْ أَكْثَرَ جَازَ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا نَوى عَنْ رَمَضَانَيْنِ، لَا يَجُوزُ لاخْتِلَافِ السَّبَبِ، كَمَا إِذَا نَوَىٰ ظُهْرَيْنِ، أَوْ ظُهْراً عَنْ عَصْرٍ، أَوْ نَوى ظُهْرَ يَوْمِ السَّبْتِ، وَعَلَيْهِ ظُهْرُ يَوْمِ الْحَمِيْسِ
:ترجمہ: چنانچہ اس پر تفریح کی ہے کہ اگر اس کے ذمہ کسی متعین دن کی قضاء ہو اور اس نے دوسرے دن کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا یا اس کے ذمہ دو دن یا اس سے زیادہ دن کے روزوں کی قضا ہو اور اس نے دو یا دو سے زائد وزوں کی قضا کی طرف سے روزہ رکھا تو جائز ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس نے دور مضانوں کی طرف سے نیت کی تو جائز نہیں ہے سبب کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ جب کہ اس نے نیت کی دو ظہر کی یا ایک ظہر کی عصر کی طرف سے یا ہفتہ کے دن ظہر کی نیت کرے حال یہ کہ اس کے ذمہ جمعرات کی ظہر ہے۔
وعلى هذا أدَاءُ الْكَفَّارَاتِ لَا يَحْتَاجُ فِيْهِ إِلَى التَّعْيِييْنِ فِي جِنْسِ وَاحِدٍ، وَلَوْ عَيَّنَ لَغَى. وفي " الأجْنَاسِ لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ كَمَا حَقَّقْنَاهُ فِى الظَّهَارِ مِنْ كِتَابِنَا شَرْحُ الْكَنْزِ» .
ترجمه: اور اس پر کفارات کی ادائیگی ہے کہ اس کی جنس واحد میں تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے تعین کی تو وہ لغو ہو گی اور اجناس میں وہ ضروری ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے اپنی کتاب "شرح الكنز“ کے باب الظهار میں تحقیق بیان کر دیا ہے۔
The determination of specification in a single genus is void due to lack of benefit, and an action when it does not correspond to its locus becomes void. Translation: So, determination in a single genus is void because there is no benefit, and the action when it is not in its proper place. Explanation: Intention of specification in a single genus is void. The purpose of intention is to create distinction between genera; when there is only one genus, it is absent. The act of intending specification in a single genus is an invalid act, void and useless. If someone is fasting today, it is sufficient to say 'I am fasting today'; it is not necessary to also say 'I am not fasting tomorrow.'
And the difference of genus is known by difference of cause.
Translation: And the difference of genus is known by difference of cause.
Explanation: Unity of genus and difference of genus are known by difference of cause. If the cause is different, then there is difference; if the cause is unified, then there is unity of genus. And with difference of cause, the obligatory differs (TatarKhani, vol. 429). And all prayers are from the category of different genera, even the two Zuhr prayers of two days or the two Asr prayers of two days, unlike the days of Ramadan, for the witnessing of the month unites them.
Translation: And all prayers are from the category of different genera, even the two Zuhr prayers of two days or the two Asr prayers of two days, unlike the days of Ramadan, because the witnessing of the month unites them.
Explanation: When it is known that the basis of difference of genus is difference of cause, then all prayers are of different genera because the cause of their obligation is different. Therefore, whenever one performs the obligatory prayer of a particular time, specification of that day is necessary. For example, today's Zuhr and yesterday's Zuhr or today's Asr or yesterday's Asr: each has a different cause of obligation, so for each performance, intention of specification is necessary.
Benefit: There is a difference among fuqaha regarding the cause of obligation of Ramadan. (1) The cause of the Ramadan fast is the day, not the night—this is the chosen view of Qadi Abu Zaid, based on the first part of the day being the cause of obligation. (2) The cause of Ramadan fasts is the witnessing of the month, which includes night and day—this is the preferred view of 'Allama Sarkhasi. Sahib al-Hidayah, after reporting non-contradiction between the two views, reconciled by saying that the first part of the month of Ramadan is the cause of obligation for all Ramadan fasts, then each day is the cause of the obligation to perform.
Therefore, it is derived from that: if one owes qada of a specific day and fasts it with the intention of another day, or owes qada of two or more days and fasts one day for the qada of two or more days, it is valid. Unlike if he intends for two Ramadans—it is not valid due to difference of cause, just as if he intends two Zuhr prayers, or Zuhr for Asr, or intends Zuhr of Saturday while he owes Zuhr of Thursday.
Translation: So, it is derived that if one owes qada of a specific day and fasts with the intention of another day, or owes qada of two or more days and fasts one day for the qada of two or more days, it is valid. Unlike the case when he intends for two Ramadans—it is not valid due to difference of cause, just as when he intends two Zuhr prayers, or Zuhr for Asr, or intends Zuhr of Saturday while he owes Zuhr of Thursday.
And upon this, the performance of expiations does not require specification in a single genus, and if he specifies, it is void. But in different genera, it is necessary, as we verified in the chapter of Zihar from our book Sharh al-Kanz.
Translation: And upon this, the performance of expiations: in a single genus it does not need specification, and if he specifies, it is void. And in different genera, it is necessary, as we verified in our book Sharh al-Kanz in the chapter of Zihar.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage discusses a key qawida: 'Determination (ta'yin) in a single genus is void.' The author, from a Hanafi perspective, explains that when all items are of the same genus, specifying one in intention is meaningless because there is no need to distinguish. The purpose of ta'yin is to differentiate between genera; where there is only one genus, it serves no purpose. For example, if one is fasting today, it is enough to intend 'today's fast' without negating other days. The passage then establishes that difference of genus is determined by difference of cause (sabab). This is a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh. All prayers (salat) are considered different genera because each prayer's obligation has a distinct cause (e.g., the time of day). Thus, if one has missed a Zuhr prayer from two different days, one must specify which day's Zuhr is intended. However, the fasts of Ramadan are an exception: they are all of the same genus because the witnessing of the month (shuhud al-shahr) unifies them. The cause of obligation for Ramadan fasts is debated among Hanafi scholars: some say the cause is the day itself, others say the month as a whole. The author reconciles by stating that the first part of the month causes the obligation for all, and each day causes the obligation to perform. Based on this, if one owes qada of a specific day from Ramadan, fasting with the intention of another day from the same Ramadan is valid because the genus is same. But if one owes qada from two different Ramadans, specification is required because the causes differ (different years). Similarly, for kaffarat (expiation), if multiple expiations are of the same genus (e.g., all are for breaking oaths), no specification is needed; if they are of different genera (e.g., one for zihar and one for murder), specification is necessary as detailed in the author's Sharh al-Kanz.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): The specification in intention of a particular item when performing an act of worship.
جنس (jins): Genus or category determined by the cause of obligation.
سبب (sabab): The cause that necessitates an obligation (wujub or ada).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone owes qada of two fasts from the same Ramadan, and he fasts one day with the intention 'qada of Ramadan', is this valid?
A) Yes, because all fasts of one Ramadan are a single genus.
B) No, because each day has a different cause.
C) Yes, only if he specifies which day.
D) No, because intention is not required for qada.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the genus of an act is determined by its cause (sabab); ta'yin is only required when there are multiple genera, otherwise it is void.

Intention Specification in Qada Fasting: The Jins Rule
Furuʿ of the rule: intention specification in qaḍāʾ fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'Unity of genus dispenses with specification; difference of genus necessitates specification' to determine the validity of intention in qada fasting cases.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, acts of worship from the same cause form one genus, eliminating the need to specify each component.

The following passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir applies a foundational qawida: when the genus (jins) of an act of worship is unified, the intention does not require specification of each component; but when the genera differ due to different causes, specification becomes necessary. This rule is crucial for a mufti ruling on the validity of mixed intentions in qada fasting and similar acts.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the maxim: 'Unity of genus dispenses with specification; difference of genus necessitates specification.' Understanding jins as determined by cause (sabab).
2
Examine the furu' cases in the text
Read each case: (1) one specific day's qada intended for another day, (2) multiple qadas intended in one day, (3) two different Ramadans intended in one fast. Note the rulings and the reasoning based on unity or difference of cause.
3
Apply the analogy to prayer cases
The text extends the rule to prayer (e.g., intending Zuhr for Asr). Recognize that the same logic applies across ibadat: different causes create different genera, requiring specification.
4
Extract the legal consequence for fatwa
As a mufti, when asked about intention mismatches, first determine whether the causes are the same or different. If same genus, accept the intention; if different, require specification for validity.

Source Text

فَتَفَرَّعَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ قَضَا يَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ، فَصَامَهُ بِنِيَّةٍ يَوْمٍ آخَرَ، أَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ قَضَاءُ صَوْمِ يَوْمَيْنِ، أَوْ أَكْثَرَ ، فَصَامَ يَوْماً عَنْ قَضَاءَ صَوْمِ يَوْمَيْنِ، أَوْ أَكْثَرَ جَازَ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا نَوى عَنْ رَمَضَانَيْنِ، لَا يَجُوزُ لاخْتِلَافِ السَّبَبِ، كَمَا إِذَا نَوَىٰ ظُهْرَيْنِ، أَوْ ظُهْراً عَنْ عَصْرٍ، أَوْ نَوى ظُهْرَ يَوْمِ السَّبْتِ، وَعَلَيْهِ ظُهْرُ يَوْمِ الْحَمِيْسِ
:ترجمہ: چنانچہ اس پر تفریح کی ہے کہ اگر اس کے ذمہ کسی متعین دن کی قضاء ہو اور اس نے دوسرے دن کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا یا اس کے ذمہ دو دن یا اس سے زیادہ دن کے روزوں کی قضا ہو اور اس نے دو یا دو سے زائد وزوں کی قضا کی طرف سے روزہ رکھا تو جائز ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس نے دور مضانوں کی طرف سے نیت کی تو جائز نہیں ہے سبب کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ جب کہ اس نے نیت کی دو ظہر کی یا ایک ظہر کی عصر کی طرف سے یا ہفتہ کے دن ظہر کی نیت کرے حال یہ کہ اس کے ذمہ جمعرات کی ظہر ہے۔
تشریح اوپر ذکر کیا گیا کہ اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں نیت تعیین ضروری ہے اور اتحاد جنس کی صورت میں نیت تعین ضروری نہیں ہے اور شہود شہر کو تمام روزوں کا ایک ہی سبب قرار دیا گیا ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ پورے رمضان کے روزے جنس واحد ہیں جن میں تعیین نیت ضروری نہیں ہے اسی پر مصنف نے تفریح پیش کی ہے اگر کسی کے ذمہ ہویں رمضان کا روزہ تھا اور اس نے پندرہویں روزے کی نیت سے روزہ رکھ لیا تو دونوں کا سبپ ایک اور جنس ایک ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسا کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر دو رمضان کے دوروزوں کی قضاء ہو تو جب تک وہ تعین نہ کرے
الات تک اختلاف سب کی وجہ سے اس کے لئے بدون تعیین نیست روزہ رکھنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے اگر کسی کے ذمہ دودن کی ظہر کی نماز ہو۔ یا عصر کی نماز ظہر کی نیت سے پڑھ لی یا سنیچر کے دن کی ظہر کی نیت کر کے مار پڑھ لی تو یہ کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اختلاف سبب کی وجہ سے اختلاف جنس کی صورت متحقق ہوگی جس میں تعیین نیست ضروری ہے اور وہ یہاں پر نیت مفقود ہے۔
From this it branched that if someone owes a specific day's qada and he fasts it with the intention of another day, or he owes two or more days of qada and fasts one day intending it for two or more, it is valid, contrary to when he intends for two Ramadans; it is not valid due to the difference of cause, just as if he intends two Zuhr prayers, or Zuhr for Asr, or intends Zuhr of Saturday while he owes Zuhr of Thursday.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage applies the general rule that in a single genus, specification of intention (ta'yin al-niyyah) is not required, while in different genera it is. The rule is derived from the principle that causes (asbab) determine the genus. In this furu', the author examines cases of qada fasting. If a person owes one specific day's fast (e.g., a missed day of Ramadan) and fasts with the intention of a different day, it is valid because both are of the same genus (qada fasting). Similarly, if he owes two or more days and fasts one day intending it for two or more, it is valid. However, if he intends a fast for two different Ramadans (e.g., missed days from two different years), it is not valid because the causes (the missed Ramadans) are different, making the genera different. The author analogizes this to prayer: intending two Zuhr prayers or Zuhr for Asr is invalid. The underlying qawida is that in acts of worship where the genus is one, the intention need not specify the exact reason; but when the genus differs due to different causes, specification is necessary.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): A category of worship defined by its cause (sabab). Multiple causes may create different genera even if the physical act is similar.
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship. Its specification (ta'yin) is sometimes required, sometimes not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi qawida, if a person owes two qada fasts from the same Ramadan and fasts one day intending both, is the fast valid?
A) No, because each fast requires a separate intention.
B) Yes, because both fasts are from the same Ramadan, same cause, same genus.
C) No, because the intention must specify the exact day.
D) Yes, only if the intention is explicitly for both days.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the necessity of specifying intention in qada fasting depends on whether the acts share the same cause: if yes, no specification needed; if no, specification is required.

Intention Specification in Multiple Expiations
Furūʿ on expiations: single genus vs. different genera

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Unity of genus dispenses with specification' to determine when intention specification is required in performing multiple expiations.

Core Idea
Specification of intention is needed only when expiations belong to different genera.

This lesson examines a key qawida (maxim) governing expiations (kaffarat). When a person owes multiple expiations of the same type, freeing slaves without specifying which expiation they fulfill is valid. However, when the causes differ, such as expiation for qatl vs. zihar, specification becomes mandatory. Understanding the genre of each expiation is critical for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
State the qawida in Arabic and English: 'Unity of genus dispenses with specification; difference of genus necessitates specification.' Understand its scope: kaffarat.
2
Distinguish Same vs. Different Genera
Genera of expiations are determined by their causes (sabab). For example, kaffarat for qatl (killing game), zihar, and yamin (breaking an oath) are different genera because their causes differ.
3
Apply to the Furuat
Work through the examples: (a) Two expiations of same genus (e.g., two kaffarat for broken oaths): freeing two slaves without specification fulfills both. (b) Expiations of different genera: freeing one slave without specification fulfills none.
4
Recognize Consequence of Missing Specification
If specification is missing when genera differ, the act does not count toward any of the expiations. The obligation remains unfulfilled.
5
Connect to the Principle's Basis
The difference in genus is due to difference in cause. The ruling (hukm) of kaffarah varies with the sabab. Hence, intention must align with the specific cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا أدَاءُ الْكَفَّارَاتِ لَا يَحْتَاجُ فِيْهِ إِلَى التَّعْييْنِ فِي جِنْسِ وَاحِدٍ، وَلَوْ عَيَّنَ لَغَى. وفي " الأجْنَاسِ لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ كَمَا حَقَّقْنَاهُ فِى الظَّهَارِ مِنْ كِتَابِنَا شَرْحُ الْكَنْزِ» .
ترجمه: اور اس پر کفارات کی ادائیگی ہے کہ اس کی جنس واحد میں تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے تعین کی تو وہ لغو ہو گی اور اجناس میں وہ ضروری ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے اپنی کتاب "شرح الكنز “ کے باب الظهار میں تحقیق بیان کر دیا ہے۔
تشریح جنس واحد میں تعیین نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اسی پرمحمول کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی ہے ایک ہی جنس کے دو کفارے واجب ہوں اور ان دونوں کی طرف سے دو غلام آزاد کر دئیے تو کفار سے ادا ہو جائیں گے اگر غلاموں کے آزاد کرتے وقت دونوں کفاروں کی نیت مبین نہ کی ہو "لمن و جهت عليه كفارة او ظهار فاعتق عبدين لا ينوى من احداهما بعينها جاز عنهما هدايه مطبوعہ كراچی ج ۳ ص (۲۱۴) اور اگر متعدد جنس کے کفارے واجب ہوں مثلاً کفارہ قتل، کفارہ ظہار، کفارہ یمین اور اس نے ایک غلام آزاد کر دیا اور یہ تعیین کی نہیں کہ کونسے کفارہ کی طرف سے غلام آزاد کر رہا ہے تو کفارہ بدون نیست تعیین ادا نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اسباب کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے اجناس مختلف ہیں اور اجناس مختلفہ میں معین نیت ضروری ہے ۔
وان اعتق عن ظهار وقتل لم يجز عن واحد عنهما ولنا ان نية التعيين في الجنس المتحد غير مفيد فتلغو و في الجنس المختلف مفید و اختلاف الجنس في الحكم وهو الكفارة ههنا باختلاف السبب هدايه ج ۳ ص / ۳۶۴)
And upon this, the performance of expiations does not require specification in a single genus, and if one specifies, it is void. And in different genera, it is necessary, as we have verified in the chapter of Zihar in our book Sharh al-Kanz.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage extends the same rule to expiations (kaffarat). If a person owes two expiations of the same genus (e.g., two kaffarat for the same type of violation), and he frees two slaves without specifying which expiation each is for, both expiations are fulfilled. However, if the expiations are of different genera (e.g., kaffarat for qatl, zihar, and yamin), and he frees one slave without specifying which expiation it is for, it does not fulfill any of them because the causes differ, creating different genera. The author references the Hidayah and his own Sharh al-Kanz for further detail. The key principle is that specification of intention is only required when the genera differ; otherwise, the general intention suffices.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory act performed to atone for a sin or violation. Genera are determined by the cause (sabab).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person owes two expiations: one for zihar and one for breaking an oath. He frees two slaves without specifying. Is this valid?
A) Yes, because both are expiations and the genus is the same.
B) No, because the causes are different, making the genera different, and specification is required.
C) Yes, because freeing two slaves covers both automatically.
D) No, because he must free four slaves.

Key Takeaway
In expiations, specification of intention is only required when the causes differ; otherwise, general intention suffices.
