Unity of Genus Dispenses with Specification in Advance Zakat
Furūʿ on zakat: advance payment and loss of nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-ittihad fi al-jins yughni an al-ta'yin' to transfer an advance zakat payment when the intended nisab is lost and a remaining nisab of the same genus exists.

Core Idea
Unity of genus makes specific intention unnecessary; advance zakat automatically transfers to surviving wealth of the same type.

This lesson explores a practical furūʿ case from zakat: what happens when you pay zakat early for one portion of your wealth, and that wealth is destroyed before the year ends? The Hanafi school answers with a powerful qawida that links zakat and other financial obligations. We will see how the principle 'unity of genus dispenses with specification' resolves this scenario.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its meaning
Identify the qawida: 'al-ittihad fi al-jins yughni an al-ta'yin'. Understand that when two items belong to the same genus (e.g., silver dirhams), one does not need to specify which one the payment is for.
The maxim is a sub-maxim (dabt) governing financial obligations.
2
Identify the scenario
A person has two nisabs of the same genus (e.g., 200 dirhams each). He pays zakat in advance for one nisab. Before the year completes, that nisab is lost. Another nisab remains.
The advance payment must have been made with the intention of zakat for a specific nisab.
3
Apply the maxim to the case
Since both nisabs are of the same genus (silver), the advance payment is not tied to the lost nisab. The intention for the lost nisab becomes void, and the payment is transferred to the remaining nisab.
The maxim operates here: unity of genus allows the payment to cover any wealth of that genus.
4
Note the condition of genus unity
If the remaining wealth is of a different genus (e.g., gold instead of silver), the advance payment does not transfer automatically. Intention becomes necessary.
This distinction is critical for correct fatwa. The maxim only applies when the genus is the same.
5
Connect to the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the transfer of the payment to the remaining nisab of the same genus. This is based on the authoritative transmission from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami'.
No significant ikhtilaf exists on this ruling; it is a standard Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا فِي الزَّكوةِ: فَقَالُوا : لَوْ عَجَّلَ خَمْسَةٌ سُوْدٍ عَنْ مَاتَى دِرْهَمٍ سُوْدِ فَهَلَكَتِ السُّوْدُ قَبْلَ الْحَوْلِ، وَعِنْدَهُ نِصَابٌ ،آخَرَ، كَانَ الْمُعَجَّلُ عَنِ الْبَاقِي.
:ترجمہ: اور بہر حال زکوۃ میں تو فقہاء نے فرمایا اگر دو سو درہم کی پانچ درہم زکوۃ پیشگی دیدی پھر سال کے طرف سے ہو جائے گی۔ پورا ہونے سے پہلے دراہم ضائع ہو گئے حالانکہ اس کے پاس دوسرا نصاب بھی ہو تو پیشگی دی گئی زکوۃ اس باقی کی سے پہلے در ہو دوسرا ہوتو دی زکوۃ اس تشریح جنس واحد میں تعیین نیت ضروری نہیں ہے اس پر تفریح پیش کرتے ہیں ایک شخص کے پاس دو نصاب تھے اس نے سال پورا ہونے سے پہلے ایک نصاب کی زکوۃ دیدی پھر سال پورا ہونے سے پہلے ہی وہ نصاب ضائع ہوگیا تو پیشگی ادا کردہ زکو یہ اس دوسرے نصاب کی طرف سے لگ جائے گی اس لئے کہ تمام دراہم جنس واحد کے قبل سے ہیں اور جنس واحد میں تعین فریت بر کار ہے لہذا اس نے بعد میں ہلاک ہونے والے نصاب کی طرف سے جوز کوۃ کی نیت کی تھی وہ نیت باطل ہوگی اور جو نصاب باقی ہے اس کی طرف سے وہ پیشگی زکوۃ کبھی جائے گی۔ قال محمد في الجامع رجل له مانتا درهم وعشرون مثقالا من ذهب عجل زكرة الماتين ثم هلك المائتان قبل تمام الحول وبقى الذهب فان المؤدى يكون زكوة عن الذهب تار تار خانیه ج ۲ ص ۲۶۲)
And as for zakat: they said: if one paid in advance five black (dirhams) for two hundred black dirhams, then the dirhams perished before the year, and he has another nisab, the advance payment goes to the remaining (nisab).
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage applies the same rule to zakat. The example: a person has two nisabs of the same type (e.g., 200 dirhams each). He pays the zakat of one nisab in advance before the year completes. Then that nisab is lost before the year ends. The advance payment is now considered for the remaining nisab because both are of the same genus (silver dirhams). The intention to pay for the lost nisab is void, and the payment is transferred to the other nisab. The author quotes Imam Muhammad from al-Jami' with a similar case involving both dirhams and gold, where the zakat intended for lost dirhams goes to the gold because both are zakatable properties (different genera? Actually gold and silver are different genera, so there is a nuance). But the principle upheld is that in the same genus, specification is not needed; in different genera, it is. Here the dirhams are same genus, so the payment transfers.

Key Terms
تعجيل الزكاة (ta'jil al-zakat): Paying zakat before the completion of the lunar year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person owns two nisabs of silver (200 dirhams each). He pays 5 dirhams in advance for the first nisab. Before the year ends, the first nisab is destroyed. What happens to the advance payment?
A) It is refunded to him.
B) It is considered invalid.
C) It is applied to the second nisab.
D) He must pay again for the first nisab.

Key Takeaway
Advance zakat is valid and, if the intended wealth is lost before the year, it automatically applies to any remaining wealth of the same genus.

Intention in Qada' Fasts and Combined Kaffarah
Applying the intention maxim to qada' and kaffarah fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to cases of combined intentions in qada' fasts and identify when general intention suffices according to the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
General intention of qada' covers multiple missed fasts and even combined kaffarah — the intention to fulfill the obligation is enough.

This lesson examines the practical application of the foundational Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) to the obligation of making up missed fasts. You will see how the school's later authorities resolved an intra-madhhab dispute about whether a person must specify the exact day when making up fasts from different Ramadans, and how this same leniency extends to combining kaffarah and qada' fasts.

Guided Path
1
State the governing qawida
Identify the hadith-based maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and recall its rank as one of the five major qawaid kubra.
This maxim is the lens through which the entire passage is understood.
2
Identify the first furu' case: qada' from same or different Ramadans
Note that the text from Fath al-Qadir discusses two sub-cases: missed fasts from one Ramadan, and from two Ramadans. The ruling is that general intention of qada' suffices without specifying the day.
The 'mukhtar' position here is Fath al-Qadir's view.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
Contrast the view of Sahib Nasb al-Rayah (requiring specification for different Ramadans) with Fath al-Qadir (sufficiency of general intention). Understand the resolution: general intention implies the first missed fast.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to the second furu' case: combined kaffarah and qada'
Consider a person who owes 60 days kaffarah and 1 day qada'. If they fast 61 days with a general intention of both, it is valid without specifying which day is for qada'.
The general intention of qada' is understood to cover the one qada' day.
5
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
Conclude that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that general intention of qada' suffices for multiple missed fasts and when combined with kaffarah, as per Fath al-Qadir.
This ruling is based on the maxim and practical ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واجب في فتح القدير من الصوم: ولو وجب عليه قضاء يومين من رمضان واحد فالأولى أن يسوي أول يوم وجب عليه قضاؤه من هذا الرمضان، وإن لم يعين جاز، وكذا لو كانا من رمضانين على المختار حتى لو نوى القضاء لا غير جاز.

ترجمہ: اور فتح القدیر کے کتاب الصوم میں ہے اگر ایک ہی رمضان کے دو دن کے روزوں کی قضا اس ہو، افضل یہ ہے کہ وہ پہلے دن کی نیت کرے جس کی قضا اس رمضان کی اس پر واجب ہے اور اگر تعیین نہ کی تو جائز ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی اگر دو رمضان کے ہوں مختار مذہب کے مطابق حتی کہ اگر صرف قضا کی نیت کی تو جائز ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ عین کی نیت کرے مثلاً یہ ارادہ کرے کہ فلاں دن کے روزہ کی قضا کرتا ہوں اور اگر تعیین نیت بھی نہ کرے تشریح: فتح القدیر کے کتاب الصوم میں مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی پر ایک ہی رمضان کے دو روزوں کی قضاء ہے تو اس رمضان کے روزے کی قضا کی نیت کر لے تب بھی کافی ہے اور اگر دو رمضان کے دو روزے یا زیادہ قضا ہیں تو مختار کے مطابق اجناس مختلفہ کی وجہ سے تعیین نیت ضروری ہونی چاہئے، صاحب نصب الرایہ اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اگر محض رمضان کے روزوں کی قضا کی نیت کر لی، اس دن کی تعین نہ کی تب بھی استحساناً جائز ہے، صاحب فتح القدیر کا یہی مسلک ہے۔ لیکن اگر آپ غور کریں گے تو صاحب نصب الرایہ اور صاحب فتح القدیر کے قولوں کے مابین منافات نہیں ہے۔ وكذا لو كانا رمضانين على المختار حتى لو نوى القضاء یہ عبارت ماقبل کے اصول سے متعارض ہے کہ دو رمضان کے دو قضا روزے مختلف الاجناس سے ہیں تو ان میں تعیین نیت ضروری ہونی چاہئے جبکہ یہاں یہ کیا گیا ہے کہ اگر صرف قضا کی نیت کر لی اس دن کی بھی تعین نہ کی تب بھی روزوں کی قضا درست ہو جائے گی۔ جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ ماقبل میں صاحب نصب الرایہ کا مسلک بیان کیا گیا ہے اور یہاں صاحب فتح القدیر کے مسلک کو بیان کیا جا رہا ہے کہ مطلق قضا کی نیت پر محمول کر کے یہ سمجھا جائے گا کہ چھوٹے ہوئے روزوں میں سے پہلا وہ رکھ رہا ہے اور اتنی تعین کافی ہے۔

وَلَوْ وَجَبَتْ عَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَةُ فِطْرِ، فَصَامَ إحدى وَسِتِّينَ يَوْماً عَنِ الْقَضَاءِ وَالْكَفَّارَةِ، وَلَمْ يُعَيِّنْ الْقَضَاءِ جَازَ .

ترجمہ: اور اگر اس کے ذمہ روزہ توڑنے کا کفارہ ہو اور اس نے کفارہ و قضا کی نیت سے ساٹھ روزے رکھے اور تھا کہ دن کی تعیین نہ کی تو جائز ہے۔

تشریح: اگر کسی نے رمضان کا روزہ رکھ کر بدون عذر شرعی توڑ دیا تو اس پر ساٹھ روزے کفارہ کے اور ایک روزہ قضا کا واجب ہو گا اب اگر اس نے اکسٹھ روزے رکھے ساتھ کفارہ کے ایک قضا کا لیکن اس نے قضا کے روزے
It is necessary in Fath al-Qadir from the book of fasting: And if he owes making up two days from one Ramadan, then the best is that he intends the first day that he owes making up from this Ramadan, and if he does not specify, it is valid. Similarly, if they are from two Ramadans according to the chosen position, even if he only intends the make-up without more, it is valid. Translation: And in Fath al-Qadir's book of fasting it says: If he has to make up two days from one Ramadan, it is best that he intends the first day that he owes making up from this Ramadan, and if he does not specify, it is valid. And similarly if they are from two Ramadans according to the chosen school, even if he only intends the make-up, it is valid. That is, he intends the exact day, for example, he intends to make up a specific day. And if he does not even specify the intention, explanation: In Fath al-Qadir's book of fasting, the issue is that if someone has to make up two days from one Ramadan, intending the make-up of a day from this Ramadan is sufficient. If he has two or more make-up days from two Ramadans, according to the chosen position, because of different types, specifying the intention is necessary; Sahib Nasb al-Rayah holds this view. If he only intends the make-up of Ramadan days without specifying the day, it is still valid by istihsan; this is the position of Sahib Fath al-Qadir. But if you reflect, there is no contradiction between the views of Sahib Nasb al-Rayah and Sahib Fath al-Qadir. The phrase 'And similarly if they are from two Ramadans according to the chosen position, even if he only intends the make-up' contradicts the earlier principle. Because two make-up days from two Ramadans are of different types, so specifying the intention would be necessary. Here it is stated that if he only intends the make-up without specifying the day, the make-up fasts are still valid. The answer is that earlier the position of Sahib Nasb al-Rayah was mentioned, and here the position of Sahib Fath al-Qadir is being mentioned: the absolute intention of make-up is interpreted to mean that he is making up the first missed fast, and that much specification is sufficient. And if he owes a kaffarah for breaking a fast, and he fasts sixty-one days with the intention of make-up and kaffarah, and does not specify the make-up, it is valid. Translation: And if he owes a kaffarah for breaking a fast, and he fasts sixty days with the intention of kaffarah and make-up, and he did not specify the make-up, it is valid. Explanation: If someone fasted in Ramadan and broke it without a valid excuse, then he owes sixty days of kaffarah and one make-up day. Now if he fasts sixty-one days with the kaffarah and one make-up, but he did not intend the make-up day,
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a furu' (application) of the major qawida 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' (Matters are judged by intentions). It discusses two cases: making up missed Ramadan fasts from one or two Ramadans, and combining kaffarah and qada' fasts. The author first quotes Fath al-Qadir, stating that for make-up days from the same Ramadan, it is best to intend the first day, but if one does not specify, it is still valid. Similarly, for make-up days from different Ramadans, the chosen position is that general intention of qada' suffices. Then a potential contradiction is raised and resolved: Sahib Nasb al-Rayah required specification for different Ramadans, while Sahib Fath al-Qadir allowed general intention. The resolution is that the general intention is interpreted as intending the first missed fast, which provides sufficient specification. The second ruling deals with combining kaffarah and qada' fasts: a person who breaks a fast deliberately must fast sixty days for kaffarah and one day for qada'. If he fasts sixty-one days with a general intention of both, without specifying which day is for qada', it is valid. The intention of qada' is satisfied by the general intention, as it is understood that the first sixty days are kaffarah and the last one is qada', or vice versa. This leniency is based on the maxim that the general intention covers the obligation.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory fast after its time has passed.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast without valid excuse; fasting sixty consecutive days.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specifying the exact day or act when intending an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from Fath al-Qadir, what is the ruling if someone has to make up two missed fasts from the same Ramadan and only intends 'qada'' without specifying the first day?
A) The fasts are invalid because specification is required.
B) The fasts are valid because general intention suffices.
C) Only the first fast is valid, the second is not.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
General intention of qada' suffices for multiple missed fasts and combined kaffarah, based on the maxim that matters are judged by intentions.

Applying Intentions to Advanced Zakat: Ta'jil and Ownership
Applying the maxim of intentions to advanced zakat payments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' to cases of advanced zakat (ta'jil) and determine when the advance is valid or invalid based on ownership and intention.

Core Idea
Zakat advanced for property you don't own is void; intention cannot substitute for ownership.

This lesson explores the application of the great legal maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' (Matters are judged by their intentions) to the practice of advancing zakat (ta'jil al-zakat). Through specific cases from the Fatawa al-Khaniyyah, you will see how the intention to fulfill zakat is conditioned by actual ownership of the nisab. Understanding these rulings is essential for a mufti advising clients on early zakat payments.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its relevance
Recall the qawida 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' which means that the ruling of an action depends on the intention behind it. In zakat, the intention to discharge obligation must align with actual ownership.
The mufti evaluates the payer's intention at the time of ta'jil.
2
Analyze first furu: two nisabs
Work through the case where a person has two separate nisabs (e.g., trade goods and camels) and advances zakat for one, but that property is later proven owned by another. The advanced zakat is invalid and cannot be transferred to the other nisab.
Reason: the intention was directed at a specific property he did not own.
3
Analyze second furu: single nisab, partial istihqaq
If the nisab is a single unit (e.g., 40 mithqals of gold kept together) and part is later found owned by another, the advance is valid for the remaining owned gold, provided it was kept as one unit. If kept separately, each unit is a separate nisab.
Contrast: unity of possession changes the ruling.
4
Analyze third furu: pregnant camels
If a person advances zakat for five pregnant camels and their unborn, and they give birth before year-end, the advance is valid for what was intended. But advancing for future offspring of the next year is invalid.
Ownership of future offspring is not established at the time of advancement.
5
Extract the principle
The common thread is that the validity of ta'jil requires that the property for which zakat is intended be owned by the payer at the time of advancement. Intention alone cannot create obligation where ownership is absent.
This is a direct application of the qawida.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي الْخَانِيَةِ لَوْ عَجَّلَ الزَّكَاةَ عَنْ أَحَدِ الْمَالَيْنِ، فَاسْتَحَقَّ مَا عَجَّلَ عَنْهُ قَبْلَ الْحَوْلِ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْمُعَجَّلُ عَنِ الْبَاقِي، وَكَذَا لَوِ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْدَ الْحَوْلِ؛ لِأَنَّ فِي الِاسْتِحْقَاقِ عَجَّلَ عَمَّا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِلْكُهُ فَبَطَلَ التَّعْجِيلُ، انْتَهَى.

ترجمہ: اور خانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر دو مالوں میں سے ایک کی طرف سے پیشگی زکوۃ دیدی اور سال کے پورا ہونے سے پہلے جس مال کی پیشگی زکوۃ دی مستحق نکل آیا تو پیشگی دی ہوئی زکوۃ باقی کی طرف سے نہ ہوگی اور ایسے ہی اگر حولان حول کے بعد مستحق نکل آیا اس لئے کہ استحقاق کی صورت میں اس مال کی طرف سے پیشگی ادا کر دی جو اس کی ملک نہیں تھا تو تعجیل باطل ہوگئی کلام پورا ہوا۔

تشریح: خانیہ میں مذکور ہے اگر کوئی دو نصابوں کا مالک ہے مثلا کسی کے پاس مال تجارت بھی ہے جو بقدر نصاب ہے اور اس کے پاس بقدر نصاب اونٹ بھی ہیں صاحب مال نے ایک نصاب مثلا اونٹوں کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدی پھر جوان حول سے پہلے یا حولان حول کے بعد کوئی اس نصاب کا مستحق نکل آیا جس کی پیشگی زکوۃ دی ہے تو یہ پیشگی دی ہوئی زکوۃ باطل ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ جس مال کی طرف سے اس نے زکوۃ دی وہ اس کا مالک ہی نہیں تھا۔ اور یہ پیشگی دی ہوئی زکوۃ دوسرے نصاب کی طرف سے نہیں کبھی جائے گی بلکہ دوسرے نصاب کی زکواۃ علیحدہ دینی ہوگی۔ البتہ اگر ایک ہی نصاب ہے مثلاً چالیس مثقال سونا اور کسی نے ہیں مثقال سونے کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدی اور کوئی آدمی میں مثقال سونے کا مستحق نکل آیا تو اس صورت میں پیشگی دی ہوئی زکوۃ باقی میں مشتقال کی طرف سے کبھی جائے گی لیکن یہ بھی اس وقت ہے جب میں مثقال سونا ایک ہی جگہ رکھا ہوا ہو۔ اور اگر ساڑھے سات تولہ سونا ایک جگہ رکھا ہے اور ساڑھے سات تولہ دوسری جگہ رکھا ہے جس ساڑھے سات تولہ سونے کی پیشگی زکوۃ دی اسی کا کوئی مستحق نکل آیا تو یہ پیشگی دی ہوئی زکوۃ اس دوسری جگہ رکھے ہوئے ساڑھے سات تولہ سونے کی طرف سے کافی نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہاں پر اس صورت میں دونوں مالوں کو الگ الگ شمار کیا جائے گا اور جس کی طرف سے زکوۃ پیشگی دی ہے وہ اس کا مالک ہی نہیں تھا اس لئے تعجیل باطل ہو جائے گی۔

وَفِيهَا أَيْضاً لَوْ كَانَ لَهُ خَمْسٌ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ الْحَوَامِلِ يَعْنِي الْحُبَالَى فَعَجَّلَ شَاتَيْنِ عَنْهَا وَعَمَّا فِي بُطُونِهَا، ثُمَّ نَتَجَتْ خَمْساً قَبْلَ الْحَوْلِ أَجْزَاهُ عَمَّا عَجَّلَ، وَإِنْ عَجَّلَ عَمَّا تَحْمِلُ فِي السَّنَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ لَا يَجُوزُ.
And in al-Khaniyyah: If he advances the zakat for one of two properties, and the property for which he advanced is found to belong to another before the year ends, the advanced payment is not counted for the remaining property. Similarly, if it is found to belong to another after the year ends, because in the case of entitlement, he advanced for something that was not his property, so the advancement is invalid. End.

Translation: And in al-Khaniyyah it is: If he gave zakat in advance for one of two properties, and before the completion of the year, the property for which he gave advance zakat turns out to belong to another, then the advanced zakat will not be counted for the remaining property. Similarly, if it turns out after the year ends, because in the case of entitlement, he gave in advance for a property that was not his ownership, so the advancement becomes invalid.

Explanation: In al-Khaniyyah it is mentioned: If someone owns two nisabs, for example, he has trade goods amounting to a nisab and also camels amounting to a nisab, and he gives advance zakat for one nisab (e.g., the camels), and then before the year or after the year, a person appears who is entitled to that nisab (i.e., proves it belongs to him), then this advanced zakat becomes invalid because the property for which he gave zakat was not his. And this advanced zakat will never be counted for the other nisab; rather, the zakat for the other nisab must be paid separately. However, if it is a single nisab, e.g., forty mithqals of gold, and he gave advance zakat for ten mithqals, and then a person appears entitled to ten mithqals, then in that case the advanced zakat will be counted for the remaining thirty mithqals, but only if all the gold is kept in one place. And if seven and a half tolas of gold are kept in one place and another seven and a half tolas in another place, and he gave advance zakat for the seven and a half tolas in one place, and that specific gold is found to belong to another, then this advanced zakat will not be sufficient for the gold in the other place, because in this case the two properties are considered separate, and the property for which he gave advance zakat was not his, so the advancement is invalid.

And in it also: If he has five pregnant camels (meaning they are expecting), and he advances two sheep as zakat covering them and their fetuses, then they give birth to five before the year ends, it suffices for what he advanced. But if he advances for what they will carry in the second year, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a furu' (application) of the qawida 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha'. It discusses the ruling on advancing zakat (ta'jil al-zakat) when the property for which zakat was advanced is later found to be owned by another. The first ruling from al-Khaniyyah states: If a person owns two nisabs (e.g., trade goods and camels) and advances zakat for one of them, but before the year ends (or even after) it is discovered that the property was not owned by him (e.g., it was rightfully someone else's), then the advanced zakat is invalid and cannot be transferred to the other nisab. The reason is that the advance was made for something he did not own. However, if there is a single nisab (e.g., 40 mithqals of gold) and he advances zakat for part of it, and then part of that gold is found to belong to another, the advance is valid for the remaining gold, provided the gold is kept as one unit. If the gold is kept separately, each portion is treated as a separate nisab. The second ruling from the same source deals with advancing zakat for pregnant camels: if a person owns five pregnant camels and advances two sheep as zakat for both the camels and their unborn, and then the camels give birth before the year ends, the advance is valid. But if he advances zakat for what the camels will carry in the second year, it is not valid because future offspring cannot be the basis for zakat advance. These rulings illustrate how intention and ownership affect the validity of ta'jil.

Key Terms
تعجیل (ta'jil): Advancing the payment of zakat before the end of the lunar year.
استحقاق (istihqaq): A claim or entitlement that proves that the property rightfully belongs to another.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khaniyyah, if a person has two nisabs and advances zakat for one, and before the year ends it is discovered that he never owned that property, what is the ruling?
A) The advanced zakat becomes valid for the other nisab.
B) The advanced zakat is invalid, and the other nisab's zakat must be paid separately.
C) The advanced zakat is considered a voluntary sadaqah.
D) The advanced zakat is valid if he intended to pay zakat in general.

Key Takeaway
The validity of advanced zakat depends on the intention directed at owned property; if the property is later found to be owned by another, the advance is void and cannot be reassigned.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
Intention in Faraid, Wajibat, and Nawafil
Applying the rule of intention to various prayers and acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of intention (niyyah) to identify when specification (ta'yin) is required and when absolute intention suffices for various acts of worship.

Core Idea
For many acts, a general intention suffices; specification is only needed when confusion between different obligations arises.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair applies the foundational maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (acts are judged by intentions) to a range of specific worship acts. It clarifies that for faraid and wajibat, absolute intention may suffice when the category is singular, while for nawafil and sunan ratibah, the Hanafi school favors flexibility. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for muftis issuing fatwas on the validity of prayer intentions.

Guided Path
1
State the underlying maxim
Identify the qawida governing intention: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (acts are judged by intentions). What does this imply about the need for specification?
2
Classify the acts
The passage distinguishes faraid/wajibat from nawafil/sunan. For each category, determine whether specification is required or not.
3
Examine the furuat
Work through each example: nadhr, witr, eid, tawaf, janazah, sajdah tilawah, nawafil, sunan ratibah. What intention is sufficient in each case?
4
Identify the istithna
When must specification be required? The passage hints: when multiple different types could be confused. Find the general rule.

Source Text

هذَا كُلَّهُ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ وَالْوَاجِبَاتِ كَالْمَنْدُوْرِ، وَالْوِتْرِ عَلَى قَوْلِ الإِمَامِ وَالْعِيْدِ عَلَى الصَّحِيح ، وَرَكْعَتَي الطَّوَافِ عَلَى الْمُخْتَارِ وَيَنْوِى الْوِتْرَ لَا الْوِتْرِ الْوَاجِبَ لِلإِخْتِلَافِ فيهِ، وَفِي صَلَاةِ الْجَنَازَةِ يَنْوِي الصَّلَاةَ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَالدُّعَاءَ لِلْمَيِّتِ، وَلَا يَلْزَمُهُ التَّعْيْنُ فِي السجودِ التَّلَاوَةِ لأى تِلَاوَةِ سَجَدَ لَهَا، كَمَا فِي الْقِنْيَةِ».
:ترجمه به یوری تفصیل فرائض اور واجبات کے بارے میں ہے جیسے منذ ور اور وتر امام صاحب کے قول پر در میون اور پسندیدہ قول کے مطابق اور طواف کی دورکعتیں مختار قول کے مطابق اور وتر کی نیت کرے نہ کہ واجب وتر میں اختلاف کی وجہ سے اور نمازہ جنازہ میں اللہ کے لئے نماز کی نیت کرے اور میت کے لئے دعا کی اور تلاوت
سے کہوں میں تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے کہ کس تلاوت کا سجدہ کر رہا ہے جیسا کہ قضیہ میں ہے۔ تشریح : ماقبل کی تفصیل سے آپ کو یہ بات معلوم ہو چکی کہ جنس واحد میں تعیین نیت کی ضرورت نہیں البتہ مختلف وں کی تمیز کے لئے نیت کی تعیین ضروری ہے لیکن عبادت میں تعیین وعدم تعیین نیت کے بارے میں جو تفصیل گزری وہ خراش اور واجبات کے بارے میں ہے جیسے کسی نے نذر مانی کہ اگر میرا افلاں کام ہو گیا تو میں دو روزہ رکھوں اور وہ کام کی تو روزہ ایک ہی جنس ہے اس لئے کہ روزہ کا سبب ایک ہی ہے اگر چہ اس کے افراد الگ الگ ہیں لہذا یہاں پر تعیین
کیاں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
پھر اس کے بعد مصنف نے فرمایا: «وَأَمَّا النَّوَافِلُ : فَاتَّفَقَ أَصْحَابُنَا أَنَّهَا تَصِحُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ وَأَمَّا السُّنَنُ الرَّوَاتِبُ فَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي اشْتِرَاطِ تَعْيِيْنِهَا وَالصَّحِيحُ الْمُعْتَمَدُ عَدَمُ الْاشْتِرَاطِ، وَأَنَّهَا تَصِحُ بِنِيَّةِ النَّفْلِ، وبمطلق النية.
ترجمه : اور بہر حال نوافل تو ہمارے اصحاب اس پر متفق ہیں کہ وہ مطلق نیت سے درست ہو جاتے ہیں اور بہر حال سنن مؤکدہ تو ان کی تعیین کے شرط ہونے میں فقہاء کا اختلاف ہے اور صحیح و معتمد شرط نہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ کہ دوش
کی نیت اور مطلق سے درست ہو جاتی ہیں۔
All this is concerning the obligatory and wajib acts, such as the vowed (nadhr), and witr according to Imam's opinion, and the Eid prayer according to the sahih, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf according to the mukhtar. And one intends witr, not 'wajib witr' due to the difference of opinion. And in the funeral prayer, one intends prayer for Allah and supplication for the deceased. And specification (ta'yin) is not necessary in the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) for which recitation he prostrates, as in al-Qunyah. Translation: The above detail concerns faraid and wajibat, such as nadhr, and witr according to Imam's opinion, and Eid according to the preferred view, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf according to the chosen view. And one intends witr, not wajib witr due to difference. In funeral prayer, one intends prayer for Allah and supplication for the deceased. In sajdah tilawah, specification is not required for which recitation he prostrates, as in al-Qunyah. Explanation: From the previous detail you have come to know that in a single category (jins wahid), specification of intention is not needed; however, for distinguishing between different types, specification is necessary. But the detail that passed about specification and non-specification in worship concerns faraid and wajibat. For example, if someone vowed: if my such work is done, I will fast for two days, and the work is done, then fasting is a single category, because the cause of fasting is one even if its individuals are separate. Therefore, specification is not needed here. Then the author said: 'As for supererogatory (nawafil): our companions (as-habuna) are unanimous that they are valid with absolute intention. As for the established sunnahs (sunan ratibah): they differed about the requirement of specification; and the correct and relied-upon view is that it is not required, and that they are valid with the intention of nafl and with absolute intention.'
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a commentary applying the general rule of intention (niyyah) to various specific acts of worship. It begins by stating that the preceding discussion about specification of intention applies to faraid (obligatory) and wajibat (necessary) acts. Examples include: nadhr (vowed acts), witr prayer (according to Imam Abu Hanifa's view that it is wajib), Eid prayer (according to the sahih view that it is wajib), and the two rak'ahs of tawaf (according to the chosen view). For witr, one should intend simply 'witr' and not 'wajib witr' because there is ikhtilaf among scholars about its status. For the funeral prayer, one intends the prayer for Allah and supplication for the deceased; no further specification is needed. In sajdah tilawah, one does not need to specify which verse of prostration is intended. Then the passage transitions to nawafil (supererogatory acts) and sunan ratibah (regular sunnah prayers). For nawafil, there is consensus among Hanafi scholars that they are valid with absolute intention (i.e., simply intending to pray nafl). For sunan ratibah, there is ikhtilaf: some Hanafis required specifying which sunnah, but the sound and relied-upon opinion is that specification is not required; they are valid with the intention of nafl or with absolute intention. This passage illustrates the principle that the need for specific intention (ta'yin) depends on the category of the act and the presence of ambiguity. When the act is of a single type (e.g., fasting in a vow), general intention suffices; when multiple types could be confused, specification is needed. However, for nawafil and sunan, the default is permissibility with absolute intention.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship; required for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, how should one intend the witr prayer?
A) Intend 'wajib witr'.
B) Intend 'sunnah witr'.
C) Intend 'witr' without specifying wajib or sunnah.
D) Intend 'nafl'.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intention is generally flexible; specification is only required when confusion between different obligations arises.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Absolute Intention for Nafl and Sunan Rawatib
States the qawida with furuat derived from it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida that sunan rawatib are valid with absolute intention to new furuat and identify the exceptions when timing is split.

Core Idea
Absolute intention suffices for sunan rawatib and nafl, but precaution recommends specification.

This lesson introduces a key qawida from the Hanafi school: that sunan rawatib (regular sunnah prayers) are valid with absolute intention, just like nafl prayers. While the school is unanimous on nafl, there was an internal debate about sunan rawatib. The relied-upon view is that no specification is required, though caution suggests specifying to avoid disagreement. This principle affects how muftis advise on daily prayers and resolves common doubts.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Identify the exact Arabic and English formulation of the qawida: 'السُّنَنُ الرَّوَاتِبُ تَصِحُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ وَبِنِيَّةِ النَّفْلِ' (The regular sunnah prayers are valid with absolute intention and with the intention of nafl).
The maxim covers both nafl and sunan rawatib.
2
Identify its scope
Determine which fiqh chapters this maxim governs. It applies to all supererogatory prayers, especially sunan rawatib and nafl, and is restricted by the condition that sunan must be started in their proper time.
Scope is limited by timing requirements for sunan rawatib.
3
Work through the furuat
Analyze the two derived cases from the text. First, if someone prays two rak'ahs as tahajjud but they fall after dawn, they count as the sunnah of Fajr. Second, if one rak'ah is before dawn and one after, they do not count as sunnah because the sunnah must be initiated in its time.
Both cases assume absolute intention (non-specification).
4
Identify the istithna
The qawida has an exception: if the prayer is split across the time boundary (one rak'ah before dawn, one after), it does not satisfy the requirement of starting the sunnah in its proper time. Therefore, the ruling changes, and the prayer remains nafl.
The exception is based on the principle that sunan must be started in their time.
5
Note related qawaid
Relate this qawida to 'Al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (acts are judged by intentions) which complements it, and 'Al-yaqin la yazul bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt) which parallels the assumption about intention despite mistaken timing.
These related maxims reinforce the underlying usul.

Source Text

وَأَمَّا النَّوَافِلُ : فَاتَّفَقَ أَصْحَابُنَا أَنَّهَا تَصِحُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ وَأَمَّا السُّنَنُ الرَّوَاتِبُ فَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي اشْتِرَاطِ تَعْيِيْنِهَا وَالصَّحِيحُ الْمُعْتَمَدُ عَدَمُ الْاشْتِرَاطِ، وَأَنَّهَا تَصِحُ بِنِيَّةِ النَّفْلِ، وبمطلق النية. ترجمه : اور بہر حال نوافل تو ہمارے اصحاب اس پر متفق ہیں کہ وہ مطلق نیت سے درست ہو جاتے ہیں اور بہر حال سنن مؤکدہ تو ان کی تعیین کے شرط ہونے میں فقہاء کا اختلاف ہے اور صحیح و معتمد شرط نہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ کہ دوش کی نیت اور مطلق سے درست ہو جاتی ہیں۔ تشريح: ہمارے اصحاب فرماتے ہیں کہ نفل نماز میں وقت وغیرہ کی تعین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ نفل نمازوں میں صرف یہ نیت کافی ہے کہ میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں ۔ سین موکدہ بھی مطلق نماز کی نیت سے اگر چہ صیح ہو جاتی ہیں اور یہی معتمد علیہ قول ہے لیکن احتیاطا تعیین کر لینی چاہنے مثلا میں ظہر کی سنت ، یا عشاء کی سنت پڑھ رہا ہوں، تا کہ اختلاف علماء سے بیچا جا سکے۔ نیز سنن مؤکدہ نفل کی اور مطلق نیت سے بھی ادا ہو جاتی ہیں کیونکہ سنن پر فل کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے۔ وفـي ســائـر السـنـن يكفيه مطلق التبة و به اخذ عامة المشائخ وفى الانفع هو الصحيح ( تارتارخانين) ص: ۳۲۸) وَتَفَرَّعَ عَلَيْهِ لَوْ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ عَلى ظَنّ أنَّهَا تَهَجُدْ بِظَنِّ بَقَاءِ اللَّيْلِ، فَتَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهَا بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجَرِ كَانَتْ عَنْ سُنَّةِ الْفَجَرِ عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ فَلَا يُصَلِّيْهَا بَعْدَهُ لِلْكَرَاهَةِ. وَأَمَّا مَنْ قَالَ: إِذَا صَلَّى رَكْعَةً قَبْلَ الطُلُوعِ، وَأخْرى بَعْدَهُ كَانَتَا عَنِ السُّنَّةِ فَبَعِيْدٌ، لَإِنَّ السُّنَّةَ لَا بُدَّ من الشروع فِيهَا فِي الْوَقْتِ وَلَمْ يُوْجَدْ. ترجمه : اور اسی پر تفریح ہے کہ اگر دورکعت نماز پڑھی اس خیال سے کہ وہ تہجد ہے اس گمان سے کہ رات باقی پس ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ طلوع فجر کے بعد ہو ئیں تو صحیح قول کے ہمو جب وہ سنت فجر کی طرف سے ہوگی پس اس کے بعدان کو نہ پڑھے کراہت کی وجہ سے اور بہر حال جس نے کہا جب ایک رکعت پڑھی طلوع سے پہلے اور دوسری رکعت اس کے بعد تو وہ دونوں سنت کی طرف سے ہوئی تو یہ بعید ہے اس لئے کہ سنت کو وقت میں شروع کرنا ضروری ہے اور ولنگ یا یا گیا۔ تشریح : اوپر کی تفصیل سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ نوافل مطلق نبیت سے ادا ہو جاتے ہیں تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے، ا کہ یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے کہ اگر کسی نے یہ گمان کر کے کہ رات باقی ہے تہجد کی نماز پڑھی پھر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ وہ دو رکت طلوع فجر کے بعد پڑھی گئیں ہیں تو اس صورت میں یہ دور کعتیں متعین نہ ضروری ہے اور یہاں نہیں ہے لہذا جو اس کے قائل ہیں کہ کافی ہو جائیں گی تو ان کی یہ بات غلط ہے۔
As for nafl prayers, our companions (Ashab) are agreed that they are valid with absolute intention. As for the rawatib sunan (regular sunnah prayers), they differed about the condition of specifying them; and the correct and relied-upon view is that there is no condition, and that they are valid with the intention of nafl and with absolute intention. Translation: And as for nafl, our companions agree that they are valid with absolute intention, and as for the mu'akkadah sunnah, the fuqaha differed on the condition of specifying them, and the correct and relied-upon view is that it is not a condition, and that they are valid with the intention of nafl and with absolute intention. Commentary: Our companions say that in nafl prayer, specification of time etc. is not required; rather, in nafl prayers, only this intention suffices: 'I am praying.' Mu'akkadah sunnah are also valid with absolute intention of prayer, and this is the relied-upon view, but out of caution one should specify, e.g., 'I am praying the sunnah of Zuhr or the sunnah of Isha', to avoid the scholars' disagreement. Also, mu'akkadah sunnah are performed with nafl and absolute intention because the term nafl applies to sunnah. And in all sunan, absolute intention suffices, and the majority of mashayikh adopted this, and the more beneficial is that it is sahih (Tatarkhaniyya p. 328). And a derivative from this: if one prayed two rak'ahs thinking they were tahajjud with the assumption that night remained, then it became clear that they were after dawn, then on the correct view they would count as the sunnah of Fajr, so he should not pray them after because of karahah. And as for whoever said: if he prayed one rak'ah before dawn and another after, they would count as sunnah, that is far-fetched, because the sunnah must be started in its time, and that was not found. Translation: And a derivative from this: if one prayed two rak'ahs thinking they were tahajjud with the assumption that night remained, then it became clear that they were after dawn, then on the correct view they would count as the sunnah of Fajr, so he should not pray them after because of karahah. And as for whoever said: when he prayed one rak'ah before dawn and another after, both would count as sunnah, this is far-fetched, because the sunnah must be started in its time, and that was not found. Commentary: From the above detail, it became clear that nafl are performed with absolute intention; specification is not required. Also, this issue is derived: if someone thought that night remained and prayed tahajjud, then later found that the two rak'ahs were after dawn, then these two rak'ahs, due to not being specified, would stand in place of the sunnah of Fajr. He should not pray sunnah of Fajr after that because it is already performed, and if he prays more under the name of sunnah of Fajr, they would be nafl, and nafl at that time is makruh. But if a person prayed tahajjud as one rak'ah before dawn and one after, then these two rak'ahs will not stand in place of sunnah of Fajr, because starting the sunnah in its time is necessary, and here it was not found; therefore those who say it would suffice are wrong.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a qawida (legal maxim) with its derived applications (furuat). The maxim states: both nafl and the regular sunnah prayers (sunan rawatib) are valid with an absolute intention, i.e., merely intending to pray without specifying the exact prayer. While the Hanafi school is unanimous on nafl, there was an internal disagreement about sunan rawatib. The relied-upon view (al-sahih al-mu'tamad) is that specification is not required; they are valid with the intention of nafl. However, as a matter of precaution (ihtiyat), the text advises specifying, e.g., 'sunnah of Zuhr', to avoid the difference of opinion. The first furu' (derived case) involves someone praying two rak'ahs thinking they are tahajjud (night prayer), but after dawn it becomes clear that they were prayed after Fajr time. According to the maxim, since no specification was made, these two rak'ahs are counted as the sunnah of Fajr (Fajr sunnah), and it is makruh to repeat the sunnah of Fajr. The second furu' considers a scenario where one rak'ah was prayed before dawn and one after; since the prayer was started in two different times, it cannot count as the sunnah of Fajr because the sunnah must be initiated within its prescribed time. Thus, the first rak'ah counts as nafl (since before dawn, no sunnah of Fajr is due) and the second as nafl as well (since sunnah of Fajr must be started before dawn). This illustrates the qawida's scope: absolute intention works, but the timing of commencement is crucial for sunan rawatib.

Key Terms
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): Absolute intention, i.e., merely intending to pray without specifying the prayer type (e.g., not specifying 'sunnah of Zuhr' or 'nafl').
سنن رواتب (sunan rawatib): The regular sunnah prayers that are associated with the five daily fard prayers (e.g., sunnah before and after Zuhr, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what intention is sufficient for performing the sunnah of Fajr?
A) One must intend specifically 'sunnah of Fajr'
B) Absolute intention to pray any sunnah is sufficient
C) One must intend 'fard'
D) One must intend 'nafl' specifically

Key Takeaway
Absolute intention suffices for sunan rawatib and nafl, though specification is recommended for caution.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Absolute Intention Sufficing for Nafl Prayers and Its Applications
Qawida with furuat and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qa'idah that absolute intention suffices for nafl prayers to scenarios such as mistaken tahajjud or fifth rak'ah, and identify when an independent takbir tahrimah is required.

Core Idea
Absolute intention suffices for all sunan and nawafil, except when no separate takbir tahrimah is initiated.

In Hanafi fiqh, the intention (niyyah) for prayer does not always require specifying the exact prayer. For supererogatory prayers (nafl and sunan mu'akkadah), a mere intention to pray 'salah' is sufficient, as established by a number of mashayikh. This lesson explores the scope of this qa'idah through its furu'at and a notable intra-madhhab dispute regarding Tarawih prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the qa'idah
Identify the exact wording of the maxim: 'وفي سائر السنن يكفيه مطلق النية' – absolute intention suffices in all sunan prayers.
The term 'sunan' here includes mu'akkadah and ghayr mu'akkadah, as well as all nawafil.
2
Understand the first branch: mistaken tahajjud
Apply the qa'idah to the case where someone prays two rak'ahs thinking it is tahajjud but it turns out to be after Fajr. The absolute intention makes them count as the sunnah of Fajr.
The ruling is that they replace the sunnah, so one should not repeat the sunnah afterwards due to karahah.
3
Analyze the exception: fifth rak'ah in Zuhr
Contrast with the case where a person mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah in Zuhr and adds a sixth. The two rak'ahs become nafl, not sunnah of Zuhr, because the sunnah requires its own takbir tahrimah which was absent.
This does not contradict the qa'idah; it is an istithna' (exception) when no independent takbir is initiated.
4
Examine the Tarawih ikhtilaf
Qadi Khan required specification (ta'yīn) for Tarawih, but the relied-upon position is that absolute intention suffices, as with other sunan.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that those requiring ta'yīn must explicitly intend Tarawih; otherwise their prayer may not count as Tarawih.
5
Apply the qa'idah and its exception
Practice applying the maxim to new cases: e.g., someone prays two rak'ahs with absolute intention after entering the mosque – this suffices for the tahiyyat al-masjid? (Yes, because it is nafl.)
Always check if a separate takbir tahrimah was intended for the sunnah.

جائے اور پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ کرنے کے بعد اسے غلطی کا احساس ہوا تو اب وہ ایک رکعت اور شامل کر لے اور سجدہ سہو کر کے نماز پوری کر لے اس صورت میں چار رکعت فرض اور دورکعت نفل ہو جائے گی لیکن یہ دورکعت نفل سنت ظہر کی طرف سے شمارنہ ہوں گی حالانکہ او پر یہ اصول گزر چکا ہے کہ سنن رواتب نفل کی نیت سے اور مطلق نیت سے ادا ہو جاتی ہیں تو پھر یہاں و و دو رکعت نفل سخت ظہیر کی طرف سے کافی کیوں نہ ہوں گی۔ جواب: اس کا یہ ہے کہ منتیں مطلق نیت سے یا نفل کی نیت سے اس وقت درست ہوتی ہیں جب سنتوں کے لئے تکبیر تحریمہ منتقل پائی جائے جبکہ اس صورت میں مستقلا تکبیر تحریمہ نہیں پائی گئی۔ مسئلہ اگر ظہر کی چوتھی رکعت میں قعدہ کئے بغیر بھول کر پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا اور پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ کرنے کے بعد احساس ہوا تو ایک رکعت اور ملا کر چھ پوری کرلے اور سجدہ سہو کر کے نماز پوری کر لے اس صورت میں چود کی چھور کعات نفل شمار ہوں گی قعدہ اخیرہ کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اول کی چار فرض نہ ہوں گی جیسا کہ کتب فقہ میں مصرح ہے۔ واختلف التصحيح في التراويح : چونکه من مؤکدہ مطلق نیت سے ادا ہو جاتی ہیں اسی لئے اکثر فقہاء کے نزدیک تراریخ بھی چونکہ سنن مؤکدہ میں سے ہیں اس لئے وہ بھی مطلق نیست سے ادا ہو جائیں گی جبکہ بعض فقہاء تعین کو ضروری قرار دیتے ہیں ان ہی میں سے قاضی خان ہیں جنہوں نے تراویح کے لئے تعین کو ضروری قرار دیا ہے۔
Our associates say that in nafl prayer, specification of time etc. is not needed; rather in nafl prayers, only this intention suffices: 'I am praying'. The emphasized sunan also become valid with the intention of absolute prayer, and this is the relied-upon statement. But as a precaution, one should specify, e.g., 'I am praying the sunnah of Zuhr or the sunnah of Isha', so that the disagreement of scholars can be avoided. Also, the emphasized sunan are performed with the intention of nafl and with absolute intention, because the term nafl applies to sunan. And in the rest of the sunan, absolute intention suffices, and with it the generality of the mashayikh have taken, and in al-Inaayah it is said to be correct (Tataarkhaaniyah p. 328). And derived from it: if one prayed two rak'ahs thinking they are tahajjud, assuming the night remains, then it becomes clear that they were after Fajr, then according to the correct view they are for the sunnah of Fajr, so he should not pray them afterwards due to karahah. As for one who said: 'If he prayed one rak'ah before dawn and another after it, they are for the sunnah,' this is far-fetched, because the sunnah must be started in its time, and that was not found. Translation: And on this is derived: if one prayed two rak'ahs thinking they are tahajjud, assuming the night remains, then it becomes clear that they were after Fajr, then according to the correct view they serve as the sunnah of Fajr, so he should not pray them afterwards due to karahah. Nevertheless, whoever said: 'If he prayed one rak'ah before dawn and another after it, they are for the sunnah,' this is far-fetched, because starting the sunnah in its time is necessary, and it was not found. Explanation: From the above detail it became clear that nawafil are performed with absolute intention; specification is not necessary. This issue is derived: if someone prayed tahajjud thinking the night remains, then later it became clear that the two rak'ahs were prayed after Fajr, then in that case the two rak'ahs, due to not being specified, stand in place of the sunnah of Fajr; afterwards he should not pray the sunnah of Fajr because the sunnah of Fajr has been performed, and if after that he prays more under the name of sunnah of Fajr, they will be nafl, and nafl at that time is makruh. But if a person prayed two rak'ahs of tahajjud such that one rak'ah was before true dawn and one after, then these two rak'ahs will not stand in place of the sunnah of Fajr, because starting the sunnah in its time is necessary and it is not present here; so those who say they would suffice are wrong. And the jurists say: if in Zuhr one mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah after the final sitting, then he should add a sixth, and the two rak'ahs become nafl, and according to the correct view they are not from the sunnah of Zuhr. And this does not indicate the requirement of specification, because the lack of sufficiency is due to the fact that the sunnah is not prescribed except with an independent takbir tahrimah, and that was not found. And the verification differs regarding tarawih: do tarawih occur with absolute intention, or is specification necessary? Qadi Khan corrected the requirement (of specification), and the relied-upon is contrary to that, like the regular sunan. Explanation: If a person mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah in Zuhr after the final sitting and after prostrating in the fifth realizes the mistake, then he should add one more rak'ah and perform sajda sahw and complete the prayer. In this case, four rak'ahs are fard and two rak'ahs are nafl, but these two nafl rak'ahs will not count as the sunnah of Zuhr. Although the principle has passed that the regular sunan are performed with nafl intention and absolute intention, then why are these two nafl rak'ahs not sufficient for the sunnah of Zuhr? The answer: Intentions with absolute or nafl intention are valid only when a separate takbir tahrimah for the sunan is found, while in this case an independent takbir tahrimah was not found. Issue: If one mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah without sitting in the fourth, and after prostrating in the fifth realizes, then he adds one and completes six, and performs sajda sahw. In this case, all six rak'ahs count as nafl because the final sitting was missed, and the first four are not fard, as is clarified in the fiqh books. And the verification differs regarding tarawih: Because the mu'akkadah sunan are performed with absolute intention, for this reason according to most jurists, tarawih also, since they are among the emphasized sunan, are also performed with absolute intention, while some jurists consider specification necessary; among them is Qadi Khan who deemed specification necessary for tarawih.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents a key qa'idah (maxim) in Hanafi fiqh: that for nafl (supererogatory) prayers, including the mu'akkadah sunan (emphasized sunnah prayers), absolute intention (niyyah mutlaqah) without specifying the particular prayer suffices. The author first states the rule, noting that the relied-upon position is that absolute intention is sufficient, but recommends specifying as a precaution to avoid scholarly disagreement. Then he derives three branches (furu'at): (1) If one prays two rak'ahs thinking they are tahajjud but they turn out to be after Fajr, they count as the sunnah of Fajr, so one should not repeat them. (2) If one mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah in Zuhr after the final sitting, the added two rak'ahs become nafl, not sunnah, because the sunnah requires an independent takbir tahrimah. (3) Regarding Tarawih, there is an ikhtilaf: Qadi Khan requires specification, but the relied-upon view is that absolute intention suffices, like other sunan. The commentary explains the reasoning behind each branch, especially why the fifth-rak'ah case does not contradict the general rule, as the takbir tahrimah was not initiated for the sunnah.

Key Terms
نية مطلقة (niyyah mutlaqah): An intention to pray without specifying the particular prayer or its time.
تعيين (ta'yīn): Specifying the exact prayer (e.g., Zuhr sunnah, Tarawih) in the intention.
سنت مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized supererogatory prayers that the Prophet regularly performed.
تحريمة مبتدأة (tahrimah mubtada'ah): An independent takbir tahrimah (opening takbir) that initiates a separate prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person prays two rak'ahs with the intention 'I am praying salah' after the time for Zuhr has ended. Can this count as the sunnah of Zuhr?
A) Yes, because absolute intention suffices.
B) No, because the sunnah must be prayed in its time.
C) Yes, because the sunnah can be made up later.
D) No, because specification is required for sunnah prayers.

Key Takeaway
The qa'idah that absolute intention suffices for all sunan and nawafil is widely relied upon, with the notable exception that a separate takbir tahrimah is required for the prayer to count as sunnah.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Sunnah Requires Its Own Takbir: The Qawida and Its Applications
Ruling on extra rak'ahs and the principle of separate takbir for sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida 'السنة لا تشرع إلا بتحريمة مبتدأة' and apply it to cases of forgetfulness in prayer and the tarawih intention dispute.

Core Idea
Sunnah prayer must begin with its own takbir; otherwise extra rak'ahs become nafl.

This passage from a later Hanafi work addresses a practical scenario: someone forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah during Zuhr prayer. The jurists rule that the extra two rak'ahs are nafl, not sunnah. The reason reveals a key qawida: the sunnah is only legislated with an initiating takbir separate from the fard. The passage then extends this principle to a dispute about tarawih prayer, showing how the same qawida functions across different chapters. Understanding this qawida helps a mufti correctly determine when a missed sunnah can be compensated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forgetfulness scenario and its ruling
Read the passage and extract the exact scenario: someone after final sitting in Zuhr forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah. The ruling is to add a sixth rak'ah. The two extra rak'ahs become nafl, not sunnah. Note that the ruling is based on the principle, not on intention.
The Urdu commentary clarifies that this is after the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah).
2
Derive the underlying qawida
The passage explicitly states: 'because the sunnah is only legislated with an initiating takbir (tahrimah)'. This is the qawida: السُّنَّةُ لَا تُشْرَعُ إِلَّا بِتَحْرِيمَةٍ مُبْتَدَأَةٍ. Understand that this is a sughra (minor) qawida, a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim).
This qawida governs all sunan prayers, especially rawatib and tarawih.
3
Apply the qawida to the tarawih intention dispute
The passage records an ikhtilaf on whether tarawih requires specified intention (ta'yin) or suffices with absolute intention. Qadi Khan held ta'yin is required; the mu'tamad (relied-upon) view is that absolute intention suffices. Why? Because the qawida about tahrimah is the decisive factor – tarawih is like other sunan rawatib; it requires its own tahrimah but not necessarily a specific verbal intention.
The dispute is not about the tahrimah requirement but about intention. The qawida clarifies that the tahrimah condition is distinct from intention.
4
Recognize the operative position in fatwa
The passage concludes that the mu'tamad view is that tarawih does not require ta'yin. In fatwa, a person performing tarawih may intend 'sunnah prayer' or even 'nafl' and it is valid, as long as they have a separate tahrimah. This illustrates how the qawida is the foundation.
This does not contradict the earlier ruling: the extra rak'ahs in the forgetfulness case lacked a separate tahrimah, so they could not be sunnah.

They said: If someone forgetfully stands for a fifth [rak'ah] in Zuhr after the final sitting, then he adds a sixth and the two rak'ahs become nafl, and they do not count for the sunnah of Zuhr according to the correct view. This does not indicate the condition of specification (ta'yin), because the lack of sufficiency is due to the fact that the sunnah is only legislated with an initiating takbir (tahrimah), and that was not present. The correct position regarding tarawih differs: do tarawih occur with absolute intention, or must there be specification? Qadi Khan authenticated the condition [of specification], but the relied-upon view is the opposite, like the regular sunan (sunan rawatib). Translation: The jurists say... Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and its underlying principle from Hanafi fiqh. It addresses a scenario where a person forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah in Zuhr after the final sitting. The ruling is to add a sixth rak'ah, making the extra two rak'ahs nafl. Critically, these two rak'ahs do not count as the sunnah of Zuhr, even though sunan rawatib can normally be performed with an absolute intention. The reason is that the sunnah requires a separate initiating takbir (tahrimah) independent from the fard prayer. Since the extra rak'ahs were performed with the same takbir as the fard, they cannot replace the sunnah. The passage then notes a dispute regarding tarawih prayers: whether they require a specific intention (ta'yin) or suffice with absolute intention. Qadi Khan held that specification is necessary, but the relied-upon (mu'tamad) view is that it is not required, similar to other sunan rawatib. This reflects the Hanafi principle that sunan are valid with absolute intention, but only when performed with their own initiating takbir.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and makes prohibited what was permissible.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specific intention in the heart, e.g., intending a particular prayer like Zuhr or tarawih.
سنن رواتب (sunan rawatib): The confirmed sunnah prayers associated with the five daily obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where someone forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah in Zuhr prayer after the final sitting, what is the ruling on the two extra rak'ahs?
A) They count as the sunnah of Zuhr.
B) They become nafl and do not count as sunnah.
C) They invalidate the entire prayer.
D) They are considered as part of the fard prayer.

Key Takeaway
A sunnah prayer must be initiated with its own takbir; without it, the prayer becomes nafl rather than sunnah.

Branch Issue: Specification for Sunan and the Principle of Essence vs. Description
Derived case from the principle of ta'yin for sunan rawatib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'if the description becomes void, the essence does not void' to cases of intention change in salah and siyam.

Core Idea
A prayer's essence survives a change in its legal description (fard/sunnah/nafl) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

This passage presents a derived case (furu') that tests whether specific intention (ta'yin) is required for regular sunan. It examines the scenario where someone prays four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah intending to make up a missed Zuhr, but later Jumu'ah is confirmed valid. The ruling depends on a deeper principle: does the invalidity of the prayer's description nullify its essence? The majority Hanafi view says no, allowing the prayer to count as sunnah. This lesson unpacks the qawida and its application to both salah and siyam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the branch scenario
The text describes a person praying four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah in a place where Jumu'ah's validity is doubted. He intends to make up a missed Zuhr (either the last Zuhr owed or the first Zuhr of the day that he missed). Later, Jumu'ah is confirmed valid.
The doubt about Jumu'ah's validity is the trigger for the entire scenario.
2
State the disputed ruling
The question: can these four rak'ahs count as the sunnah of Jumu'ah? According to the relied-upon view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), yes, provided the person did not actually owe a missed Zuhr. According to Imam Muhammad, they cannot.
The phrase 'المعتمد' indicates the operative fatwa.
3
Uncover the underlying qawida
The ruling branches from the principle: 'If the description of a prayer becomes void, its essence does not become void' (إذا بطل وصف الصلاة لا يبطل أصلها). This principle is attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This is a sughra qawida (minor maxim) used to resolve cases of intention mismatch.
4
Apply the qawida to the scenario
The prayer's essence (the four rak'ahs) remains valid even though its intended description (make-up Zuhr) became void when Jumu'ah was validated. Therefore, the prayer can be reassigned as sunnah of Jumu'ah.
The condition 'if no missed Zuhr was owed' ensures no actual fard was neglected.
5
Extend the logic to supererogatory fasts
The author analogizes supererogatory fasts (sunan siyam) to supererogatory prayers, concluding that specification (ta'yin) is not required for recommended fasts either.
This is a qiyas (analogical deduction) from salah to siyam.

وَتَفَرَّعَ أَيْضاً عَلَى إِشْتِرَاطِ التَّعْيِينِ لِلسُّنَنِ الرَّوَاتِبِ، وَعَدَمِهِ مَسْأَلَةٌ أُخْرَى هِيَ لَوْ صَلَّى بَعْدَ الْجُمُعَةِ أَرْبَعاً فِي مَوْضِعٍ يَشْكُّ فِي صِحَّةِ الْجُمُعَةِ، نَاوِياً آخِرَ ظُهْرٍ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ أَوَّلَ مَا أَدْرَكَ وَقْتُهُ وَلَمْ يُؤَدِّهِ. ثُمَّ تَبَيَّنَ صِحَّةُ الْجُمُعَةِ فَعَلَى الصَّحِيحِ الْمُعْتَمَدِ تَنُوبُ عَنْ سُنَّةِ الْجُمُعَةِ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِ ظُهْرٌ فَائِتٌ، وَعَلَى الْقَوْلِ الْآخَرِ: لَا ، كَمَا فِي فَتْح الْقَدِيرِ: وَهُوَ أَيْضاً يَتَفَرَّعُ عَلَى أَنَّ الصَّلَاةَ إِذَا بَطَلَ وَصْفُهَا لَا يَبْطُلُ أَصْلُهَا عَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ، خِلَافَاً لِمُحَمَّدٍ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُقَالَ فِيْهَا: إِنَّهَا تَكُونُ عَنِ السُّنَّةِ إِلَّا عَلَى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ. وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُلْحَقَ الصِّيَامَاتُ الْمَسْنُوْنَةُ بِالصَّلَوَاتِ الْمَسْنُوْنَةِ، فَلَا يُشْتَرَطُ لَهَا التَّعْيِينُ، وَلَمْ أَرَ مَنْ نَبَّهَ عَلَيْهِ.
ترجمہ: اور سنن مؤکدہ کی تعین کے شرط ہونے اور نہ ہونے پر ایک دوسرا مسئلہ بھی متفرع ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر جمعہ کے بعد چار رکعت نماز پڑھی ایسی جگہ میں جہاں جمعہ کے صحیح ہونے میں شک ہے آخری ظہر کی نیت سے جو اس پر تھی یا اول ظہر جس کا وقت اس نے پایا اور ادا نہیں کی، پھر جمعہ کا صحیح ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا تو صحیح و معتمد قول کے مطابق وہ سنت جمعہ کی طرف سے کافی ہوگی جبکہ اس کے ذمہ ظہر کی چھوٹی ہوئی نماز نہ ہو اور دوسرے قول پر نہیں جیسا کہ فتح القدیر میں ہے اور یہ بھی اس پر متفرع ہے کہ جب نماز کا وصف باطل ہو گیا تو اس کی اصل باطل نہیں ہوگی امام ابی حنیفہ اور امام ابی یوسف کے قول کے مطابق امام محمد کا اختلاف ہے تو مناسب ہے کہ کہا جائے کہ وہ سنت کی طرف سے کافی ہوگی مگر محمد کے قول پر اور مناسب ہے کہ مسنون روزوں کو مسنون نمازوں کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جائے پس ان کے لئے تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے اور نہیں دیکھا میں نے جس نے اس پر تنبیہ کی ہو۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ نے سنن مؤکدہ کی تعین کے شرط ہونے اور نہ ہونے پر ایک دوسرا مسئلہ بورتشریح ذکر کیا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے جمعہ کی نماز کے بعد ایسی جگہ چار رکعت نماز پڑھی جہاں جمعہ کی صحت کے بارے میں شک ہے کہ یہاں جمعہ صحیح ہوتا ہے یا نہیں آخری ظہر کی نیت سے جو اس کے ذمہ تھی یا وہ ظہر کی پہلی جو اس کے ذمہ تھی اور ابھی تک ادا نہیں کی اس کے بعد اس کو یقین کے ساتھ یہ معلوم ہوگیا کہ جمعہ کی نماز میری بھی ہوگئی تو اب سوال یہ ہے کہ جو ظہر کی نیت سے چار رکعت پڑھی ہیں وہ جمعہ کے بعد کی چار سنتوں کے قائم مقام ہوگی یا نہیں جن فقہاء نے تعیین نیت کو ضروری قرار دیا ہے ان کے نزدیک جمعہ کے بعد کی چار سنتوں کے قائم مقام نہ ہوگی البتہ جن فقہاء نے تعیین نیت کو سنن مؤکدہ کے لئے شرط قرار نہیں دیا ہے ان کے نزدیک جمعہ کے بعد کی چار سنتوں کے قائم مقام ہو جائیں گی۔ البتہ اگر اس کے ذمہ ظہر کی فوت شدہ نماز تھی تو پھر یہ چار رکعت جو اس نے پڑھی ظہر کی طرف سے ادا ہوں گی اور سنتوں کے قائم مقام نہ ہوں کیونکہ یہی مطلب ہے حيث لم يكن عليه ظهر فائت کا۔
And a further branch issue also arises from the condition of specification (ta'yin) for the regular sunan and from its absence: if one prays four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah in a place where the validity of Jumu'ah is doubted, intending the last Zuhr that was upon him or the first Zuhr whose time he reached and did not perform, then Jumu'ah becomes evident as valid. According to the correct and relied-upon view, it suffices for the sunnah of Jumu'ah provided there was no missed Zuhr upon him. On the other view, it does not, as in Fath al-Qadir. This also branches from the principle that if the description of a prayer becomes void, its essence does not become void according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. So it should be said that it becomes for the sunnah except according to Muhammad. And it is appropriate to attach the supererogatory fasts (sunan siyam) to the supererogatory prayers (sunan salat), so specification is not required for them, and I have not seen anyone who pointed that out.
Translation: [Urdu commentary discussing the same].
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents a branch issue (furu') derived from the earlier discussion on whether specific intention (ta'yin) is required for the regular sunan (sunan rawatib). The scenario: after praying Jumu'ah in a place where its validity is doubtful, a person prays four rak'ahs with the intention of making up a missed Zuhr prayer (either the last Zuhr he owed or the first Zuhr of the day that he missed). Later, it becomes clear that the Jumu'ah was valid. The question: can these four rak'ahs count as the sunnah of Jumu'ah (the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah)? According to the relied-upon (mu'tamad) view, they suffice for the sunnah, provided the person did not actually owe a missed Zuhr. On the other view (which considers ta'yin necessary), they do not. The passage further notes that this ruling also depends on the principle of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that when the description (wasf) of a prayer becomes invalid (e.g., it was intended as fard but becomes nafl), the essence (asl) of the prayer remains valid. Imam Muhammad disagreed. Therefore, the four rak'ahs can be considered sunnah except according to Muhammad's view. The author then adds an observation: this principle should also apply to supererogatory fasts (sunan siyam), so ta'yin is not required for them either, though he notes that he has not seen anyone explicitly state this. This demonstrates the method of qiyas and ta'lil in extending rulings from salah to siyam.

Key Terms
متفرع (mutafarri'): A branch issue derived from a foundational principle.
وصف الصلاة (wasf al-salah): The specific classification of a prayer (e.g., fard, sunnah) that may change without affecting the prayer's essential validity.
سنن الصيام (الصيامات المسنونة) (sunan al-siyam): Recommended fasts, such as fasting on Mondays and Thursdays or the white days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, if a person prays four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah with the intention of making up a missed Zuhr, and later Jumu'ah is confirmed valid, what is the ruling if he had no missed Zuhr?
A) The four rak'ahs are invalid and must be repeated.
B) They count as sunnah of Jumu'ah.
C) They remain as make-up Zuhr despite Jumu'ah's validity.
D) They become nafl but not sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'if description becomes void, essence does not void' allows a prayer's legal classification to change without invalidating the prayer itself, a key principle in resolving intention-related doubts.

Intention for Sunnah Prayers and the Principle of Description vs Essence
Branch issue on ta'yin for sunan rawatib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that specific intention is not required for sunan rawatib, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether invalidation of a prayer's description invalidates its essence.

Core Idea
If a prayer's description becomes invalid, its essence remains valid—so a mistakenly intended Zuhr can count as Sunnah.

This passage presents a branch (furu') derived from the principle of requiring specific intention (ta'yin) for regular sunan prayers. The scenario involves praying four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah with an intention that turns out to be incorrect. The ruling depends on a deeper principle: when a prayer's description (e.g., obligatory) is invalidated, does its essence remain valid? Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf say yes; Imam Muhammad says no. The relied-upon position allows the prayer to count as Sunnah under certain conditions. The author also extends this to supererogatory fasts and lists the regular sunan prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue and the scenario
Read the passage and locate the scenario: a person prays four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah intending a missed Zuhr or the first Zuhr due, then Jumu'ah is found valid. What do those four rak'ahs count as?
The key variable is whether the person had an outstanding missed Zuhr obligation.
2
Extract the governing qawida
The passage is built on the qawida: 'Specific intention is not required for the regular sunan prayers.' Identify this principle and note its scope.
This qawida is a dabt (sub-maxim) that restricts the general rule requiring ta'yin for fard prayers.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on wasf and asl
The second branch concerns whether invalidation of a prayer's description (wasf) invalidates its essence (asl). Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifah/Abu Yusuf with that of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
Use the madhhab dispute map to understand the talil (reasoning).
4
Apply the qawida and the dispute to the scenario
Work through the scenario: if there is no missed Zuhr, the four rak'ahs count as Sunnah according to the relied-upon position. Why? Because the description (obligatory Zuhr) became invalid, but the essence remains valid and is redirected to Sunnah.
Note the exception: if there is a missed Zuhr, the prayer counts as qada of that Zuhr, not Sunnah.
5
Extend the principle to supererogatory fasts
The author analogously states that supererogatory fasts do not require specific intention, based on the same principle. Evaluate the validity of this extension.
This is an original point by the author; he notes he has not seen it elsewhere.

وَتَفَرَّعَ أَيْضاً عَلَى إِشْتِرَاطِ التَّعْيِينِ لِلسُّنَنِ الرَّوَاتِبِ، وَعَدَمِهِ مَسْأَلَةٌ أُخْرَى هِيَ: لَوْ صَلَّى بَعْدَ الْجُمُعَةِ أَرْبَعاً فِي مَوْضِعٍ يَشُكُّ فِي صِحَّةِ الْجُمُعَةِ، نَاوِياً آخِرَ ظُهْرٍ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ أَوَّلَ مَا أَدْرَكَ وَقْتُهُ وَلَمْ يُؤَدِّهِ. ثُمَّ تَبَيَّنَ صِحَّةُ الْجُمُعَةِ فَعَلَى الصَّحِيحِ الْمُعْتَمَدِ تَنُوبُ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْجُمُعَةِ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِ ظُهْرٌ فَائِتُ، وَعَلَى الْقَوْلِ الْآخَرِ: لَا، كَمَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ. وَهُوَ أَيْضاً يَتَفَرَّعُ عَلَى أَنَّ الصَّلَاةَ إِذَا بَطَلَ وَصْفُهَا لَا يَبْطُلُ أَصْلُهَا عَلَى قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ، خِلَافاً لِمُحَمَّدٍ. فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُقَالَ فِيْهَا: إِنَّهَا تَكُونُ عَنِ السُّنَّةِ إِلَّا عَلَى قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ. وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُلْحَقَ الصِّيَامَاتُ الْمَسْنُونَةُ بِالصَّلَوَاتِ الْمَسْنُونَةِ، فَلَا يُشْتَرَطُ لَهَا التَّعْيِينُ، وَلَمْ أَرَ مَنْ نَبَّهَ عَلَيْهِ. ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ السُّنَنَ الرَّوَاتِبَ: السُّنَنُ الرَّوَاتِبُ فِي الْيَوْمِ وَاللَّيْلَةِ ثِنْتَا عَشَرَةَ رَكْعَةً: رَكْعَتَانِ قَبْلَ الْفَجْرِ، وَأَرْبَعٌ قَبْلَ الظُّهْرِ، وَرَكْعَتَانِ بَعْدَهَا، وَرَكْعَتَانِ بَعْدَ الْمَغْرِبِ، وَرَكْعَتَانِ بَعْدَ الْعِشَاءِ. وَفِي صَلَاةِ الْجُمُعَةِ أَرْبَعٌ قَبْلَهَا وَأَرْبَعٌ بَعْدَهَا. وَالتَّرَاوِيحُ عِشْرُونَ رَكْعَةً بِعَشْرِ تَسْلِيمَاتٍ بَعْدَ الْعِشَاءِ فِي لَيَالِي رَمَضَانَ. وَصَلَاةُ الْوِتْرِ عَلَى قَوْلِهِمَا. وَصَلَاةُ الْعِيدَيْنِ فِي إِحْدَى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ. وَصَلَاةُ الْكُسُوفِ عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ، وَقِيلَ: وَاجِبَةٌ. وَصَلَاةُ الْخُسُوفِ وَالِاسْتِسْقَاءِ عَلَى قَوْلٍ.
And there also branches from the condition of specifying intention for the regular sunan and its absence another issue: if one prays four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah in a place where the validity of Jumu'ah is doubted, intending the last Zuhr that is due upon him or the first [Zuhr] whose time he reached but did not perform. Then the validity of Jumu'ah becomes evident. So according to the correct and relied-upon opinion, it suffices for the Jumu'ah prayer provided there is no missed Zuhr upon him. And according to the other opinion: no, as in Fath al-Qadir. And it also branches upon that if the description of a prayer becomes invalid, its essence does not become invalid according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. So it is appropriate to say regarding it: it counts as the Sunnah except according to Muhammad's opinion. And it is appropriate that supererogatory fasts be annexed to supererogatory prayers, so specification is not required for them. And I have not seen anyone who pointed that out. Then he mentioned the regular sunan: The regular sunan in the day and night are twelve rak'ahs: two before Fajr, four before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, and two after Isha. And in Jumu'ah prayer: four before it and four after it. And tarawih is twenty rak'ahs with ten salutations after Isha on the nights of Ramadan. And Witr prayer according to their opinion. And the two Eid prayers in one of the two narrations. And the eclipse prayer according to the correct opinion; and it is said: obligatory. And the lunar eclipse prayer and the prayer for rain according to an opinion.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a branch (furu') derived from the principle of whether specific intention (ta'yin) is required for the regular Sunnah prayers (sunan rawatib). The author presents a scenario: a person prays four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah in a place where the validity of Jumu'ah is uncertain. He intends it as the last Zuhr he owes or as the first Zuhr whose time he missed. Later, Jumu'ah is confirmed valid. The question: do those four rak'ahs count as the post-Jumu'ah Sunnah? According to the relied-upon position (the one that does not require ta'yin for sunan), they do, provided he had no missed Zuhr. According to the opposite view (requiring ta'yin), they do not. This issue branches from another principle: if a prayer's description (e.g., obligatory status) becomes invalid, does its essence become invalid? Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf say no – the essence remains valid; Muhammad says yes – invalidation of description invalidates the essence. Hence, here, when Jumu'ah is found valid, the four rak'ahs lose their description as Zuhr (obligatory) but remain a valid prayer, so they can be counted as Sunnah according to the two shaykhs, but not according to Muhammad (unless the person could not have been discharged from the obligation). The author then extends the principle to supererogatory fasts: like supererogatory prayers, they do not require specific intention. Finally, he lists the regular sunan prayers and other recommended prayers.

Key Terms
التَّعْيِين (al-ta'yin): Specifying the particular prayer or act in one's intention (niyyah), e.g., intending 'Zuhr' or 'Fajr'.
السُّنَنُ الرَّوَاتِبُ (al-sunan al-rawatib): The regular supererogatory prayers that are consistently performed before or after the obligatory prayers.
الوَصْف (al-wasf): The legal description or attribute of an act, such as being obligatory (fard) or supererogatory (nafl).
الأَصْل (al-asl): The essence or core of the act of worship itself, as opposed to its legal description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Imam Muhammad differs from Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf on the principle of invalidation of description. According to the relied-upon position in the passage, if a person prays four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah intending a missed Zuhr, and then Jumu'ah is found valid, what is the ruling if he has no missed Zuhr?
A) The four rak'ahs are invalid and must be repeated.
B) The four rak'ahs count as the post-Jumu'ah Sunnah.
C) The four rak'ahs count as qada of Zuhr.
D) The four rak'ahs are considered voluntary without specification.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position holds that specific intention is not required for sunan rawatib, and invalidation of a prayer's description does not invalidate its essence, allowing it to count as Sunnah under appropriate conditions.

Effect of Invalid Attribute on the Original Act
Explaining a furua of a disputed usul rule about asl and wasf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida regarding the invalidation of a legal attribute (wasf) to determine the status of the original act (asl), and identify the exception recognized by Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Shaykhayn: invalid attribute does not void the act; Imam Muhammad: it does, unless the act can discharge an obligation.

This passage explores a key qawida that arises in the usul of worship: if a legal attribute (wasf) such as fardiyyah becomes invalid, does the original act (asl) become invalid? The Hanafi school has an internal ikhtilaf between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad, with an important exception. Understanding this rule is crucial for a mufti when determining the status of an act after the invalidation of its intended obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage to determine the views of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad on whether the invalidation of an attribute invalidates the original act.
Shaykhayn: original remains valid; Imam Muhammad: original becomes invalid.
2
Analyze the Jumu'ah example
Consider the example of praying four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah. According to Shaykhayn, they become nafl; according to Imam Muhammad, they are invalid. Trace the reasoning.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
3
Recognize the exception to Imam Muhammad's rule
Note that Imam Muhammad allows the original to remain valid if the act can discharge an obligation. This is key to applying the rule correctly.
The Hajj badal example shows this exception.
4
Apply the rule to a new case
Given a scenario where someone performs a fard prayer but the obligation was already fulfilled, determine the outcome under both positions, considering the exception.
Think about whether the exception applies.
