ولو نوى الاقتداء بالأمام وهو يرى انه زيد فاذا هو عمرو صح اقتداء ه لان العبرة بمانوى لا شمیری و هر قد نوى الاقتداء بالأماه رخانية على هامش الهنديه ج ۱، ص : ۸۳)
وفي النَّادَارُ خَانِيَّةِ تَوَصَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، وَتَوَى أَنَّ هَذَا ظُهْرُ يَوْمِ الثَّلَنَاءِ، فَتَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهُ مِنْ يَوْمٍ الْأَرْبَعَاءِ جَازَ ظُفْرُهُ، وَالْغَلَط فِى تَعْيِينِ الْوَقْتِ لا يَضُرُّ ، إنتهى .
تشريح
ترجمه: اور تار تار خانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ظہر کی نماز پڑھی اور یہ نیت کی کہ یہ منگل کے دن کی ظہر ہے پھر پتہ چا کہ دیدہ کا دن ہے تو اس کی ظہیر جائز ہے اور وقت کی تعیین میں غلطی مضر نہیں ہے تارتار خانہ کا کام پر ہوا۔ اگر کسی شخص نے آج کی ظہر کی نماز پڑھی تو آج کی ظہر کی نیت سے اس کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی دان کی تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے لیکن اگر دن کی تعیین میں غلطی ہو جائے تو مضر نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً اس نے نیت کی آج منگل کی خبر پڑھ رہا ہوں پھر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ وہ بدھ کے روز کی ظہر ہے تو اس کی ظہر کی نماز بیج ہو جائے گی اور وقت کی تعین میں غلطی مضر نہ ہوگی۔ رجل صلى الظهر و نوى ان هذا من ظهر الثلثاء فتبين ان ذلك من يوم الاربعاء جاز ظهره الخلط فى تعيين الوقت لا يضر ( تار تار خانیه ج ص : ۴۳۴)
وَمِثْلُهُ فِي الصَّوْمِ لَوْنَوَى قَضَاءَ يَوْمِ الْخَمِيْسِ، فَإِذَا عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ لَا يَجُوْزُ، وَلَوْنَوَى قَضَاءَ مَا عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الصَّوْمِ ، وَهُوَ يَظُنُّهُ يَوْمَ الْخَمِيسِ ، وَهُوَ غَيْرُهُ جَازَ.
ترجمه اور ان کے مثل ہے روزہ میں اگر جمعرات کے دن کے روزے کی قضاء کی بھر معلوم ہوا کہ اس کے ذمہ اس کے علاوہ کی قضا تھی تو جائز نہیں اور اگر اس روزہ کی قضاء کی جو اس کے ذمہ تھی اور وہ اسے جمعرات کا دن خیال ا کر رہا ہے حالانکہ وہ اس کے علاوہ تھا تو جائز ہے۔ تشریح کسی کے ذمہ کسی دن کے روزے کی قضا تھی قضا کرتے وقت اس نے یہ نیت کی کہ میں جمعرات کے دن کے روزے کی قضا کر رہا ہوں پھر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ اس کے اوپر دوسرا بھی روز و سے تو تعیین میں خطا کی وجہ سے روز وادانہ ہوگا چونکہ جس دن کا روز در کھا اس دن کی قضا اس کے میتھی ہی نہیں اور جس دن کے روزہ کی قضاتی و درکھا ہی نہیں اس لئے سیدوز وقضا کا نہ ہو کر نفل ہو جائے گا۔ ولونوى قضاء ما علیه: اگر کسی نے اس نیت سے قضا روزہ رکھا کہ جو روز و میرے ذمہ ہے و ہ روز در کھ رہا ہوں اور خیال اس کا یہ ہوگا کہ غالباً وہ جمعرات کا روزہ تھا حالانکہ تھا وہ بدھ کا روزہ تو اس صورت میں اس کا روزہ درست ہو جائے گا چونکہ اس صورت میں نیت اصلاً صرف یہ ہے کہ جو روزہ میرے ذمہ ہے وہ رکھ رہا ہوں اتنی نیست درست و کافی ہے اور اس کا اس دن کو جمعرات تصور کرنا یہ نیت کی غلطی نہیں بلکہ خیال و تصور کی غلطی ہے جو معبر نہیں ہے قاعدہ ہے لو وقع الخطأ في الاعتقاددون التعيين فانه لا يضر
It will be harmful, like when someone specifies prayer in place of fasting or fasting in place of prayer, or specifies Asr prayer instead of Zuhr: this error harms him, because for the validity of fasting and each prayer, specification (ta'yin) is necessary. So when there is an error in the very essence of the act, it will be considered, and the prayer or fast will not be valid. And from that category is the case when one intends to follow Zaid but it turns out to be 'Amr. It is better not to specify the imam when the congregation is large, lest it be revealed that he is not the specified one—which is not permissible. So one should intend the person standing in the mihrab, whoever he may be, even if it does not cross his mind that he is Zaid or 'Amr, and following him is valid. And if one intends to follow the standing imam while thinking he is Zaid but he is 'Amr, his following is valid because consideration is given to what he intended, not what he saw; and he intended following the imam. Translation: And from that category is the case when one intended following Zaid and it turned out to be 'Amr. It is better not to specify the imam when the congregation is large... [continues with examples from fasting, etc.] And the principle is: 'If error occurs in belief without determination, it does not harm.'
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair discusses the fiqhi qawida regarding errors in intention (niyyah). It distinguishes between two types of error: error in determination (ta'yin) and error in belief (i'tiqad). The commentary first gives examples from prayer and fasting, then extends to following an imam. The core rule: if one intends a specific act (e.g., 'Zuhr of Tuesday') but is mistaken about the identity of the act (it is actually Wednesday's Zuhr), the error in the determination of time does not harm because the intention was genuinely for Zuhr prayer. However, if one specifies a particular obligation (e.g., 'the fast of Thursday') but it turns out a different day's qada was due, the error in specification invalidates the fast because the intended object does not match the actual liability. The key distinction: when the error is in the belief about the day (i'tiqad) while the core intention is correct (qada of what is owed), it is valid. But when the error is in the determination (ta'yin) of which specific day's qada, it invalidates. The passage ends by stating the qawida: 'Error in belief without determination does not harm.'

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Explicit specification of the object of intention (e.g., naming a specific person or day).
اعتقاد (i'tiqad): Belief or assumption about the object of intention without explicit specification.
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart; the purpose behind an act of worship or transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man owes a qada fast from last month. He intends to fast 'what is owed to me' and happens to think it is Thursday's fast, but it is actually Wednesday's fast. What is the ruling?
A) The fast is invalid because he specified the wrong day.
B) The fast is valid because he intended the general qada, and the error in belief does not harm.
C) The fast is invalid unless he specifies the correct day.
D) The fast becomes a nafl fast.

Key Takeaway
Always distinguish between an error in the specification of the act (ta'yin) and an error in one's belief about it (i'tiqad); only the former invalidates the intention in Hanafi fiqh.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Error in Belief Does Not Harm: The Qawida and Its Applications
Explaining the rule that error in belief does not harm if the specific intent is correct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-ibratu bi ma nawa la bi tasmiyatihi' to distinguish valid and invalid intentions in salah, sawm, and janazah.

Core Idea
What matters is your actual intent, not the mistaken labels you attach.

This lesson unpacks a vital Hanafi maxim: error in belief (i'tiqad) does not harm the validity of an act, provided the specific intention (ta'yin) is correct. The text provides several furu' to illustrate the boundary. As a mufti, you must grasp that the subjective reality of niyyah can override mistaken naming or belief.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the maxim in Arabic and English: الاعتبار بما نوى لا بتسميته. Consideration is given to what one intended, not to his naming.
2
Distinguish i'tiqad vs ta'yin
Understand that ta'yin is the specific object of intention (e.g., which prayer, which fast), while i'tiqad is the belief about its attributes. Error in i'tiqad is harmless if ta'yin is correct.
3
Apply to salah scenarios
Work through the two salah examples: (a) mistaken day of Zuhr, (b) mistaken identity of imam when seen or described.
Note that ishara (pointing) makes naming irrelevant.
4
Apply to sawm scenarios
Compare two qada fast cases: one invalid (intending a specific day not owed) and one valid (intending the owed fast with mistaken belief about day).
This is the key istithna': if the ta'yin itself is wrong, the act is invalid.
5
Apply to janazah and conclude
For multiple bodies, intend the one the imam prays upon. Summarize the principle: error in belief does not harm; error in specific intention does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَو نَوَى الاقْتِدَاءَ بِالإِمَامِ وَهُوَ يَرَى أَنَّهُ زَيْدٌ فَإِذَا هُوَ عَمْرٌو صَحَّ اقْتِدَاؤُهُ لأَنَّ الْعِبْرَةَ بِمَا نَوَى لا بِتَسْمِيَتِهِ، وَهُوَ قَدْ نَوَى الاقْتِدَاءَ بِالإِمَامِ. وَفِي النَّادَرُخَانِيَّةِ: تَوَصَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، وَنَوَى أَنَّ هَذَا ظُهْرُ يَوْمِ الثَّلَثَاءِ، فَتَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهُ مِنْ يَوْمِ الأَرْبِعَاءِ جَازَ ظُهْرُهُ، وَالْغَلَطُ فِي تَعْيِينِ الْوَقْتِ لا يَضُرُّ. وَمِثْلُهُ فِي الصَّوْمِ لَوْ نَوَى قَضَاءَ يَوْمِ الْخَمِيسِ، فَإِذَا عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ لا يَجُوزُ، وَلَوْ نَوَى قَضَاءَ مَا عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الصَّوْمِ، وَهُوَ يَظُنُّهُ يَوْمَ الْخَمِيسِ، وَهُوَ غَيْرُهُ جَازَ. وَلَوْ كَانَ يَرَى شَخْصَهُ فَنَوَى الاقْتِدَاءَ بِهَذَا الإِمَامِ الَّذِي هُوَ زَيْدٌ فَإِذَا هُوَ خِلافُهُ جَازَ لأَنَّهُ عَرَّفَهُ بِالإِشَارَةِ فَلَغَتِ التَّسْمِيَةُ، وَكَذَا لَوْ كَانَ فِي آخِرِ الصُّفُوفِ لا يَرَى شَخْصَهُ فَنَوَى الاقْتِدَاءَ بِالإِمَامِ الْقَائِمِ فِي الْمِحْرَابِ الَّذِي هُوَ زَيْدٌ فَإِذَا هُوَ غَيْرُهُ جَازَ أَيْضًا. وَمِثْلُهُ مَا ذَكَرْنَا فِي الْخَطَأِ فِي تَعْيِينِ الْمَيِّتِ فَعِنْدَ الْكَثْرَةِ يَنْوِي الْمَيِّتَ الَّذِي يُصَلِّي عَلَيْهِ الإِمَامُ كَذَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ.
If he intended to follow the imam while he thought it was Zayd, but it turned out to be `Amr, his following is valid because consideration is given to what he intended, not his naming. And in al-Nadarukhaniyyah: He prayed Zuhr intending that this is Zuhr of Tuesday, then it became clear it is from Wednesday; his Zuhr is valid, and error in specification of time does not harm. And similar is in fasting: if he intended to make up the fast of Thursday, then it turned out a different day was due, it is not valid; but if he intended to make up the fast due upon him, while he thought it was Thursday but it was different, it is valid. And if he saw the person and intended to follow this imam who is Zayd, then it turned out to be someone else, it is valid because he identified him by pointing, so the naming is irrelevant. Similarly if he was in the last row not seeing the person, and intended to follow the imam standing in the mihrab who is Zayd, then it turned out to be someone else, it is also valid. And similar is what we mentioned about error in specifying the deceased: when there are many, he intends the deceased upon whom the imam prays – thus in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents a key qawida (maxim) in Hanafi fiqh: error in belief (i`tiqad) does not invalidate an act if the specific intention (ta`yin) is correct. The mufti or student should understand that the criterion is the actual intent, not mistaken labels. The author provides several furu` (applications): (1) In salah, if one intends to pray Zuhr and mistakenly specifies the day, the prayer is valid. (2) In qada sawm, if one intends the fast due upon him but mistakenly thinks it is Thursday, it is valid; but if he intends a specific fast that he does not owe, it is not valid. (3) In following an imam, if one sees him and points, the naming is irrelevant; even if unseen, the description 'the imam in the mihrab' suffices. (4) In janazah, when there are many bodies, one should intend the corpse on which the imam prays. The principle is that what matters is the actual object of intention, not erroneous beliefs about its attributes. This is from the Hanafi school's emphasis on the subjective reality of niyyah.

Key Terms
تَعْيِين (ta`yin): Specification of the exact object of the action (e.g., which prayer, which fast).
اعْتِقَاد (i`tiqad): Belief or assumption about the attributes of the intended object.
تَسْمِيَة (tasmiyah): Naming or labeling the intended object (e.g., saying 'Zayd' when it is `Amr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida, if a person intends to pray Asr and mistakenly thinks it is Dhuhr, his prayer is:
A. Invalid because he intended the wrong prayer.
B. Valid because he actually intended Asr.
C. Invalid because belief is part of intention.
D. Valid only if he didn't say 'Dhuhr'.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of an act depends on the actual object of intention (ta'yin), not on mistaken beliefs (i'tiqad) about its attributes.

The Rule of Indication Overriding Naming in Intention (Isharah wa Tasmiyah)
Ruling on mistaken identity in following the imam with analogy to funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim that indication overrides naming to cases of mistaken identity in congregational and funeral prayers, and state the fatwa hierarchy that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Indication prevails over naming: visual or locational identification of the imam determines validity, not the verbal name.

In congregational prayer, a follower may mistakenly name the imam in his intention. Does this error invalidate the prayer? The Hanafi school answers with a clear principle: if the follower has correctly identified the imam by sight or by location (the mihrab), the name is irrelevant. This lesson unpacks the maxim derived from this ruling and shows how it applies to funeral prayer as well. You will learn to parse the scenarios, extract the legal maxim, and apply it in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and list the two situations: (1) follower sees the imam's person, (2) follower does not see the imam but knows his location (the mihrab).
In both, the follower incorrectly names the imam.
2
Extract the governing legal maxim
Notice that both scenarios are upheld as valid. The common principle is that actual identification (by sight or location) determines the object of intention, not the verbal name. State this maxim in Arabic and English.
The maxim is: الإشارة تقدم على التسمية (Indication overrides naming).
3
Analyze the rationale (talil)
Why does indication override naming? Because intention follows what is known with certainty. Visual or locational indication provides certain identification, whereas a name may be incorrectly applied.
This is based on the broader principle that certainty is not removed by doubt.
4
Apply the maxim to funeral prayer
The passage analogizes to janazah: when multiple deceased are present, the follower should not name a specific deceased but rather intend to follow the imam's intended deceased. The same maxim applies: the indication (the imam's action) overrides any naming by the follower.
Fath al-Qadir supports this extension.
5
Determine the fatwa hierarchy
Identify the authority level of this ruling. It appears in later Hanafi works (Halabi Kabir, Fath al-Qadir) and is the mufta bihi position. Recognize that this is a settled rule within the school.
Source authority: fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa works).

وَلَوْ كَانَ يَرَى شَخْصَهُ فَنَوَى الْاقْتِدَاءَ بِهَذَا الإِمَامِ الَّذِى هُوَ زَيْدٌ فَإِذَا هُوَ خِلَافُهُ جَازَ لِأَنَّهُ عَرَّفَهُ بِالْإِشَارَةِ، فَلَغَتِ التَّسْمِيَةُ، وَكَذَالَوْ كَانَ فِي آخِرِ الصُّفُوْفِ لَا يَرَى شَخْصَهُ فَنَوَى الْاقْتِدَاءَ بِالْإِمَامِ الْقَائِمِ فِى الْمِحْرَابِ الَّذِي هُوَ زَيْدٌ، فَإِذَاهُوَ غَيْرُهُ جَازَ أَيْضًا. ترجمہ: اور اگر وہ اس کی شخصیت کو دیکھ رہا ہے اور اس نے اس امام کی اقتداء کی نیت کی کہ وہ زید ہے پھر معلوم ہوا کہ وہ اس کے علاوہ ہے تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے اسے اشارہ سے متعین کر دیا تھا، تو تسمیہ لغو ہو گیا اور یسے ہی اگر وہ آخری صف میں ہو جو اس کی شخصیت کو نہ دیکھ رہا ہو، پس اس امام کی اقتداء کی نیت کی جو محراب میں ہے کہ وہ زید ہے پھر پتہ چلا کہ وہ اس کے علاوہ ہے تو جائز ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب کتاب فرماتے ہیں کہ مقتدی نے یہ نیت کی کہ امام کی اقتدا میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہے امام پر اس کی نظر پڑی اور مقتدی یہ سمجھا کہ امام زید ہے حالانکہ امام عمرو ہے، تو اقتداء درست رہے گی کیونکہ جب اشارہ اور تسمیہ دونوں میں تعارض ہو جائے تو ایسی صورت میں اشارہ معتبر ہوتا ہے اور تسمیہ کا العدم اور لغو ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اگر مقتدی ایسی جگہ کھڑا ہے جہاں سے امام نظر نہیں آ رہا ہے اور اس کا خیال یہ ہے کہ زید امام ہے حالانکہ امام ید کے علاوہ ہے لیکن ایس نے یہ نیت کی تھی کہ میں اس امام کی اقتداء کر رہا ہوں جو محراب میں کھڑا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی انتہا صرف اس تعیین کا ہے کہ میں محراب میں کھڑے ہونے والے امام کی اقتداء کر رہا ہوں تسمیہ زید کا اعتبار نہیں اس لئے اگر امام زید کے علاوہ کوئی اور بھی ہے تب بھی اقتداء درست ہے۔
ولو كان المقتدى يرى شخص الامام وقال اقتديت بهذا الإمام الذي هو عبدالله وظهر انه ابو جعفر جاز لانه عرفه بالإشارة فلغت التسمية (حلبي كبير ص: (۲۵۲)
وَمِثْلُهُ مَاذَكَرْنَا فِي الْخَطَا فِي تَعيِينِ الْمَيِّتِ ، فَعِنْدَ الْكَفْرَةِ يَنْوِي الْمَيِّتَ الَّذِي يُصَلِّى
عَلَيْهِ الْإِمَامُ كَذَا فِي ”فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ “. ترجمه اور اس کے مثل وہ ہے جسے ہم نے تعیین میت کی غلطی میں ذکر کیا ہے چنانچہ کثرت کے وقت وہ ال میت کی نیت کرے جس پر امام نماز پڑھ رہا ہے، فتح القدیر میں ایسا ہی ہے۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شخص نماز جنازہ میں امام کی اقتداء کر رہا ہے تو اسے چاہئے کہ وہ بہ نیت نہ کرے کہ میں فلاں کی نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں ہو سکتا ہے جس نام کے ساتھ تعین کی ہے وہ میت اس کے علاوہ کسی اور نام کی ہو تو نماز جنازہ درست نہ ہوگی بلکہ اسے چاہئے کہ وہ صرف اتنی نیت کرے کہ امام جس میت کی نماز پڑھ رہا ہے میں بھی اسی کی پڑھ رہا ہوں۔ ولكن ينبغي ان ينوى الاقتداء بالامام في الصلواة على الميت الذي يصلي الامام عليه
(خانیه بر حاشیه بندی ج ۱ ص: ۸۳)
If he sees his person and intends to follow this imam who is Zaid, but it turns out to be someone else, it is valid because he identified him by indication, so the naming is nullified. Similarly, if he is in the last row and does not see his person, and intends to follow the imam standing in the mihrab who is Zaid, but it turns out to be someone else, it is also valid. Translation: If he sees his person and intends to follow this imam thinking he is Zaid, then it becomes clear he is someone else, it is permissible because he specified him by indication, so the naming becomes void. Similarly, if he is in the last row not seeing his person, and intends to follow the imam in the mihrab thinking he is Zaid, then it becomes clear he is someone else, it is permissible. Explanation: The author says that the follower intended to pray following the imam, he saw the imam and thought the imam was Zaid whereas the imam was Amr; the following is valid because when indication and naming conflict, indication is relied upon and naming is disregarded and void. And if the follower is standing where he cannot see the imam and he thinks Zaid is the imam but the imam is someone else, but he intended to follow the imam standing in the mihrab, then in this case the specification is only that I am following the imam standing in the mihrab, the naming of Zaid is not considered; so even if the imam is someone other than Zaid, the following is valid. And if the follower sees the imam's person and says, 'I have followed this imam who is Abdullah,' and it appears he is Abu Ja'far, it is valid because he recognized him by indication, so the naming is nullified (Halabi Kabir p. 252). And similar is what we mentioned regarding the error in specifying the deceased: when there are many, he should intend the deceased upon whom the imam is praying. This is in Fath al-Qadir. Translation: And similar to that is what we mentioned about the mistake in specifying the deceased: when there are many, he should intend the deceased upon whom the imam is praying, as in Fath al-Qadir. Explanation: If a person follows the imam in funeral prayer, he should not intend that I am praying for so-and-so, because it is possible that the name he specified belongs to a different deceased, and the funeral prayer would not be valid. Rather, he should only intend that I am praying for the same deceased upon whom the imam is praying. But he should intend to follow the imam in the prayer over the deceased upon whom the imam is praying (Khaniyah on the margin of Hindi vol. 1 p. 83).
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on intention (niyyah) in following an imam in congregational prayer, specifically when the follower makes a mistake in identifying the imam's name. The author states two scenarios: first, when the follower sees the imam physically and intends to follow him, thinking he is Zaid, but it turns out to be someone else, the prayer is valid because the visual identification (isharah) is the real determinant, and the name (tasmiyah) becomes irrelevant. Second, when the follower cannot see the imam (e.g., in the last row) but intends to follow the imam standing in the mihrab, thinking he is Zaid, but it turns out to be someone else, the prayer is also valid because the intention is attached to the person in the mihrab, not the name. The principle is that when indication (isharah) and naming (tasmiyah) conflict, indication prevails. This is supported by a quote from Halabi Kabir. The passage then extends this analogy to funeral prayer (salat al-janazah): when there are multiple deceased, the follower should not specify a name but should intend to follow the imam in praying over the same deceased the imam is praying over. This prevents invalidation due to error in naming. The explanation in Urdu clarifies these points, emphasizing that the validity depends on correct identification of the person (dhat) through visual indication or location, not on the name.

Key Terms
الإشارة (al-isharah): Visual indication or identification of the imam by sight or by pointing to him.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Naming the imam verbally in the intention, e.g., intending to follow 'Zaid'.
تعيين الميت (ta'yin al-mayyit): Specifying the deceased person in the intention for funeral prayer.

A) The prayer is invalid because the naming was incorrect.
B) The prayer is valid because visual identification overrides the naming.
C) The prayer is valid only if the follower repeats the intention.
D) The prayer is invalid unless the follower knew the imam's name beforehand.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'indication overrides naming' ensures that a follower's prayer remains valid if he correctly identifies the imam by sight or location, even if he makes a mistake in the name.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
The Description-Based Intention Rule and Its Applications
Rulings on description errors in intention and extraction of a maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-wasf mu'tabar 'inda 'adam ta'yin al-dhat' to identify when an error in description invalidates an act of worship and when it does not.

Core Idea
When the essence is unspecified, a description error invalidates; when the essence is specified, description is irrelevant.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Fatawa and subsequent commentaries establishes a crucial distinction for the mufti: the role of description (wasf) in intention. The text presents a case where a follower describes the imam as young but he is old — the prayer is invalid. Yet the reverse (describing as old when he is young) is valid because of common honorary usage. The underlying maxim is extracted: description is only considered when the essence (dhat) is not specified. This rule then extends to funeral prayer and other cases, providing a consistent framework for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two imam cases and their rulings
Contrast the two scenarios: (1) saying 'I follow this young man' but he is old → invalid; (2) saying 'I follow this old man' but he is young → valid. Understand that the asymmetry is due to the respectful use of 'shaykh' for a knowledgeable youth.
The second case is valid because 'shaykh' can be honorary, not an exception to the rule.
2
Extract the underlying maxim
From the commentaries, extract the maxim: 'al-wasf mu'tabar 'inda 'adam ta'yin al-dhat' — description is considered only when the essence is not specified. This is the core legal principle governing these cases.
The maxim applies when the essence is not visually determined through isharah dhatiyyah.
3
Resolve the apparent conflict with the earlier isharah-overrides rule
The doubt raised: why does isharah not override tasmiyah here as before? The answer distinguishes isharah of dhat (points to the specific person) from isharah of wasf (points to a description). Only isharah of dhat overrides; here the isharah was to a description, so it does not override.
This resolution maintains consistency in the usul.
4
Apply the maxim to funeral prayer and number of deceased
Apply the same reasoning: if one intends prayer on a male deceased but it turns out female (or vice versa), it is invalid because the description was wrong and the essence was not visually specified. For number of deceased: specifying ten but finding more invalidates the extra; fewer may be valid.
The maxim applies uniformly across acts of worship involving intention.

:ترجمہ: اور عمدۃ الفتاویٰ میں ہے اگر کہا کہ میں نے اس نو جوان کی اقتداء کی تو پتہ چلا کہ وہ بوڑھا ہے تو یج نہیں اور اگر کہا کہ میں نے اس بوڑھے کی اقتداء کی پتہ چلا کہ وہ نو جوان ہے تو صحیح ہے، اس لئے کہ نوجوان کو شیخ سے پکارا جاتا ہے اس کے علم کی وجہ سے بخلاف اس کے بر عکس کے عمدۃ الفتاویٰ کا کلام پورا ہوا اور اشارہ یہاں کافی نہیں، اس لئے کہ اس اشارہ و امام کی طرف نہیں یہ تو نوجوان یا بوڑھے کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ فتأمل ۔ تشریح مقتدی نے جو ان امام کی نیت کی پھر پتہ چلا کہ وہ بوڑھا ہے تو اقتدار پیچ نہ ہوگی کیونکہ ذات کی تعیین نہ ہونے کی صورت میں وصف کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور یہاں اس سے وصف میں خطا ہوئی ہے تو گویا اب اس نے امام کے علاوہ کسی اور کی اقتداء کی کیونکہ عرف میں بھی جو ان کو بوڑھا نہیں کہا جاتا۔
ولوقال اقتديت بهذا الشاب فاذا هو شيخ لم يصح (البحر الرائق كراچی ج ۱ ص: ۱۰۲) اور اگر صراحت کے ساتھ کہا کہ میں اس شیخ کی اقتداء کر رہا ہوں پتہ چلا کہ وہ تو نو جوان ہے تو اقتدار آتا ہے کیونکہ کبھی کبھی جو ان کو بھی علم کی وجہ سے تعظیماً شیخ کہ دیا جاتا ہے۔ وفى عمدة الفتاوى ولوقال اقتديت بهذا الشيخ وهو شاب صح لان الشاب يدعى شيخا للتعظیم (شامی زکریا ج ۲ س: ۱۰۶)
ایک شبہ اور اس کا ازالہ شبہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ ابھی آپ نے چند سطر پہلے کہا تھا کہ جب اشارہ اور تسمیہ میں تعارض ہو جائے تو تسمیہ باطل ہوجاتا ہے اور اشارہ کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہئے ، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اشارہ کا اس وقت تعارض کی صورت میں اعتبار ہوتا ہے جب وہ ذات کی طرف ہو اور جب وہ وصف کی طرف ہو تو اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا اور یہاں اشارہ وصف کی طرف ہے اس لئے اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوا اور تسمیہ میں اس سے غلطی واقع ہوئی ہے۔ والحاصل ان الوصف معتبر عند عدم تعيين الذات فاما عند تعيينها فلا (حلبى كبير ص:۲۵۲)
وَعَلَى هَذَا لَوْنَوَى الصَّلَاةَ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ الذَّكَرِ فَتَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهُ أُنثَى أَوْ عَكْسُهُ لَمْ يَصِحُ، وَلَمْ أَرَ حُكْمَ مَا إِذَا عَيَّنَ عَدَدَ الْمَوْتَى عَشَرَةً، فَبَانَ أَنَّهُمْ أَكْثَرُ أَوْ أَقَلُّ وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ لَا يَضُرَّ إِلَّا إِذَا بَانَ أَنَّهُمْ أَكْثَرُ فَإِنَّ مِنْهُمْ مَنْ لَّمْ يَنوِى الصَّلاةَ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الزَّائِد.
And in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: If he said, 'I follow this young man,' and it turns out he is an old man, it is not valid. And if he said, 'I follow this old man,' and it turns out he is a young man, it is valid because the young man is called 'sheikh' due to his knowledge, unlike the opposite. And the indication here is not sufficient because it was not an indication to the imam, but rather to a young man or an old man, so reflect. Translation: And in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: if he said 'I followed this young man' and it turned out he is old, it is not valid; and if he said 'I followed this old man' and it turned out he is young, it is valid because a young man is called sheikh out of respect for his knowledge, unlike the opposite. (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Karachi, vol. 1, p. 102) Explanation: The follower intended the imam and then it turned out he was old, so the following is not valid because when the essence (dhat) is not specified, the description (wasf) is considered, and here there was an error in description, so it is as if he followed someone other than the imam, because in common usage a young man is not called old. And if he explicitly said 'I follow this old man' and it turned out he is young, it is valid because sometimes a young man is called sheikh out of respect for his knowledge. A doubt and its removal: The doubt is that earlier it was said that when indication and naming conflict, naming is invalid and indication is considered, so the same should apply here. The answer is that indication is considered when it is of the essence (dhat), but when it is of a description (wasf), it is not considered; and here the indication is of a description, so it was not considered, and the naming had an error. The conclusion is that the description is considered when the essence is not specified; when the essence is specified, it is not considered. (Halabi Kabir p. 252) And upon this, if one intends prayer on a male deceased and it turns out to be female, or vice versa, it is not valid. And I have not seen the ruling for when he specifies the number of deceased as ten, and it turns out they are more or less. The appropriate view is that it is not harmful unless it turns out they are more, because then there are some upon whom he did not intend prayer (the extra ones).
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on intention errors in following an imam, focusing on descriptions (wasf) rather than essence (dhat). It quotes 'Umdat al-Fatawa: if a follower says 'I follow this young man' and it turns out the imam is old, the prayer is invalid because there is a mismatch in description; but if he says 'I follow this old man' and it turns out he is young, it is valid because it is common to call a young man 'sheikh' out of respect for his knowledge. The reason is that when the essence of the imam is not specified by visual indication (isharah), the description becomes the effective determinant. A doubt is raised: why does the principle that isharah overrides tasmiyah not apply here? The author clarifies that isharah only overrides when it points to the essence (dhat), but here the indication is to a description (young/old), so it is not sufficient. The general rule extracted is: 'The description is considered when the essence is not specified; when the essence is specified, it is not.' This is the legal maxim (al-wasf mu'tabar 'inda 'adam ta'yin al-dhat). The passage then applies this to funeral prayer: if one intends prayer on a male deceased but it turns out to be female (or vice versa), the prayer is invalid because the description was incorrect and the essence was not visually specified. Finally, it discusses the case of specifying the number of deceased: if one intends ten bodies but finds more, the prayer is invalid for the extra ones because they were not included in the intention; if less, it may be valid. The Urdu commentary reinforces these points.

Key Terms
الذات (al-dhat): The essence or specific identity of the imam or deceased, identified by sight or clear location.
الوصف (al-wasf): A description or attribute used to identify the imam or deceased, such as young/old or male/female.
الشبهة (al-shubhah): A doubt or misconception about why a ruling seems inconsistent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the imam did not respond appropriately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-wasf mu'tabar 'inda 'adam ta'yin al-dhat' governs intention errors: description matters only when the essence is not specified; upon specification, description is irrelevant.

The Maxim of Description vs Essence in Following an Imam
Ruling on validity of iqtida' when imam's age description is mistaken.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-wasf mu'tabar inda 'adam ta'yin al-dhat' to evaluate the validity of following an imam when the intended description differs from reality, and distinguish between factual and honorific descriptions.

Core Idea
A sincere mistake in description invalidates following only if the description is factual, not honorific.

When you intend to follow an imam, you must specify him. But what if you describe him as 'young' and he is old? The Hanafi school has a nuanced ruling based on the nature of the description. This lesson unpacks the maxim that a description matters only when the essence is not directly specified, and distinguishes factual from honorific descriptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases from 'Umdat al-Fatawa
Read the source passage carefully. There are two scenarios: (1) saying 'young' but imam is old – invalid; (2) saying 'sheikh' but imam is young – valid. Note the difference in outcome.
Focus on the reason given for validity in the second case: honorific usage.
2
Classify the description as factual or honorific
Determine whether the description is a factual attribute (age) or an honorific title. 'Young' is factual; 'sheikh' can be honorific when applied to a knowledgeable young person.
The Hanafi principle of custom ('urf) allows calling a learned person 'sheikh' regardless of actual age.
3
Apply the maxim: الوصف معتبر عند عدم تعيين الذات
The maxim states: description is considered only when the essence (dhat) is not specified. Here, the follower pointed to the imam but through description (young/old). Since the essence was not directly specified, the description matters. If the description is factual and wrong, it invalidates. If honorific and not contradictory, it does not.
The maxim is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) within the broader framework of intentions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي عُمْدَةِ الْفَتَاوَى لَوْ قَالَ: اقْتَدَيْتُ بِهَذَا الشَّابِ، فَإِذَا هُوَ شَيْخٌ لَمْ يَصِحُّ، وَلَوْ قَالَ اقْتَدَيْتُ بِهَذَا الشَّيْخِ، فَإِذَا هُوَ شَابٌ صَحَّ لِأَنَّ الشَّابَّ يُدْعَى شَيْخاً لِعِلْمِهِ، بِخِلَافِ عَكْسِهِ، انْتَهَى. وَالْإِشَارَةُ هَهُنَا لَا تَكْفِي لِأَنَّهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ إِشَارَةً إِلَى الْإِمَامِ إِنَّمَا هِيَ إِلَى شَابٍ أَوْ شَيْخٍ، فَتَأَمَّلْ. ترجمہ: اور عمدۃ الفتاویٰ میں ہے اگر کہا کہ میں نے اس نو جوان کی اقتداء کی تو پتہ چلا کہ وہ بوڑھا ہے تو یج نہیں اور اگر کہا کہ میں نے اس بوڑھے کی اقتداء کی پتہ چلا کہ وہ نو جوان ہے تو صحیح ہے، اس لئے کہ نوجوان کو شیخ سے پکارا جاتا ہے اس کے علم کی وجہ سے بخلاف اس کے بر عکس کے عمدۃ الفتاویٰ کا کلام پورا ہوا اور اشارہ یہاں کافی نہیں، اس لئے کہ سی شار و امام کی طرف نہیں یہ تو نوجوان یا بوڑھے کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ فتأمل ۔ تشریح مقتدی نے جو ان امام کی نیت کی پھر پتہ چلا کہ وہ بوڑھا ہے تو اقتدار پیچ نہ ہوگی کیونکہ ذات کی تعیین نہ ہونے کی صورت میں وصف کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور یہاں اس سے وصف میں خطا ہوئی ہے تو گویا اب اس نے امام کے علاوہ کسی اور کی اقتداء کی کیونکہ عرف میں بھی جو ان کو بوڑھا نہیں کہا جاتا۔ ولوقال اقتديت بهذا الشاب فاذا هو شيخ لم يصح (البحر الرائق کراچی ج ۱ ص: ۱۰۲) اور اگر صراحت کے ساتھ کہا کہ میں اس شیخ کی اقتداء کر رہا ہوں پتہ چلا کہ وہ تو نو جوان ہے تو اقتدار آتا ہے کیو نکہ کبھی کبھی جو ان کو بھی علم کی وجہ سے تعظیماً شیخ کہ دیا جاتا ہے۔ وفى عمدة الفتاوى ولوقال اقتديت بهذا الشيخ وهو شاب صح لان الشاب يدعى شيخا للتعظیم (شامی زکریا ج ۲ س: ۱۰۶) ایک شبہ اور اس کا ازالہ شبہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ ابھی آپ نے چند سطر پہلے کہا تھا کہ جب اشارہ اور تسمیہ میں تعارض ہو جائے تو تسمیہ باطل ہوجاتا ہے اور اشارہ کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہئے ، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اشارہ کا اس وقت تعارض کی صورت میں اعتبار ہوتا ہے جب وہ ذات کی طرف ہو اور جب وہ وصف کی طرف ہو تو اس کا معاہدہ ہوا با کسی کا تیار ہوا اور یہاں تسمیہ میں اس سے غلطی واقع ہوئی ہے و الاشارة ھھنا“ سے اس شہر اور ازالہ کو بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ والحاصل ان الوصف معتبر عند عدم تعيين الذات فاما عند تعيينها فلا (حلبى كبير ص:۲۵۲)
And in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: If he said, 'I followed this young man,' and it turned out that he was old, it is not valid; and if he said, 'I followed this old man,' and it turned out that he was young, it is valid, because a young man is called 'sheikh' due to his knowledge, contrary to the opposite. End. And the pointing here is not sufficient because it was not a pointing to the Imam; rather, it was to a young man or an old man, so reflect. Translation: And in 'Umdat al-Fatawa, if he said, 'I followed this young man,' and it turned out he was old, then it is not valid; and if he said, 'I followed this old man,' and it turned out he was young, then it is valid, because a young man is called sheikh due to his knowledge, contrary to the opposite. The words of 'Umdat al-Fatawa are complete. And the pointing here is not sufficient because the pointer is not towards the Imam, rather it is towards a young or old man. So reflect. Commentary: The follower intended the Imam, then it turned out he was old, so the following does not occur because in the absence of specifying the essence, the description is considered, and here there was a mistake in description, so it is as if he followed someone other than the Imam, because in custom a young man is not called old. And if he said, 'I followed this young man,' and it turned out he was old, it is not valid (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Karachi, vol. 1, p. 102). And if he explicitly said, 'I am following this sheikh,' and it turned out he was young, then the following occurs because sometimes a young man is also called sheikh out of respect due to his knowledge. And in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: If he said, 'I followed this sheikh,' and he was young, it is valid because a young man is called sheikh for respect (Shami, Zakariyya, vol. 2, p. 106). A doubt and its removal: The doubt is that you said a few lines earlier that when pointing and naming contradict, the naming becomes void and the pointing is considered, so here it should be the same. Its answer is that pointing is considered in case of contradiction only when it is towards the essence, and when it is towards the description, then it is like a covenant or something. Here the naming contained a mistake in description. The phrase 'and the pointing here' indicates this doubt and its removal. The conclusion: The description is considered when the essence is not specified; but when it is specified, it is not (Halabi Kabir, p. 252).
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from 'Umdat al-Fatawa regarding the validity of following an imam when the description given in the intention (e.g., 'young' or 'old') turns out to be mistaken. The ruling distinguishes between two cases: if one specifies 'young' and finds the imam is old, the prayer is invalid because in custom a young man is not called old, so the intention does not match reality. Conversely, if one specifies 'old' and finds the imam is young, it is valid because a young man can be honorifically called 'sheikh' due to knowledge or respect. The passage then addresses a potential contradiction: earlier it was stated that when pointing and naming conflict, the naming is void and pointing prevails. The author clarifies that this applies only when the pointing is to the essence (dhat) of the person, not to a description (wasf). Here, the pointing was to the description (young/old), not to the essence of the imam, so the naming (description) is considered. The underlying principle is that description matters only when the essence is not directly specified.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer by intending to follow him.
الشاب (al-shab): A young man, typically referring to someone not old.
الشيخ (al-shaykh): An old man or a title of respect due to knowledge or position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because a young learned person can be called sheikh honorifically.
B) No, because the description was wrong.
C) Yes, only if the imam is actually old.
D) No, because pointing takes precedence over naming.

Key Takeaway
When specifying an imam, a factual misdescription invalidates; an honorific misdescription does not.

Specifying Gender or Number in Funeral Prayer Intention
Ruling on mistaken gender or number in funeral prayer intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-wasf mu'tabar 'inda 'adam ta'yin al-dhat' to determine the validity of funeral prayer when gender or number is mistakenly specified, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A mistaken description in intention invalidates unless the subject is already fully identified.

In the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), the intention (niyyah) must correspond to the actual deceased. If you specify the gender or the number of the deceased and it turns out wrong, does the prayer remain valid? The Hanafi jurists derive the answer from a general maxim: a description is considered only when the essence is not already specified. This lesson applies that maxim to concrete cases and clarifies the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The question is: what happens if the worshipper specifies a gender or number in intention and it turns out to be different?
The source passage rules that gender mistake invalidates; for number, only excess invalidates.
2
Extract the governing maxim
The reasoning relies on the maxim: 'al-wasf mu'tabar 'inda 'adam ta'yin al-dhat' (the description is considered when the essence is not specified; when it is, it is not). Understand how this maxim applies here.
If the essence (the specific deceased) is not identified by a fixed attribute (like name), then a descriptive specification matters. If the attribute is mistaken, the intention fails.
3
Apply the maxim to gender case
When the worshipper intends 'male deceased' but the deceased is female, the description 'male' is part of the intended essence. Since it contradicts reality, the intention does not correspond to the actual subject, so the prayer is invalid.
The deceased is likened to the imam: a mistake in specifying the imam invalidates the congregational prayer.
4
Apply the maxim to number case
If the worshipper specifies a number (e.g., ten) but there are more, the extra ones were not intended, so the prayer is invalid for all. If there are fewer, all intended are present, so the prayer is valid for those present.
The text advises avoiding number specification altogether to prevent invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَى هَذَا لَوْنَوَى الصَّلَاةَ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ الذَّكَرِ فَتَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهُ أُنثَى أَوْ عَكْسُهُ لَمْ يَصِحُ ، وَلَمْ أَرَ حُكْمَ مَا إِذَا عَيَّنَ عَدَدَ الْمَوْتَى عَشَرَةً، فَبَانَ أَنَّهُمْ أَكْثَرُاوْ أَقَلُّ وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ لَا يَضُرَّ إِلَّا إِذَا بَانَ أَنَّهُمْ أَكْثَرُ فَإِنَّ مِنْهُمْ مَنْ لَّمْ يَنوِى الصَّلاةَ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الزَّائِد. ترجمہ: اور اس پر محمول ہے وہ صورت اگر مذکر میت پر نماز کی نیت کرے، اور ظاہر ہو کہ وہ مونث ہے یا اس كے برعکس تو بیج نہیں ہے اور اس صورت کا حکم میں نے نہیں دیکھا جب وہ مرے ہوئے کی تعداد دس متعین کرے پھر ظاہر ہو کہ وہ زیادہ ہیں یا کم ہیں اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ یہ مضر نہ ہو، مگر اس صورت میں جبکہ ان کا زیادہ ہونا ظاہر ہو اس لئے کہ ان میں وہ بھی ہے جس پر نماز کی نیت ہی نہیں کی اور وہ زائد ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی شخص نے جنازہ کی نیت کی اور نیت کرتے وقت اس نے مردمیت کی بیت کی تھی بعد میں میت کا عورت ہونا معلوم ہوا یا اس کا بر عکس تو ایسی صورت میں اس کی نماز صحیح نہ ہوگی کیونکہ میت امام کے مثل ہے اس کی تعین کے اندر خطا کرنا امام کی تعیین کے خطاء کے مقتل ہے۔ وفى الشامية لان الميت كا لامام فالخطأ فى تعيينه كا لخطأ في تعيين الامام. (شای ج۲ : ۱۰۳) ولماز حكم ما اذا عین: کسی نے دس اموات پر جنازہ کی نیت کی مگر بعد میں ان کی تعداد کم و بیش ظاہر ہوئی تو کم والی صورت میں تو تعیین نقصان دہ نہ ہوگی لیکن جب موتی کی تعدادزیادہ معلوم ہو جائے تو زائد کی نیت نہ ہونے کی سے تعین مضر ہوگی ، اور جس کی نیت نہیں ہوئی اس کی نماز درست نہ ہوئی اور یہ احتمال ہر ایک کے بارے میں ہے کو زائد سے جس کی نیت نہیں کی اس لئے کسی کی بھی نماز درست نہ ہوگی اس لئے بہتر یہ ہے کہ یہ نیت کرے جو جنازے میرے سامنے ہیں یا جن کی امام نماز پڑھا رہا ہے تو میں بھی ان کی نیت کرتا ہوں ۔ وان لا يضر تعيين عدد الموتى الا اذا بان انهم اكثر لعدم نية الزائد و تحته في الشامية اى اذا عين عددهم لا يضره التعيين المذكور فى حالة من الاحوال سواء وافق ما عين او خالفه الا اذا كانوا اكثر مماعين (الدر الختار مع رد المختار ج ۲ ص: ۱۰۵)
And on this analogizes: if one intends prayer over a deceased male and it turns out that it is female, or vice versa, it is not valid. And I have not seen the ruling when one specifies the number of deceased as ten, and it turns out they are more or less; and it seems appropriate that it does not harm except when it turns out they are more, because among them are those whom he did not intend to pray over—the extra ones. Translation: And upon this is based the case if he intends prayer on a male deceased and it appears it is female or its reverse, then it is not valid. And I have not seen the ruling when he specifies the number of deceased as ten, then it appears they are more or less; and it is appropriate that it does not harm except when it appears they are more, because among them is one on whom he did not intend prayer—the extra one. Commentary: The case is that a person intended funeral prayer and at the time of intention he specified the gender; later it became known the deceased was female or vice versa; then his prayer is not valid because the deceased is like the imam; error in its specification is like error in specifying the imam. (Shami, vol. 2, p. 103). And as for the ruling when he specifies: someone intended funeral prayer for ten deceased, but later their number appeared less or more; in the case of less, the specification does not harm, but when the number is found to be more, then the specification harms due to lack of intention for the extra ones, and the prayer for the unintended is not valid, and this probability applies to each, so none of the prayers is valid. Therefore it is better to intend: 'the funeral prayers that are before me' or 'those for whom the imam is praying, I also intend for them.' And the specification of the number of deceased does not harm except when it turns out they are more, due to lack of intention for the extra. And under it in al-Shamiyya: that is, if he specifies their number, the aforementioned specification does not harm him in any case, whether it matches what he specified or not, except when they are more than he specified. (al-Durr al-Mukhtar with Radd al-Muhtar, vol. 2, p. 105)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage extends the principle from the previous lesson to funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The ruling states that if one intends to pray over a deceased person specifying their gender (male or female) and it turns out to be the opposite, the prayer is invalid. This is because the deceased is analogous to the imam in that a mistake in specifying the subject invalidates the act. The passage then addresses a scenario where the worshipper specifies the number of deceased persons (e.g., ten). If the actual number is fewer, it does not harm because the intention covers those present. However, if the actual number is greater, the prayer is invalid for all because the intention did not include the extra ones. The recommended practice is to avoid specifying number and instead intend generally for all those before one or for those for whom the imam intends.

Key Terms
الميت (al-mayyit): The deceased person for whom funeral prayer is performed.
تعيين العدد (ta'yin al-‘adad): Specifying the number of deceased persons in the intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, if a person intends funeral prayer for three deceased but there are actually five, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid for the three intended.
B) The prayer is invalid for all five because the extra two were not intended.
C) The prayer is valid for all five because the intention can be extended.
D) The prayer is valid for the three, and the two can be included by a separate intention during the prayer.

Key Takeaway
A mistaken description in funeral prayer intention invalidates only when it introduces an extra subject not intended; a lesser actual number does not harm.

Intention in Acts of Means (Wasail): Wudu, Ghusl, Tayammum
Defining the rule of intention for purificatory acts that are means to worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that intention in wasail acts does not require specification, and identify when an exception applies (tayammum).

Core Idea
For means acts like wudu, general intention of the goal suffices; only tayammum demands specific intention due to Quranic text.

In Hanafi usul, distinguishing between acts that are ends in themselves (maqsuda) and those that are means (wasila) is crucial for determining the role of intention (niyyah). This lesson unpacks the qawida that governs intention in purificatory acts, addressing common objections and establishing the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish maqsuda vs wasila
Define the two categories: acts that are independent worship (ibadat maqsuda) vs acts that are means to an end (wasail). For the latter, specific intention of the act itself is not required.
Maqsuda: prayer, fasting, zakat. Wasila: wudu, ghusl, tayammum.
2
Identify the base qawida
State the governing rule: 'Intention in means acts does not require specification; rather, intending the maqsud or removal of hadath suffices.' This is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) within the larger qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.
The qawida is from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair.
3
Examine the furuat: wudu and ghusl vs tayammum
Apply the rule to wudu and ghusl: one does not need to specifically intend 'wudu'; intending removal of hadath or a worship that requires purification suffices. For tayammum, the rule is reversed due to explicit Quranic command—specific intention of a maqsuda act is required.
Tayammum's exception is mentioned in the passage with Quranic evidence (al-Ma'ida 5:6).
4
Understand objections and resolutions
The passage discusses objections by al-Zaylai against al-Kanz and by others against al-Quduri. The resolution from al-Kafi clarifies that the correct sunna intention is removal of hadath or establishment of prayer, not merely intending wudu or purification.
The pronoun 'niyyatuhu' in al-Kanz is interpreted to refer to the person, not to wudu itself.
5
Determine the mufta bihi for fatwa
The preferred madhhab position (mufta bihi) is that one must intend removal of hadath (رفع الحدث) or a specific worship that requires purification (e.g., prayer, sajdat al-tilawa). Intending purification alone (نية الطهارة) is considered insufficient by some, though al-Kasani held it acceptable.
The tarjih is based on the clarity in al-Kafi and the majority of later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنِ الْمَنْوِيُّ مِنَ الْعِبَادَاتِ الْمَقْصُوْدَةِ وَإِنَّمَاهُوَ مِنَ الْوَسَائِلِ كَالْوُضُوء وَالْغُسْلِ وَالتَّيَمُّمِ، قَالُوْا فِى الْوُضُوْءِ : لَا يَنْوِيْهِ، لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِعِبَادَةٍ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال جب کہ وہ جس کی نیت کی جارہی ہے عبادات مقصورہ میں سے نہ ہو بلکہ وہ وسائل سے؟ جیسے وضو غسل اور تیم تو فقہا وضو کے بارے میں کہتے ہیں کہ وہ اس کی نیت نہ کرے اس لئے کہ وہ عبادت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر منوی عبادات مقصورہ میں سے نہ ہو بلکہ اس کا تعلق وسائل سے ہو جیسے وضو اور غسل وغیر و توان میں تعیین نیت ضروری نہیں ہے، رہا مسئلہ تمیم کا تو اس میں نیت نص قرآنی کی وجہ سے ضروری ہے، البتہ حصول ثواب کے لئے عبادات غیر مقصودہ میں بھی نیت ضروری ہے۔ وَإعْتَرَضَ الشَّارِحُ الزيلعي على الكنر " فِي قَوْلِهِ : وَنِيَّتُهُ بِنَاءً عَلَى عَوْدِ الضَّمِيرِ إلى الْوُضُوْءِ، وَكَذَا اعْتَرَضُوا عَلَى الْقُدُوْرِي فِي قَوْلِهِ : يَنوى الطَّهَارَةَ، وَالْمَذْهَبُ أَنْ يَتْرِى مالا يصح إلا بِالطَّهَارَةِ مِنَ الْعِبَادَةِ، أو رفع الحَدَثِ وَعِندَ الْبَعْضِ فِيَّة الطَّهَارَةِ تَكْفِي. ترجمہ: اور شارح زیلعی نے کنز پر اس کے قول و نیتہ پر اعتراض کیا ہے جو ضمیر کے وضو کی طرف لوٹے پرمبنی ہے اور ایسے ہی فقہاء نے قدوری پر اس کے قول مینوی الطہار پر اعتراض کیا ہے اور پسندیدہ مذہب یہ ہے کہ اس عبادت کی نیت کرے جو بدون طہارت صحیح نہیں ہوتی یا رفع حدث کی نیت کرے اور بعض کے نزدیک طہارت کی نیت کافی ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب کنز نے وضو کی سنت شمار کرتے ہوئ ونیہ کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہے جس میں امیر کا مرجب بندہ ہے اس پر علامہ زیلعی نے اعتراض کیا ہے کہ مصنف کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تحصیل سنت کے لئے وفضولی نیت کافی ہے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ وضو میں تحصیل سنت کے لئے یا تو ایسی عبادت کی نیت ہو جو بغیر رفع حدث کے درست نہ ہو، یا اقامت صلاۃ کی نیت ہو۔ علامہ ابن قیم نے اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ دیا ہے کہ نیت میں ضمیر کا مرجع وضو نہیں ہے بلکہ متوضی ہے کی (from page 180) Scanned by CamScanner  ربع حدث یا اقامت صلوٰۃ کی نیت کرنا مسنون ہے۔ وضو سے مفہوم ہے اور اصل عبارت ہے نیة المتوضى رفع الحدث او اقامة الصلواة ہے، یعنی متوضی کا دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ نیتہ میں ضمیر کا مرجع وضو ہی ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ وضو کی حیثیت رفع حدث کے علاوہ اور کچھ نہیں ہے وضو اور رفع حدث میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے بلکہ رفع حدث تو حدث اصغر کو شامل ہے اور حدث اکبر کو بھی اور وضو عرف حدث اصغر کے ازالہ کے لئے خاص ہے اس لئے وضو کی نیت اقرب الی السنتہ ہے۔ وكذا إعترضوا : صاحب قدوری نے سنن وضو میں تحریر فرمایا ہے سینوی الطہارۃ یعنی تحصیل سنت کے لئے طہارت کی نیت کی جائے ، فقہاء نے اس پر اعتراض کیا ہے کہ لفظ طہارت ازالہ حدث کے لئے بھی مستعمل ہے اور ازالہ نبث (باطنی ناپاکی ،فساد عقیدہ) کے لئے بھی اس لئے بالخصوص طہارت صغریٰ کی نیت نہیں پائی گئی معلوم ہوا کہ ادائیگی سنت کے لئے طہارت کی نیت کافی نہیں ہے۔ جواب: اگر چه لفظ طہارت از اللہ بخبث کو بھی شامل ہے لیکن وہ طہارت صغریٰ کے لئے بھی مستعمل ہے اور تحصیل منت کے لئے طہارت صغریٰ کا خاص ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ علامہ کا سائی نے بدائع میں فرمایا ہے کہ نیت طہارت سے بھی سنت ادا ہو جائے گی اور صاحب الاشباہ بھی فرمارہے ہیں کہ بعض کے نزدیک نیست طہارت کافی ہے، اس لئے جمہور علم کے نزدیک بہتر یہ ہے کہ بوقت وضو جو نیت مسنون ہے وہ رفع حدث کی نیت کرے، یا ایسی عبادت مقصودہ کی جو غیر وضوکے صحیح نہ ہوتی ہے یا عبادت مقصودہ کے کسی ایک فرد کی مثلا سجدہ تلاوت وغیرہ کی۔ أى و نية المتوضى رفع الحدث او إقامة الحدث هذا هو مراد المصنف كما افصح عنه في الكافي فلا حاجة حينئذ إلى ماذكره الزيلعي كما لا يخفى الى قوله قالوا المعتبر قصد رفع الحدث او اقامة الصلاة كما ذكر او استباحتها او امتثال الامر ( البحر الرائق کراچی ج ۱ ص ۲۳) وَأَمَّا فِي التَّيَمُّم : فَقَالُوْا : إِنَّهُ يَنْوِى عِبَادَةً مَقْصُوْدَةً لَا تَصِحُ إِلَّا بِالطَّهَارَةِ مِثْلُ سَجْدَةِ الثَّلَاوَةِ، وَصَلَاةِ الظُّهْرِ، قَالُوا: وَلَوْ تَيَمَّمَ لِدُخُولِ الْمَسْجِدِ، أَوِ الْأَذَانِ، أَوِ الْإِقَامَةِ لَاتُؤَدُّى بِهِ الصَّلَاةُ، لأنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِعِبَادَةٍ مَقْصُوْدَةٍ، وَإِنَّمَاهُنَّ أَتْبَاعٌ لِغَيْرِهَا. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال تیم کے بارے میں تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ نیت کرے ایسی عبادة مقصودہ کی جو بدون طہارت صحیح نہ ہوتی ہو جیسے سجدہ تلاوت ، نماز ظہر ، فقہاء فرماتے ہیں اگر تم کیا مسجد میں داخلہ کے لئے یا اذان اور اقامت کے لئے تو اس سے نماز ادا نہیں کی جائے گی، اس لئے کہ وہ عبادت مقصودہ نہیں ہیں بلکہ وہ تو اپنے علاوہ کے تابع ہیں۔
As for when the intended act is not from the intended acts of worship (maqsuda) but rather from the means (wasail), like wudu, ghusl, and tayammum, they said regarding wudu: one does not intend it, because it is not an act of worship. Translation: And whenever the intended thing is not from the intended acts of worship but rather from the means, like wudu, ghusl, and tayammum, then the jurists say regarding wudu: one should not intend it, because it is not an act of worship. Commentary: If the intended thing is not from the intended acts of worship but rather related to means, like wudu and ghusl, then specific intention is not necessary; as for the issue of tayammum, intention is necessary due to the clear Quranic text; however, for acquiring reward, intention is necessary even in non-maqsuda acts. And the commentator al-Zaylai objected to al-Kanz regarding his statement 'and his intention' based on the pronoun returning to wudu; similarly, they objected to al-Quduri regarding his statement 'he intends purification'. And the preferred madhhab is that one intends an act of worship that is only valid with purification, or removal of hadath; according to some, intention of purification suffices. Translation: And al-Zaylai objected to al-Kanz's phrase 'and his intention' which is based on the pronoun returning to wudu; similarly, the jurists objected to al-Quduri's phrase 'he intends purification'. The preferred madhhab is that one intends an act of worship that is only valid with purification, or removal of hadath; according to some, intention of purification suffices. Commentary: The author of al-Kanz, while counting the sunan of wudu, used the word 'and his intention' where the pronoun refers to the person performing wudu. al-Zaylai objected that the author's expression suggests that intending wudu is sufficient for obtaining sunna, but it is not. Rather, for obtaining sunna in wudu, one must intend either an act that is not valid without removal of hadath, or the establishment of prayer. Ibn al-Qayyim gave one answer: the pronoun's referent is not wudu but the person performing wudu. Second answer: the pronoun's referent is wudu, and it is clear that wudu's nature is nothing other than removal of hadath; there is no difference between wudu and removal of hadath; rather, removal of hadath includes minor hadath and major hadath, while wudu is specific to removing minor hadath, so intending wudu is closer to the sunna. Similarly they objected: al-Quduri wrote in the sunan of wudu 'intends purification' meaning for obtaining sunna, one should intend purification. The jurists objected that the word 'purification' is used for removal of hadath and also for removal of internal impurity (corrupt belief), so specifically intention of minor purification is not found; it follows that intention of purification is not sufficient for performing the sunna. Answer: Although the word 'purification' includes removal of inner impurity, it is also used for minor purification, and being specific to minor purification is not necessary for obtaining the sunna. Allamah al-Kasani said in Bada'i': intention of purification will also fulfill the sunna, and the author of al-Ashbah says that according to some, intention of purification suffices. Therefore, according to the majority of scholars, the recommended sunna intention at the time of wudu is to intend removal of hadath, or an intended act of worship that is not valid without wudu, or one particular intended act such as prostration of recitation, etc. Meaning: the intention of the person performing wudu is removal of hadath or establishment of prayer—this is what the author meant, as clarified in al-Kafi, so there is no need for what al-Zaylai mentioned, as is evident until his statement: they said the valid intention is the intention of removal of hadath or establishment of prayer as mentioned, or making it permissible, or fulfilling the command (Bahr al-Ra'iq, Karachi, vol. 1, p. 23). As for tayammum, they said: one intends an intended act of worship that is not valid without purification, like the prostration of recitation and Dhuhr prayer. They said: if one performs tayammum for entering the mosque, or the adhan, or the iqama, prayer will not be performed with it, because they are not intended acts of worship, but rather they are followers of something else.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a qa'ida (legal maxim) regarding intention in acts that are means (wasail) to worship, such as wudu, ghusl, and tayammum. The rule: for means acts that are not themselves independent acts of worship (maqsuda), a specific intention of that act is not required. Instead, one should intend the intended worship (e.g., prayer) that requires purification. The passage discusses criticisms of al-Kanz and al-Quduri by later scholars, showing that the correct sunna intention at the time of wudu is either removal of hadath or an act that requires purification. For tayammum, due to its specific Quranic evidence, intention of a maqsuda act is explicitly required; tayammum for mere entry to the mosque or adhan does not enable prayer. The authoritative text (al-Kafi) clarifies that the intended niyyah is removal of hadath or establishment of prayer, settling the dispute.

Key Terms
وسائل (wasail): Acts that are means to an end, not independent acts of worship, e.g., wudu, ghusl.
عبادات مقصودة (ibadat maqsuda): Independent acts of worship intended for their own sake, like prayer, fasting.
منوي (manwi): The act that is intended; in this context, if it is a wasila, specific intention is not required.
رفع الحدث (raf' al-hadath): Removal of the state of ritual impurity (minor or major).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the minimum sufficient intention for wudu to be sunna?
A) Intending wudu itself
B) Intending removal of hadath or an act of worship that requires purification
C) Intending only purification
D) No intention needed

Key Takeaway
For means acts like wudu, intention of the goal (removal of hadath or maqsuda worship) suffices; tayammum is the sole exception requiring specific intention.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
Intention for Fard, Wajib, and Nafl Prayers
Stating rulings on specifying intention for different types of prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on intention (niyyah) for fard, wajib, and nafl prayers, and evaluate the derived subsidiary cases (furu'at) using the maxim 'al-wajibat wa al-fara'id la tu'ada bi mutlaq al-niyyah'.

Core Idea
Fard and wajib prayers require specific intention; nafl and sunnah ratibah are valid with absolute intention.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair details the specific intention required for different categories of prayer. It establishes a key maxim that differentiates obligatory from voluntary acts, and then derives several practical rulings that every student of fiqh and mufti must know. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for the validity of daily prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of prayer and their intention requirements
From the passage, extract the requirements for fard, wajib, and nafl prayers. Note the three necessary elements for fard: intention of prayer, intention of fardiyyah, and intention of specification (ta'yin).
2
Locate the governing maxim and its scope
Find the statement from al-Ghiyathiyyah: 'Al-wajibat wa al-fara'id la tu'ada bi mutlaq al-niyyah ijma'an.' Understand that this is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) of wusta rank.
The maxim is restricted by the exception for nafl and sunnah ratibah.
3
Work through the subsidiary cases (furu'at)
Apply the maxim to each of the five cases listed: ignorance of fard, inability to distinguish, intending fard for all, mistaken belief, and following an imam. State the ruling for each.
Refer to the furuat in the qawida_panel.
4
Note the exception for nafl and sunnah
Contrast the requirements for fard/wajib with the rule for nafl and sunnah ratibah: they are valid with absolute intention or even contrary intention. Understand the rationale: absolute intention defaults to the lowest rank (nafl).
This is the istithna' from the maxim.
5
Summarize the practical rule for a mufti
Synthesize: For any obligatory prayer (fard or wajib), the worshipper must intend the prayer, its obligatory nature, and the specific prayer. For voluntary prayers, a general intention suffices. When in doubt, specify the prayer to be safe.
This is the mufta bihi position.

الْرَّابِعُ فِي صِفَةِ الْمَنْوِيِّ مِنَ الْفَرِيْضَةِ وَالنَّافِلَةِ وَالْآدَاءِ وَالْقَضَاءِ. أَمَّا الصَّلَاةُ: فَقَالَ فِى الْبَزَّازِيَةِ إِنَّهُ يَنْوِى الْفَرِيضَةَ فِي الْفَرْضِ فَقَالَ مُعْزِياً إِلَى الْمُجْتَبى لابُدَّ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الصَّلَاةِ، وَنِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِ، وَنِيَّةِ التَّعْبِيْنِ حَتَّى لَوْ نَوَى الْقَرْضَ لَا يُجْزِنُهُ. وَلَوْ نَوَى الصَّلَاةَ وَلَمْ يَنُوِّ أَنَّهَا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى يَكُونُ شَارِعاً فِي النَّفَلِ إِذَا لَمْ يَذْكُرْ لَفَظَ الْفَرْضِ أَوْ مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ كَصَلَاةِ الظُّهْرِ. وَلَا بُدَّ لِلْمُفْتَرِضِ الْمُنْفَرِدِ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِ الْمُعَيَّنِ فِي الْوَقْتِ كَالظُّهْرِ وَغَيْرِهِ. وَالْوَاجِبَاتُ كَالْفَرَائِضِ كَمَا فِى التَّاتَارُخَانِيَةِ. وَأَمَّا النَّافِلَةُ وَالسُّنَّةُ الرَّاتِبَةُ: فَقَدَّمْنَا أَنَّهَا تَصِحُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ، وَبِنِيَّةٍ مُبَائِنَةٍ. وَفِى الْغِيَاثِيَةِ الْوَاجِبَاتُ وَالْفَرَائِضُ لَا تَتَأَدَّى بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ إِجْمَاعًا. فَإِنْ كَانَ مُتَنَفِّلًا يَكْفِيهِ نِيَّةُ مُطْلَقِ الصَّلَاةِ لِأَنَّ الصَّلَاةَ أَنْوَاعٌ فِي مَنَازِلِهَا وَأَدْنَاهَا مَنْزِلَةً النَّفَلُ فَانْصَرَفَ مُطْلَقُ النِّيَّةِ إِلَيْهِ. وَتَفَرَّعَ عَلَى إِشْتِرَاطِ نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ أَنَّهُ لَوْلَمْ يَعْرِفِ الْفَرَائِضَ الْخَمْسَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يُصَلِّيْهَا فِي أَوْقَاتِهَا لَا تَجُوْزُ، وَكَذَا لَوْ اعْتَقَدَ أَنَّ مِنْهَا فَرْضاً وَنَفْلًا وَلَا يُمَيِّزُ، وَلَمْ يَنْوِي الْفَرْضَ فِيْهَا، فَإِنْ نَوَى الْفَرْضَ فِي الْكُلِّ جَازَ، وَلَوْ ظَنَّ الْكُلَّ فَرْضاً جَازَ، وَإِنْ لَّمْ يَظُنُّ ذلِكَ، فَكُلُّ صَلَاةٍ صَلَّاهَا مَعَ الْإِمَامِ جَازَ : إِنْ نَوَى صَلَاةَ الْإِمَامِ، كَذَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ.
The fourth [topic] is concerning the description of that which is intended from obligatory, supererogatory, performance, and make-up. As for prayer: In al-Bazzaziyyah it is said that one intends obligatory in the obligatory; then referring to al-Mujtaba it is said that intention of prayer, intention of obligatory, and intention of specification are necessary, such that if one intended [only] obligatory it does not suffice. If one intended prayer but did not intend that it is for Allah Almighty, he becomes a performer of supererogatory if he did not mention the word obligatory or what indicates it like Zuhr prayer. And for the one performing obligatory alone, it is necessary to intend the specific obligatory in its time like Zuhr and others. And obligatory [prayers] are like obligatory duties as in al-Tatar Khaniyyah. As for supererogatory and the regular sunnah: we have already stated that they are valid with absolute intention and with contrary intention. And in al-Ghiyathiyyah: obligatory and obligatory duties are not fulfilled by absolute intention by consensus. For if one is performing supererogatory, the intention of absolute prayer suffices because prayer has types in their ranks and the lowest rank is supererogatory, so absolute intention refers to it. And derived from the condition of intention of obligatory is that if he does not know the five obligatory prayers but prays them in their times, it is not valid; likewise if he believes that some are obligatory and some supererogatory and does not distinguish, and does not intend obligatory in them; if he intends obligatory in all, it is valid; if he thinks all are obligatory, it is valid; if he does not think that, then every prayer he prays with the imam is valid if he intends the prayer of the imam. Thus in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal ruling (hukm) regarding the intention (niyyah) required for different categories of prayer: fard (obligatory), wajib (necessary), nafl (supererogatory), and sunnah ratibah (regular voluntary). The author begins by stating that for fard prayers, three elements are necessary in intention: the intention of prayer itself, the intention of obligatory (fardiyyah), and the intention of specification (ta'yin, such as Zuhr, Asr, etc.). If one intends only the word 'fard' without specifying prayer or type, it does not suffice. However, if one intends absolute prayer without specifying it is for Allah, and does not mention 'fard' or a specific prayer like Zuhr, the prayer becomes nafl. This shows that a general intention automatically directs to the lowest rank, nafl. For an individual performing fard alone, he must intend the specific fard of the time. Wajib prayers (like witr) are treated like fard in this respect: they also require specific intention and are not fulfilled by absolute intention. In contrast, nafl and sunnah ratibah are valid with absolute intention (e.g., just intending to pray) and even with an intention that contradicts the actual act (e.g., intending fard while performing nafl, it becomes nafl). The consensus from al-Ghiyathiyyah affirms that fard and wajib are not fulfilled by absolute intention. The passage then derives several subsidiary rulings (furu'): (1) A person who does not know the five fards but prays them in their times without intending fard does not have valid prayer; he must make them up. (2) If one believes some prayers are fard and some nafl but cannot distinguish, and does not intend fard for any, none are valid. (3) If he intends fard for all, all are valid. (4) If he mistakenly believes all are fard, his prayer is valid. (5) When praying behind an imam, it suffices to intend the imam's prayer (without specifying fard or nafl). These rulings are taken from Fath al-Qadir and other sources. The underlying principle is that the intention must match the reality of the act; since fard and wajib have a specific legal nature, the intention must reflect that. Nafl is the default rank, so absolute intention defaults to it.

Key Terms
نية الصلاة (niyyat al-salat): The intention to perform the act of prayer as an act of worship.
نية الفرضية (niyyat al-fardiyyah): The intention that the prayer being performed is obligatory (fard).
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): The intention specifying which particular prayer is being performed, e.g., Zuhr, Asr.
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): An absolute intention without specifying the type or name of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for an obligatory prayer (fard) if one intends only 'prayer' without specifying fardiyyah or the specific prayer?
A) The prayer is valid as fard because intention of prayer is sufficient.
B) The prayer becomes nafl unless the word 'fard' or the specific name (e.g., Zuhr) is mentioned.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
D) It is valid because intention is not required for any prayer.

Key Takeaway
For fard and wajib prayers, intention must include both the category (fard/wajib) and the specific prayer; for nafl and sunnah ratibah, absolute intention suffices.
